## ✅ Done

### B387 — Drag-to-resize columns in the PDF/Print Exhibit `[Scheduler]` (feature)  *(owner-dropped from chat as "NEW-3" 2026-06-22; minted **B387**)*
`[x]` **Filed AND fixed + headless-verified (V109, 10/10) + merged the SAME session per STANDING RULE #1 (branch `claude/practical-edison-ggcm1k`).** The exhibit columns can now be tuned by dragging a column's right edge in the preview — the same interaction as resizing a column in the live schedule grid — with the preview reflowing live and the tuned layout persisting.
- **Handles + live drag (`buildPDFHtml`, `public/sequence/index.html`):** every column header in the **preview** (never the print output — `@media print{.col-rs{display:none}}` + emitted only when `forPreview`) carries an absolutely-positioned `.col-rs` `col-resize` handle on its right edge. A small preview-only script tracks the drag and resizes the dragged column **live across every paginated page** (sets the width on all `th[data-k]` + each `.split-table`/`.split-gantt`), trading the delta against the Gantt — which keeps `EXHIBIT_MIN_GANTT` (240px) — and clamping to the column's `[min,max]`. On release it posts `{type:'planarColResize',key,w}` to the parent.
- **Persistence (`PDFExportModal`):** a `planarColResize` message handler stashes the width as a per-column override (`cfg.colWidths[key]`), flushes the preview immediately (like the collapse-toggle path), and writes through `setData` to **`data.exportColWidths`** so a tuned exhibit comes back next time the modal opens (`cfg.colWidths` is seeded from it). A **Reset** affordance under the Columns section clears the overrides back to content-fit. (Persisted at schedule-data level — the exhibit renders one shared column layout across all selected projects, so a per-project-keyed store wouldn't apply; this is "comes back the way you left it" at the right granularity.)
- **Starts from B385's auto-fit:** an override wins for its column; everything else stays content-fit. Drag handles render only in the split (Gantt) view, where the table-vs-Gantt trade-off is well-defined (the reported screenshot).
- **Pagination fix bundled:** the paginator rebuilds the split and the Gantt container had **lost its `.split-gantt` class** (a no-class `div`); restored it so the live width-trade (and any `.split-gantt` selector) lands on the real post-paginate element instead of pushing/overflowing the chart.
- **DEDUPE / RECONCILE with B160 (left Open):** B160 is a single *ratio slider* for the whole table-vs-Gantt split; B387's **per-column** drag now changes the table block's total directly and the Gantt auto-takes the remainder (≥ MIN_GANTT) — complementary, not a duplicate. B387 sets the default total from content-fit; if B160's slider is built later it sets the overall budget B387's columns fit within. Added a reconcile note to B160 in `BACKLOG.md`; not built here (it wasn't in this drop and is a distinct control).
- **Verified:** see the shared verification note under B385.

### B386 — Year-boundary divider lines on the exhibit Gantt timeline `[Scheduler]` (feature)  *(owner-dropped from chat as "NEW-2" 2026-06-22; minted **B386**)*
`[x]` **Filed AND fixed + headless-verified (V109, 10/10) + merged the SAME session per STANDING RULE #1 (branch `claude/practical-edison-ggcm1k`).** A multi-year exhibit Gantt (the example spanned 2025→2027) had no visual break between calendar years.
- **Root cause (read the code, not the brief):** `buildGanttSVG`'s month gridlines were drawn **behind** the opaque per-row background bands (`<rect width=svgWidth fill=bg>`), so in the chart **body** they were invisible — only the dark header strip showed month labels. There were effectively no body gridlines at all, year or month.
- **Fix:** a new `yearLines` string drawn **over** the row bands (in the return, `${gridLines}${rows}${yearLines}${arrows}${todayLine}`): a heavier solid **medium-slate `#7b8290`, 1.3px** vertical at each Jan 1 (`yearMarkers`, the existing `m.mo===0` filter), so the split between years reads at a glance. Solid slate keeps it distinct from the red **dashed** Today line and the colored **dashed** dependency arrows. Also **emphasized the January month-axis labels** (bold + white vs the faint `#e8e8e8` other months) so each year's start is legible on the axis itself (doubles as the year label). A single-year exhibit (no January boundary in range) gets no divider — correct.
- **Scope:** the exhibit only (the explicit request — "the Gantt's result … should at least have divisions between the years"). Mirroring onto the on-screen `GanttView` was deferred (different render path; not requested).
- **Verified:** see the shared verification note under B385.

### B385 — PDF/Print Exhibit table columns mis-sized: oversized Task-Name gap + truncated Start/End/Duration `[Scheduler]` (bug)  *(owner-dropped from chat as "NEW-1" 2026-06-22; minted **B385** — highest B# across both files was B384)*
`[x]` **Filed AND fixed + headless-verified (V109, 10/10) + merged the SAME session per STANDING RULE #1 (branch `claude/practical-edison-ggcm1k`).** Three symptoms, **one** cause: in the split-view (table + Gantt) exhibit the columns were sized by **fixed widths, not fitted to content** — a large dead band between TASK NAME and START, Start/End rendering clipped (`06/2…`, `09/0…`), and DUR clipped (`1…`, `4…`).
- **Root cause:** the split table used `table-layout:fixed` at a hardcoded ~50%-of-page width, with fixed per-column px from `COL_DEFS` and the **Task-Name column at `w:null`** — so Name absorbed ALL the leftover width (the giant gap) while the fixed **42px** Start/End and **28px** Duration columns were too narrow for `MM/DD/YY` / multi-digit durations and clipped via `overflow:hidden;text-overflow:ellipsis`.
- **Fix — content-fit width model.** New pure, DOM-free module-scope helpers (above `buildPDFHtml`, so preview + print + tests agree): `approxTextPx(str,fs)` approximates rendered width from per-character advances for the exhibit's Inter face (deliberately generous so a fixed-format value never clips); `layoutExhibitCols(specs,opts)` lays columns out from their content-fit base, lets a user drag-override win, clamps each to `[min,max]`, makes the **table block exactly its columns' total**, and gives the Gantt the rest — never below `EXHIBIT_MIN_GANTT` (240px), shrinking the **flexible** columns (name/owner/predecessors/cost) toward their min, then a uniform scale, only if the columns would crowd the chart. `buildPDFHtml` measures each visible column's widest value across **all** selected projects (the exhibit stacks them under one shared header) via a plain-text `cellText` + a `COL_FIT` profile (font px, clamp range, flex flag, the Status dot+gap extra), then sizes the split from the result.
- **Per the brief:** the short fixed-format columns (Start/End/Duration/%/Status) are **NOT flexible** — a date is never the value that gets clipped to make room; only Name/Owner/Predecessors/Cost cap + ellipsize. **Respects the column on/off checkboxes** (only the turned-on `colDefs` are measured/sized). Tables-only mode (no Gantt) is **untouched** — its auto-layout already content-fits, so the bug was split-only; the fix is scoped there.
- **Shared verification (B385/B386/B387):** lint **0 errors** · **1210 tests** (1201 + 9 new in `test/exhibitCols.test.js`, with a faithful copy in `ui-audit/stress/exhibit-cols.mjs` + anti-drift guards) · build green · JSX transpiles (`jsxcheck-sequence`) · `Scheduler` lazy chunk intact. Headless **V109** (`ui-audit/verify-exhibit-columns.mjs`, **10/10**, drives page → sequence iframe → preview iframe on the real app): Start **and** End dates render in full with no ellipsis clip (`12/27/26`, `07/23/25`, `02/02/27`); Duration full (`389d`, `21d`); Task-Name content-capped (no runaway gap, name=280px); Gantt keeps a real share (322px); year-boundary divider lines present; a resize handle drags **live** (53→87px) and the new width **round-trips/persists** through the parent re-render. Screenshot: `ui-audit/screens/exhibit-fixed-zoom.png`.

### B383 — "Add parcel" action in the Parcel left-hand panel `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(owner-dropped from chat as "NEW-1" 2026-06-22; minted **B383** — highest B# across both files was B382)*
`[x]` **Filed AND fixed + headless-verified + merged the SAME session per STANDING RULE #1 (branch `claude/determined-volta-hzjxmc`).** The only obvious way to add parcels lived back on the map (MapFinder); once you were in the Site Planner there was no single front-door for "add more land to this plan." Now the Parcel panel leads with a primary **＋ Add parcel** control (accent chip, full-width, under the `PARCELS · N` header) that opens an `AnchoredMenu` — the same portal flyout the right-rail Boundary menu uses — with the add methods in priority order:
- **Identify from county GIS (headline)** — arms the existing `identifyMode` (`setIdentifyMode(true)`) → click-to-identify → result card → `addIdentifiedParcel` → `setParcels((a) => [...a, ...pcs])`. **Origin gate:** when `origin` is null the menu shows the disabled copy ("Identify needs a georeferenced plan. Bring a parcel in from the map to enable it.") instead of a live control.
- **Draw a new boundary** — `selectTool("parcel")` (the existing parcel draw tool), reachable from the Parcel panel now, not only the right-rail Boundary submenu. Needs no `origin`, so it stays enabled regardless — the fallback when there's no GIS frame.
- **Consolidation:** the standalone `🔍 Identify parcel` toggle at the panel bottom was folded into the menu's "Identify from county GIS" path — no two entry points for the same action. The result card, `＋ Add to plan`, and `⚖︎ Jurisdiction & road authority` behavior are unchanged; an in-panel "Identifying — click a spot (Esc to stop)" status row is the off-switch (so is Esc, which already cleared `identifyMode`/`identifyRes`). The bottom block now renders only when `identifyMode || identifyRes`.
- **Reuse, not fork** (same single-pipeline rule as B232/B233): `addIdentifiedParcel`, `setParcels`, `identifyMode`, and the parcel draw tool already existed — this surfaces + groups them, no new add pipeline. Added parcels keep `locked:true` (lock-by-default, B99). Salience: the accent fill (`--canvas-selection`) reads as a primary action, distinct from the per-parcel rows and the (only-when-armed-accent) Merge button.
- **Code:** `SitePlanner.jsx` — new `addParcelMenu` state + `addParcelAnchor` ref; the ＋ Add parcel button + `AnchoredMenu` at the top of the Parcel `Section`; the bottom identify block rewritten to drop the duplicate toggle and gate on `identifyMode || identifyRes`; empty-state copy now points at ＋ Add parcel.
- **Deduped:** net-new. NOT B233 (the *map's* address→select+info card), NOT B231/B36c (the multipart-import pipeline it reuses via `addIdentifiedParcel`), NOT B99/B100 (the lock/active model it inherits).
- **Verified:** lint 0 errors · **1201 tests** · build green · `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact; headless **V108** (`ui-audit/verify-b383-add-parcel.mjs`, **14/14** — primary-salience accent bg, both menu methods, Identify arm/disarm, Draw arms the parcel tool, toggle consolidated away, origin-null disabled-copy + Draw-still-works, 0 app errors). The deferred "Add by address" stretch is filed as **B384** (Open) — the geocode logic lives in MapFinder and needs a clean shared extraction, explicitly out of this pass per the request.

### B382 — Parcels in the Fort Bend / Harris seam "take forever to load" then "can't be clicked" while a county CAD host is down `[Site Planner / Map]` (bug)  *(owner-reported from chat 2026-06-22 — "Fort Bend, Cadd … isn't working … takes forever to load, and then … it doesn't work"; minted **B382** — highest B# across both files was B381 (concurrent main PR #285 took B381 for the Schedule-toolbar restore while this was in flight); a recurrence of B244/B137 territory, deduped against them)*
`[x]` **Filed AND fixed + headless-verified the SAME session per STANDING RULE #1 (branch `claude/confident-meitner-j3tv25`).** Two symptoms, ONE upstream cause confirmed with LIVE probes (not guessed): **FBCAD (`gis.fbcad.org`) was down again** — timed out / slow-503 at 12–15s from both Node and headless Chromium — while HCAD and the statewide TxGIO host were up (the exact B244 condition, recurred 2026-06-22). The two existing mitigations didn't fully cover it:
- **Symptom 1 ("forever to load") — the DISPLAY layer had no timeout.** B244's 8s `AbortController` lives only in `fetchJson` (the click/identify path). The visible purple parcel outlines are an esri-leaflet `featureLayer` (`makeParcelLayer`, `MapFinder.jsx`) that bypasses `fetchJson`, so when FBCAD hangs the outline layer spins with no recovery. **Fix:** `addDisplay` now arms an 8s hang-guard for a real county layer (armed on the layer's `requeststart`, disarmed by `load`, so a below-outline-zoom view never false-flags); on timeout/`requesterror` it pulls the dead layer, records the host as failing (feeds the breaker so CLICKS skip it too), and leans on the always-present statewide TxGIO outlines for that ground — keeping what you SEE == what you can SELECT (the B137 rule). The **statewide layer is exempt** from the guard: a slow statewide outline is allowed to finish rather than be pulled (a slow outline beats no outline — that "took a while but worked" wait IS this layer; pulling it would leave nothing to see OR click).
- **Symptom 2 ("can't click the lots") — every click waited on the hung host.** `identifyParcelDetailed` used `Promise.allSettled`, which waits for EVERY candidate — so even though TxGIO answered, each click stalled the full 8s on FBCAD's timeout before resolving, reading as "clicking does nothing." **Fix:** new `identifyParcelEager` (`lib/arcgis.js`) resolves the moment the FIRST source returns a lot (real CADs are queried before the statewide fallback, so a healthy county still answers first), and feeds the circuit breaker the full per-source health via an `onSettled` callback once the slow ones finish (so the next click skips the dead host). The no-hit verdict still waits for all to settle, so "reached a server, no parcel" vs "couldn't reach any server" stay honest (B245). `handleClick` + the address-search `selectParcelAt` both switched to it.
- **Tests/verify:** +3 unit (`test/arcgis.test.js`) — eager returns the hit WITHOUT tripping/awaiting the hung source's timeout then feeds the breaker for both; the no-hit path reports responded/errors honestly; a real-CAD hit is preferred over the statewide one. Full suite **1201 green** (unchanged after merging main — PR #285 added a Playwright harness, no vitest tests), build green, esri-leaflet 3.0.19 `requeststart`/`load`/`requesterror` event contract confirmed present. Headless **V107** (`ui-audit/verify-parcel-resilience.mjs`) — run against the LIVE failing hosts tonight: select mode loads with **0 uncaught errors**, the map stays alive through the full FBCAD hang window (no freeze), and a click resolves in a **bounded 8.1s** (the AbortController cap on the worst-case no-hit path) instead of the open-ended 12–30s+ the raw hung hosts give. (A real lot with a fast source resolves in ~1–4s, per the unit tests.)
- **Forward note:** tonight the statewide TxGIO *query* op was itself slow (its metadata was fast, but spatial queries timed out 30s+ from Node) — so when FBCAD is down AND TxGIO query is degraded, even the universal fallback is slow. This fix makes the click *bounded and non-freezing* and keeps see==click, but it can't make a slow statewide host fast. If TxGIO-query slowness becomes chronic, the roadmap **GIS layer caching** item (stale-while-revalidate parcel outlines) is the durable answer.

### B381 — Restore the missing Schedule toolbar controls (regression) `[Schedule]` (bug)  *(arrived as cross-chat "NEW-1" 2026-06-22; first filed B380, renumbered **B381** — concurrent main PR #284 took B380 for the Schedule render-crash fix while this was in flight, so B381 is the real next free ID; net-new, the completion of B203)*
`[x]` **Filed AND fixed + headless-verified (V106, 15/15) + merged the SAME session per STANDING RULE #1 (branch `claude/vigilant-newton-rovl4l`).** Owner: opening the Schedule module on any project, the Gantt/timeline toolbar was reduced to the **single floating Columns button** above the grid — timeline zoom, Contacts, Export (PDF/print), Version History, the Grid/Split/Gantt view switcher, Automation, Settings and the Review toggle were all gone.
- **Root cause — hidden, NOT deleted (read the code + git, not the brief).** The Schedule module embeds the standalone sequence app (`public/sequence/index.html`) in an **iframe**; the shell's Row-1 breadcrumb takes over project nav, so the sequence app hides its own duplicated nav when `.in-iframe` (the embed app even documents this at the postMessage bridge: "runs in an iframe with its OWN header … hidden"). But the rule was `html.in-iframe .app-header { display:none }` — it hid the **ENTIRE** header, and the whole action toolbar (view switch, Review, Format, Zoom, Export, Save, Version History, Contacts, Automation, Settings) lives inside that same `.app-header`. So every tool vanished; only the in-grid **Columns** button (rendered inside `GridView`, not the header) survived — exactly the reported symptom. All handlers were intact the whole time; a pure CSS over-reach. Confirmed hidden vs deleted (the fix is re-show, not re-add).
- **Fix (`public/sequence/index.html`, 2 small edits).** Narrowed the `.in-iframe` rule to hide ONLY the genuinely-duplicated branding/nav — the logo (gave it a new `.hdr-logo` class), the Dashboard/Projects toggle (`.hdr-mode`) and the project picker (`.hdr-project`), all of which the shell breadcrumb already provides (bridged via the B203 postMessage nav). The rest of `.app-header` (view switcher + Review + the full action group) is visible again, in its original position, with its original handlers — no re-wiring needed because nothing was ever removed.
- **Authoritative restored set (from the actual `.app-header` markup, not the brief):** Grid/Split/Gantt view switcher · Review toggle · Format · timeline Zoom −/%/+ (shown in split/gantt) · Export (PDF·Print Exhibit / Web Snapshot) · Save indicator · Version History · Contacts · Automation · Settings. **The brief's speculative "fit-to-view / today-date-jump / status-filter" controls do NOT exist in this app** — none were ever shipped, so none were restored (per "do not rebuild from a guessed list").
- **Verified working, not just present (V106, `ui-audit/verify-schedule-toolbar.mjs`, 15/15 headless):** toolbar visible in the iframe; logo/mode/project correctly hidden; every action control renders; switching to Gantt reveals the zoom controls; zoom-in changes the % (17→33, proving the handler is wired, not a no-op); Contacts opens its panel. New Playwright regression harness so this can't silently regress again. **Site + Markup checked — NOT affected** (they aren't iframes; they feed their toolbars through the shell's `toolbarContent` slot, which `.in-iframe` can't reach). lint **0 errors** · **1186 tests** green (1198 after merging main's B380) · build green · `Scheduler` lazy chunk intact.
- **Dedup:** NET-NEW, the **completion of B203** (DONE). B203 diagnosed this same `.in-iframe .app-header{display:none}` hide and bridged the **nav half** (project picker + Dashboard/Projects toggle) up to the shell breadcrumb — but the **action-toolbar half** the same rule hid was never re-homed and stayed dark; B381 restores it. NOT a dup of main's **B380** (a separate intermittent Schedule *render-crash* race in `Scheduler.jsx` — different file, different cause, shipped the same day), nor B341 (chrome hardcoded-color/token regressions), nor the Markup `toolbarContent` relocation.

### B380 — Intermittent render crash on Schedule load ("Cannot read properties of undefined"), caught by the workspace ErrorBoundary `[Scheduler]` (bug)  *(arrived as cross-chat diagnosis brief "NEW-1" 2026-06-22; minted **B380** — highest B# across both files was B379; net-new, deduped vs B221/B239 stale-chunk + B315 undo-race)*
`[x]` **Filed AND fixed + headless-verified (V105) the SAME session per STANDING RULE #1 (branch `claude/relaxed-dijkstra-sokq4a`).** Opening the Schedule module would intermittently show the workspace ErrorBoundary's **non-chunk "Try again / Reload page"** fallback with a `<pre>` of the "Cannot read properties of undefined (reading '…')" form; **Try again** (a state reset, not a reload) recovered cleanly. Confirmed NOT the stale-chunk family (B221/B239) — the boundary took the genuine-render-crash path and a pure re-render fixed it.
- **Root cause — reproduced, not guessed.** The Schedule shell embeds the standalone Gantt in an iframe (`/sequence/`) and bridges that app's project list to the shared Row-1 breadcrumb over postMessage (`planar:nav-state`). The shell derives the breadcrumb's current project with `projects.find((p) => p.id === activeId)` (the brief's #1 candidate, `Scheduler.jsx`). The embedded app builds its list as `Object.values(data.projects).map(p => ({id, name}))`; while ITS own data is still loading it can transiently emit a **sparse / not-yet-resolved** list containing an `undefined`/null entry. One such entry makes `p.id` throw **inside the Scheduler's render** → caught by the workspace boundary. A pure re-render recovers because the steady-state list is well-formed, which is exactly why it presents as intermittent. The brief's other candidates (`AppHeader`/`ProjectBreadcrumb` `p.id`/`p.name`, `useProfile/displayName` in `Shell.jsx`) were each verified **already null-safe** (signed-in + real-iframe headless repro, 0 crashes); the deref that actually throws is the Scheduler's `.find`.
- **Fix — guard at the source (not optional-chaining at every call site).** New pure, unit-tested `src/workspaces/scheduler/lib/navState.js` (matches the B315 pure-module precedent): `parseNavState(message)` validates source/type and routes through `sanitizeProjects(list)`, which coerces the inbound list to an array of plain `{id, name}` objects — **dropping the null/undefined/primitive entries that are the only values that throw on a later `p.id`/`p.name` read**; `deriveCurrentProject(projects, activeId, section)` never throws and never returns `undefined` (Dashboard/reports → null; a stale activeId not in the list → null, the empty/loader state). `Scheduler.jsx` routes both the inbound message and the current-project derivation through these. One **data-entry guard** in the shared `ProjectBreadcrumb` (`(controlled ? controlledProjects : internalProjects).filter(Boolean)`) hardens its own `p.id`/`p.name` map for any controlled caller. The race is **removed** so the (now-rare) genuine crash still stays visible — NOT widened `isChunkLoadError`, NOT a blanket ErrorBoundary auto-retry (per the brief).
- **Behaviour preserved.** For the real embedded app's well-formed `{id,name}` payload the output is identical to the previous inline logic — only the not-ready/malformed shapes are made safe.
- **Tests/verify:** +12 unit (`test/schedulerNavState.test.js`) — sanitize drops the throwing entries / keeps real objects, parse validates + sanitizes, derive is null-safe on the race/Dashboard/stale-id paths. Full suite **1198 green**, lint **0 errors**, build green, `Scheduler` lazy chunk intact. Headless **V105** (`ui-audit/verify-scheduler-no-crash.mjs`, 9/9) — the first-render race shows the loader/empty (no boundary), a deliberately malformed nav-state doesn't crash the header and the good projects still render, signed-in-with-late-profile doesn't crash; **proven to FAIL (boundary + page error) with the guard off**, so it's a real regression net. Existing `verify-schedule-picker.mjs` still **8/8** (no regression to the bridge/switch/dashboard).

### B378 — Sheet labels are garbage on text-dense (general-notes / specs) sheets `[Doc Review / Markup]` (bug)  *(arrived as cross-chat "NEW-1" 2026-06-22; minted **B378** — highest B# across both files was B373, so B378 is the real next free ID; extends/hardens B266 + the shared `sheetMeta` reader, deduped against B266/B348)*
`[x]` **Filed AND fixed + headless-verified the SAME session per STANDING RULE #1 (branch `claude/ecstatic-maxwell-6y8aq1`).** A structural general-notes set labelled "atrociously": body boilerplate shown AS the sheet title ("…reproduced or used without…", "CJ DENOTES…"), the same cross-referenced number on several rows ("Structural · S202" ×4), and a mix of those with plain "Sheet N." Root cause: every read was tuned for a normal drawing (sparse plan + one dense title-block strip); a notes sheet (wall-to-wall text, no drawing area) violates all of those assumptions at once. Fixed at the shared reader so BOTH the Markup sidebar and the Stitcher benefit:
- **Title scorer was backwards (`readSheetTitle`, `sheetMeta.js`).** It scored `lineHeight × letterCount`, which *rewards* long sentences — so the copyright block and a legend row outscored the real short title. Re-weighted to **prefer font height, with a small word/letter cap** (a title is a few words, not a sentence): candidates over 7 words / 48 letters are dropped, height dominates the score, letters only break ties. Added a **boilerplate filter** (`property of` / `reproduced` / `copyright` / `denotes` / `continued` / "may not be …") to the existing skip list. Net: "GENERAL NOTES" wins over the boilerplate it used to lose to.
- **The "band-first" guarantee was fictional for the number (`readSheetMeta`).** `parseSheetNumber` ran over the whole-page joined string, and its `(?:no\.?|#)?` is optional, so a body cross-reference ("SEE DWG S202") was grabbed as THIS sheet's number — identical on every sheet that referenced it. Made the number read **title-block-zone-scoped**: from the detected band, or — when a dense notes sheet defeats the density-based band detector — from the right/bottom edge **strip** where title blocks live; only a non-dense sheet may fall back to the whole-page read. So the sheet's OWN number ("S-001") is read and the body cross-ref ("S202") is excluded.
- **`reconstructLines` merged across the full page width.** Two items sharing a baseline but ~900 pt apart (a title-block label and a far-left body note) were joined into one "line", which then failed the title filter as "too wordy" — losing the title entirely on a notes sheet. Now **splits a row on a large horizontal gap** (generous threshold — far bigger than any intra-phrase word gap, so "MATCH LINE … SEE SHEET C-6" still joins), so a title-block title can't bleed into a body line.
- **Sidebar gate too weak (`DocReview.jsx`).** The old `hasReal = sheetNumber || titleBlock` let a bare band authorize a title-derived label. Replaced with a `trustedTitle` gate: a title is surfaced only when it came from a real band, OR is corroborated by a zone-read number, OR the sheet is a recognized text page (general notes/specs) — else it falls back cleanly to the discipline item, then the number, then "Sheet N." Singles now show the real title ("GENERAL NOTES · S-001") instead of a generic discipline label.
- **Identical adjacent numbers = a misread → drop it.** New pure `markAdjacentDuplicateNumbers` (`sheetGroups.js`) clears a sheet number that repeats on an adjacent page (a real set never prints the same # twice in a row) and lowers confidence, so the no-band fallback can't produce a run of identical wrong rows. Applied in both the Markup consumer (`DocReview` `orderedMeta`) and the Stitcher path (`readSheets`).
- **Tests:** +9 unit (`sheetMeta`/`sheetGroups`/`sheetRead`): the title scorer ignores boilerplate, the number is zone-scoped (reads S-001 not the S202 cross-ref), `textDense` is flagged, the dedup clears adjacent duplicates. Full suite **1153 green**, lint 0 errors, build green, `DocReview` lazy chunk intact. Verified **V104**.

### B379 — False auto-calibration ("·≈") on general-notes / specs sheets `[Doc Review / Markup]` (bug)  *(arrived as cross-chat "NEW-2" 2026-06-22; minted **B379** — next free ID after B378; relates to B267 `statedCalibration`, deduped against it)*
`[x]` **Filed AND fixed + headless-verified the SAME session per STANDING RULE #1 (branch `claude/ecstatic-maxwell-6y8aq1`).** On the same structural set, pure-text notes sheets (S00x) showed "·≈" (auto-calibrated) even though they carry no plan scale, while sheet 1 correctly read "NOT TO SCALE." Root cause: `parseSheetScale` matches a scale-looking string **anywhere** in the dense notes text, and `statedCalibration` only gated on a standard plot size — so a 36×24 general-notes sheet with a stray "1\"=20'" in its body auto-calibrated. Auto-calibrating a non-drawing sheet silently mis-scales it (crash-severity per "never auto-guess" — a wrong calibration poisons every downstream takeoff).
- **Fix — classify the sheet, then gate.** `readSheetMeta` now computes a **`textDense`** flag (a general-notes / specifications / legend sheet): true when the title is a notes/specs/legend/index title, or the drawing area is saturated with sentence-like prose (≥10 lines of ≥6 words — plans carry only short labels). `statedCalibration` **returns 0 when `textDense`**, so such a sheet is left uncalibrated ("not present" ≠ "couldn't parse", per B267) rather than silently scaled. A real plan sheet (sparse drawing-area text, a stated scale in its title block) still auto-calibrates exactly as before.
- **Tests:** +1 unit (`sheetRead`: a textDense sheet with a stated scale on a standard plot → 0) plus the `textDense` true/false assertions under B378. Verified **V104** (the same harness asserts the notes sheet shows no "·≈" while the plan sheet still does).

### B374 — Area measurements can't be selected by their filled interior (dead-centre hit target) `[Doc Review / Markup]` (bug)  *(owner-reported from chat 2026-06-22 — "no easy way to delete this little triangle … insane"; minted **B374** — highest B# across both files was B373; batch B374–B377)*
`[x]` **Filed AND fixed + headless-verified + shipped the SAME session per STANDING RULE #1 (branch `claude/youthful-mccarthy-xjcotz`).** Michael's "triangle" was an **uncalibrated Area measurement** — its value label falls back to the literal string **"set scale"** when a sheet has no feet-per-page-unit (`measureLabel`, `lib/takeoff.js`). Clicking the triangle's body to select it (the natural first step to delete it) did nothing.
- **Root cause:** in `DocReview.jsx` `hitTest`, **rect/cloud** got a point-in-bbox interior test (B33) but **area fell through to the generic measures branch — nearest vertex/segment only**. The Area polygon renders FILLED (`fill="#0e749022"`), so it reads as a solid clickable object while its **interior was a dead hit target**; only a click on the thin edge/a vertex registered, and at low zoom (e.g. 26%) that band is nearly impossible to hit → the measurement felt undeletable.
- **Fix:** added an `m.kind === "area"` branch to `hitTest` — `pointInPoly(p, pts)` returns d=0 for a click anywhere inside the polygon. `pointInPoly` is now **EXPORTED** from `lib/takeoff.js` (the same ray-cast already behind `centroidOf`, not a 2nd copy; handles concave outlines). A <3-pt / degenerate area still selects by its edge or vertex via the fallback (now incl. the **closing edge**, which the old branch skipped — also applied to perimeter). Added a **smaller-shape-wins tie-break** on interior (d===0) hits so a small markup sitting on a big filled area isn't swallowed by the area underneath.
- **Verified (V104):** new `ui-audit/verify-delete-markup.mjs` **10/10** (chromium-1228, 0 page errors) — draws an uncalibrated "set scale" Area, then: a **centroid click selects it** (stroke 2→3), a click **outside does NOT** select (hit test stays specific), and Delete removes it. No regression: V72 viewer **13/13**, B300–B302 green. lint 0 · 1144 tests · build green.

### B375 — No on-canvas delete control for a selected markup (deletion was keyboard-only) `[Doc Review / Markup]` (feature) — pairs with B374
`[x]` **Same session/branch.** Even once a markup is selected, removing it was **Delete/Backspace only**, plus a "Delete selected" button buried in the (collapsible) Takeoff panel — nothing on the canvas where the user is looking, so deletion wasn't discoverable. Added a clear **× button anchored to the selected markup's top-right**, rendered OUTSIDE the `pointerEvents:none` overlay (like the inline text/calibrate editors) so it takes its own click; `stopPropagation` on pointer-down keeps that click from starting a pan/draw underneath. Runs the same one-undo-frame path as the Delete key (`pushHistory` → filter out the id → `setSel(null)`). Hidden while editing text / calibrating. Theme tokens only (`--danger-text` fill + `--on-accent` glyph — AA in both themes; no raw hex). Verified in V104 (× appears on the selection and deletes the markup).

### B376 — Per-item delete in the Takeoff list (all markups) + a deletable measure list in the Stitcher `[Doc Review / Markup + Stitch]` (feature)
`[x]` **Same session/branch.** The hit-test-independent removal path, so anything can always be taken off — even on a dense sheet or when not in Select mode.
- **Markup:** the Takeoff "This sheet" list now lists **every markup** (measures + redline rect/cloud + text notes), not just measurements; each row is click-to-select **and carries its own × delete**. Empty-state copy → **"Nothing on this sheet yet."** (the old "No measurements yet" would mislead now that redlines/notes are listed).
- **Stitcher:** it previously had **no way to delete a committed measure at all** — the keyboard handler only trimmed a mid-draw vertex, so a stray "set scale" area on the stitched canvas was permanently stuck. Added a per-measure list under the stitched takeoff totals, each row with a × delete (undoable via the Stitcher's existing `{measures, ftPerUnit}` history snapshot). Full on-canvas select-on-stitch is deliberately **not** built (it never existed there; the list closes the gap without that larger refactor).
- **Verified:** Markup rows in V104 (row × deletes independent of canvas selection); new `ui-audit/verify-stitch-delete-measure.mjs` **ALL PASS** — draw an Area over the auto-aligned base sheet → it's listed with a × → the × removes it (0 page errors). Updated the B300–B302 harness's empty-state copy assertion to the new text.

### B377 — Scanned-sheet OCR worker threw "logger is not a function" on every page (error storm) `[Doc Review / Stitch + OCR]` (bug)  *(found while headless-verifying B374–B376; minted **B377**)*
`[x]` **Same session/branch.** Surfaced by the Stitcher harness runs: a page with no text layer triggers the B352 Tesseract OCR fallback, and the worker threw **`TypeError: logger is not a function`** repeatedly (13× in one B300–B302 run). **Root cause:** `defaultMakeWorker` (`lib/ocr.js`) passed `logger` — always `undefined`, since no caller supplies one — straight into `createWorker({ …, logger })`. Tesseract invokes `logger` on the **main thread** for every progress packet the worker posts back, and an explicit `logger: undefined` **clobbers Tesseract's own default no-op**, so each message threw. **Fix:** default `logger = () => {}` (still injectable for a real progress UI later). Confirmed gone in the unminified dev build (0 `PAGEERROR`) and across all Stitcher harnesses — **B300–B302 uncaught JS errors 13 → 0**. OCR unit tests unaffected (they inject the recognizer, bypassing the default worker). NB the WASM core + English model still load from the jsDelivr CDN at runtime; only the logger crash was in scope.

### B373 — Restore the compact, app-wide cloud-sync indicator in AppHeader Row 1 `[App Shell / all workspaces]` (feature)  *(arrived as cross-chat "NEW-1" 2026-06-22 — a provisional label colliding with the older NEW-1 open-file intent + the B365/B372 NEW-1 markers/delete items; first filed **B366**, renumbered **B373** — a concurrent `main` (PRs #277/#278) took B366–B372 (GIS Site Analysis resilience + source registry, delete-persistence) while this was in flight, so B373 is the real next free ID)*
`[x]` **Filed AND shipped + headless-verified the SAME session per STANDING RULE #1 (branch `claude/vibrant-dijkstra-i3ddzg`).** The small save-status indicator the owner expected in the header had drifted away: the Site Planner showed a **text** chip ("Synced ✓"), Document Review had moved its chip out of Row 1 down to the Row-2 Reviews control (B358), and the Stitcher carried its own — so there was no single, compact, app-wide indicator, and the owner's design intent (a **cloud glyph + check, no "Saved" text**) had been lost. Worse, the failure mode that made it "disappear" was a silent drop-to-blank on error. Restored as **one shared component, app-wide, that goes LOUD on a failed write and never silently vanishes.**
- **New shared `src/shared/ui/CloudSyncBadge.jsx`** — a compact cloud glyph (no text label) driven by the **normalized `saveState` every workspace already computes** (so it reflects the REAL cloud write, never an optimistic always-green). Pure exported `cloudBadgeView(state)` is the whole truth-table → glyph + color + loud/actionable flags. States, each visually distinct (not text-dependent): **synced** = quiet green cloud-check (the resting default); **saving** = amber cloud-up, pulsing; **offline** = amber cloud-pause (saved on device, will sync); **error** = **LOUD** red cloud-slash + a red ring, click → popover with what-failed + **Retry now**; **local** = muted "device" glyph (signed out); **null** = nothing (no project/doc loaded — legitimately empty, not a hidden error).
- **The crash-severity guardrail in code (the headline ask):** the badge wraps itself in a small error boundary (`CloudBadgeBoundary`) that, if the badge ever throws while rendering, shows the **loud error glyph instead of returning null** — the exact "silent unmount" that made the old indicator vanish. Keyed on `state` so a transient throw clears once inputs change, and so it tracks live state across module/project switches without going stale.
- **`AppHeader` renders it once, in Row 1, from `saveState`** — so it's genuinely shared across Site / Schedule / Markup. New optional `onRetrySave` + `saveDetail` props let a workspace supply the retry action and a tailored popover message (e.g. "reload to merge" for a conflict, where a blind retry is wrong).
- **Site Planner:** retired the text `plannerSaveSlot` chip (the compact badge replaces it); wires `onRetrySave={retryCloudSave}` (suppressed for a conflict, which needs a reload) + a conflict `saveDetail`. The loud failure **banners** (cloudSaveFailed / cloudConflict) stay as the can't-miss interrupt; the badge is the always-present at-a-glance state.
- **Document Review + Stitcher:** new pure exported `docSaveState(status, signedIn, idle)` (in `usePersistence.js`) maps the doc-review raw status onto the normalized vocabulary — **a failed/conflicting write → "error" (LOUD)**, idle (nothing loaded) → null (no cry-wolf at rest), signed-in → synced, signed-out-with-content → local. DR feeds it to AppHeader; the **Stitcher has its own chrome (no AppHeader), so it renders its own `CloudSyncBadge`** in its toolbar — same glyph, same loudness, everywhere.
- **Retired the now-redundant Row-2 ReviewsBar save chip** (its `chipFor` + `SaveIcon`) so a module never shows two competing save indicators — the app-wide Row-1 badge is the single source. ReviewsBar is now purely the filing control. Removed the obsolete `test/reviewsBadge.test.js`; its "failed-write-is-loud / no-cry-wolf" contract migrated to the new badge test.
- **Tests:** new `test/cloudSyncBadge.test.js` (13) locks the contract — **a failed save is never visually identical to "all good"** (distinct glyph + color + loud flag), null shows nothing, the crashed fallback is loud, and the doc raw→normalized mapping keeps failures loud. Full suite green post-merge (lint 0 errors, build green; `SitePlannerApp`/`DocReview` lazy chunks intact).
- **Verified (V103):** two headless harnesses (chromium-1194, 0 page errors). `ui-audit/verify-new1-cloud-badge.mjs` **20/20** — every state present and visually distinct, error is loud + click-to-Retry fires the handler, null renders nothing, and **a crashed badge falls back to the loud glyph (does NOT vanish)**. `ui-audit/verify-new1-header-integration.mjs` **5/5** — the badge is wired into the **live** Row-1 header with a project open, shows the honest on-device state logged-out (not a fake green "synced"), and **survives switching modules** (Site → Markup hides it when nothing's loaded → back to Site restores it). Screenshots in `ui-audit/screens/new1-*.png`.

### B372 — A deleted site reappears (delete not persisting) `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(owner-reported 2026-06-22 from chat as "NEW-1"; first filed B366, renumbered **B372** — a concurrent `main` (PR #277) took B366–B371 (GIS Site Analysis resilience + source registry) while this was in flight, so B372 is the real next free ID)*
`[x]` **Filed AND fixed + headless-verified + pushed the SAME session per STANDING RULE #1 (branch `claude/cool-ride-pm0m2l`).** Deleting the HOLLISTER site brought it back — on a hard reload (path A) **and** mid-session with no reload (path B). Crash-severity per the silent-failure principle: a delete that looks successful in the UI but doesn't stick is silent data divergence.
- **ONE root cause for both paths (so kept as one item — the owner said split only if path B were independent).** The site you delete from the map is, in the common case, the one you had **open**: opening it sets `activeSiteId`, and "Back to map" only flips the view — the `SitePlanner` stays **mounted (hidden)**, keyed to that `activeSiteId`. Deleting it calls `deleteSiteGroup` → `setActiveSiteId(null)`, which **unmounts** that planner; its unmount cleanup `persistOrDrop()` (and the `beforeunload`/visibility flush + any queued debounced autosave) then ran `saveSite()` for the just-deleted id, **re-writing the row**. (a) The existing in-planner `deletedSelfRef` guard only covered the *single-plan* delete from inside the planner, NOT the map's whole-site delete. (b) **Path B:** the resurrected record sits in the local store and re-surfaces on the next `refreshSites()` (any map↔plan nav). (c) **Path A:** on reload, `pullCloud`'s heal-the-split sees a local-only row the cloud is missing and **re-pushes it to the cloud**, making the resurrection permanent. This also explains "maybe it's just that project" — it was the one he had open; sites never opened this session had no mounted planner to resurrect them.
- **Fix 1 — kill the resurrection at the one chokepoint (`lib/storage.js`).** A per-tab session tombstone `recentlyDeleted` (Set): `deleteSite` adds the id; `saveSite` refuses to **re-create a deleted, currently-absent row** (`if (!existing && recentlyDeleted.has(id)) return false`). EVERY resurrection path (unmount persist, beforeunload/visibility flush, debounced autosave, a cross-tab storage echo) funnels through `saveSite`, so this closes all of them — not just the one the bug surfaced. A normal edit-save (record still present) and a brand-new site (id never deleted) are untouched; `stageLegacySite`/`importOneSiteToCloud` lift the tombstone so a deliberate same-id re-import still works; it's per-tab and clears on reload (by then the delete has settled).
- **Fix 2 — make a real cloud-delete failure LOUD (never a phantom success).** `cloudDelete` now uses `.delete(…).select("id")` so a 0-row no-op (already gone, or an ownership/RLS mismatch) is distinguishable from a real removal, and a thrown/4xx error returns `{ok:false}`. `deleteSite` **returns** that promise; `deleteSiteGroup`/`deletePlan` AWAIT it, and on a genuine error show a red **"Couldn't delete … from the cloud — it may reappear when you reload"** banner and **re-pull** so the list reflects the honest truth instead of a fake success. (Decision: a 0-row delete is treated as success, not an alarm — a local-only site never pushed to the cloud legitimately removes 0 rows, so alarming on 0-row would cry wolf; RLS also means a row a user can *see* is a row they *can* delete. We alarm only on an actual error, which is the silent case that mattered. This refines the owner's literal "0 rows = failure" into the safer rule that won't false-alarm.)
- **Why the ownership-mismatch theory didn't pan out as the cause (checked first, as asked):** RLS `select` is `auth.uid() = user_id`, so a row visible in the list is owned by the current user — a foreign-owned row would never appear to be deleted in the first place, and wouldn't return from `cloudList` on reload either. The real mechanism was the mounted-planner resurrection above. `cloudDelete` is still hardened to surface a true permission/network error loudly.
- **Verified (V102):** new `ui-audit/verify-b372-delete-durable.mjs` — boots into the planner for HOLLISTER, returns to the map (planner stays mounted), deletes it, and asserts on the **store source-of-truth** + the rendered list: **6/6** (Chromium, logged-out, 0 page errors), incl. not-resurrected immediately, no mid-session reappearance after a list refresh, and still-gone after reload (Schiel preserved). **Proven to have teeth — with the guard disabled the harness FAILS exactly as reported (`store ids = [s2,s1]`, card returns, survives reload).** Plus **9 new unit tests** (`test/deletePersistence.test.js`: `interpretDelete` row-count/error matrix + the end-to-end resurrection guard). **lint 0 · build green · `SitePlannerApp`/`DocReview` lazy chunks intact** (full suite re-run green post-merge).
- **Note for the signed-in tail:** the loud-banner path on a *genuine cloud-delete error* can't be driven logged-out (the sandbox CORS-blocks Supabase auth); its logic is unit-locked (`interpretDelete`) and the local resurrection (the actual bug) is fully headless-verified. A one-line signed-in confirm is noted in VERIFICATION V102, not owed from Michael.

### B368 — Repoint Oil&Gas wells + Pipelines to the authoritative statewide RRC source; pin the Wetlands tier `[Site Planner / Analysis]` (bug — data correctness / false-clean)  *(arrived as coworker-brief "NEW-3" 2026-06-21; minted **B368** — highest B# across both files was B365, batch B366–B369)*

Reporting "no wells" on a Mont Belvieu industrial site is a correctness/liability failure.

Summarizers + detail updated to the RRC columns. The retired hctx endpoints are gone from the screen.

Registered as a **`tier: "monitored-exception"`** in the new registry (B369) with a reason — acknowledged + machine-tracked, not a silent `/Test/` URL.

### B366 — Screening resilience + honest error taxonomy (a 503 is not "CORS") `[Site Planner / Analysis]` (bug)  *(arrived as coworker-brief "NEW-1" 2026-06-21; minted **B366**)*
`[x]` **Fixed + verified 2026-06-22 (branch `claude/nice-cori-ghm37q`).** The screen fired ~8–10 ArcGIS `/query` calls **all at once**; under that burst hosts (even Esri-hosted ones) returned transient **HTTP 503**, with **no retry** (one blip → permanent UNKNOWN) and **every** failure mislabeled "Couldn't reach the GIS server (network or CORS)" though CORS is fine on every endpoint. (A 503 whose error response lacks the CORS header surfaces to `fetch` as an opaque "Failed to fetch" — which is exactly why the catch-all blamed CORS.)
- **New shared `lib/gisFetch.js`:** `fetchArcgisJson` = one resilient fetch — **AbortController timeout** + **jittered exponential-backoff retry** (3 attempts) on a transient 5xx/429/network/timeout + automatic **GET→POST** when a dense-polygon URL gets over-long. `classifyGisError` → an honest `{kind, message, retryable}` taxonomy: `http-5xx`/`http-4xx`/`arcgis`/`timeout`/`network`/`offline` — **never** a blind "CORS" (a bare "Failed to fetch" reads "couldn't reach / temporarily unavailable", since in-browser a header-less 503 is indistinguishable from a real CORS block and a retry usually clears it). `pLimit` concurrency limiter.
- **`runSiteAnalysis` now throttles the WHOLE fan-out** (environmental + jurisdiction + road) through ONE pool of **3** — the burst that provoked the 503s is gone.
- **State machine:** new **`unavailable`** finding status (retryable; amber; a per-source **↻ Retry** control), **visually + semantically distinct from `absent`/"None found"** — a failure is NEVER read as clear (the silent-error guard). The honest reason (e.g. "HTTP 503 — temporarily unavailable") is surfaced; jurisdiction/road use the same shared classifier.
- **Tests:** `test/gisFetch.test.js` (15 — retry-then-succeed, give-up-after-budget, no-retry-4xx, arcgis-200-error-body, POST-for-long-URL, pool max-in-flight, honest-not-CORS). Live headless `gis-verify/site-analysis-resilience-verify.mjs` **11/11** (V101): forced-503 → honest "503", Retry present, 0 "network or CORS", 0 page errors. lint 0 · build green.

Only a failure with **no** cached copy is a hard UNAVAILABLE. Every result already carries its data-age + a screening-only caveat (generalized from the Floodplain "last-good" UI to all rows).

### B369 — GIS Source Registry + verification harness (stop shipping test / non-authoritative endpoints) `[Site Planner / Platform]` (feature / infra)  *(arrived as coworker-brief "NEW-4" 2026-06-21; minted **B369**. Map-display-layer migration tail = B370, Open.)*
`[x]` **Done + verified 2026-06-22 (branch `claude/nice-cori-ghm37q`).** Answers the owner's "why do we keep mapping to test / non-final places?" — two failure modes now have a machine guard: **(1)** we mis-wire it (NWI on `/Test/`, Wells/Pipelines on a Harris republication) and **(2)** agencies move/rename/retire services.
- **Registry** `src/shared/gis/sources.js` — ONE versioned source of truth: per row `key, label, provider, serviceUrl, layerId, geometryType, fields, coverage, tier, lastVerified, fixtures`. The screen (`siteAnalysis.js`) + jurisdiction identify (`jurisdiction.js`) now read EVERY endpoint from here — **zero inline service URLs** in the analysis path.
- **Tier/lint guard (CI — blocks merge):** `ui-audit/gis-source-audit.mjs` + `test/gisSources.test.js` fail the build on a `/Test/`,`/staging/`,`geogimstest`,… URL that isn't an acknowledged **`monitored-exception`** (the only one is Wetlands, locked down), or if an endpoint is re-inlined in the analysis connectors. Wired as a named step in `build.yml`.
- **Coverage / authority fixtures (the centerpiece — what catches 14-vs-8,014):** each row carries known-truth assertions (Chambers wells ≥ 1000, Mont Belvieu well ≥ 1, …); `gis-verify/gis-source-coverage-verify.mjs` checks reachability + that every `outField` still exists on the live layer (schema-drift catch) + the coverage minimums. **Verified in-sandbox** against FEMA/NWI/TxGIO/TxDOT (all pass); RRC rows run in CI (host not on the sandbox allow-list).
- **Drift detection + alerting:** `.github/workflows/gis-drift.yml` re-runs the live verify **weekly**; on any regression it opens/bumps a single **@claude** GitHub issue with the report (auto-closes when green).
- **Runtime fallback chain (#6):** a row may carry `fallbacks`; `analyzeSource` tries the mirror before failing, then the SWR cache (B367) — degrading honestly (B366 taxonomy). Tests: `test/gisSources.test.js` (10) + `test/gisFetch.test.js`. lint 0 · 1129 tests · build green.

### B365 — Redesign project-status map markers for correct visual hierarchy `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as cross-chat "NEW-1" 2026-06-21; first filed **B362**, renumbered **B365** — a concurrent `main` took B362–B364 (bump-out resize, bonded-child rotation, scanned/DWG reading) while this was in flight, so B365 is the real next free ID)*
`[x]` **Filed AND shipped + headless-verified the SAME session per STANDING RULE #1 (branch `claude/trusting-cori-rkn2x3`).** The status markers inverted the hierarchy — Pursuit (most important) was a thin **dashed cool-blue hollow outline** that vanished into the aerial, while settled Complete shouted. Fixed so salience now tracks importance: **Pursuit = eye-magnet, Complete = recessive.**
- **One source of truth (already existed — extended, not duplicated).** `src/shared/ui/statusTokens.js` (`STATUS_TOKENS`/`statusToken`, the B234 set shared by map pins, list rows, filter chips, group headers, and the status menu) is the single map the item asked for. Re-hued + extended it with map-pin fields (`halo`, `tier`, `mapOpacity`, `z`, `mapHollow`, `hideByDefault`); every surface updates together. These status constants stay **deliberately separate** from the module-accent tokens (Site/Schedule/Markup), per the locked rule.
- **Color reassignment (deliberate):** Pursuit blue→**coral `#D85A30`** (warm advances), Active green→**blue `#378ADD`** (blue, NOT green, so it never collides with the Site accent green `#1D9E75`), On&nbsp;Hold amber `#BA7517`, Complete gray `#888780`, Dead red `#E24B4A`. `src/index.css` `--status-*` light + dark mirrors updated to match (dark = lighter variants per B320). **Contrast held:** `contrast-audit.mjs` green in BOTH themes (status glyph-on-card floor 3.0 → coral 3.9 light / 6.6 dark; blue 3.6 light / pass dark).
- **Map pin rebuild (`MapFinder.jsx` `buildingPinIcon`):** solid status fill; **white halo only** (a fattened white copy under the body — no drop-shadow, which flashed on re-render + cost perf) sized by importance (~3/2.5/2/2 px); **size tiers** Pursuit→Complete (largest→smallest, ~25% smaller overall than before); crisp **inline-SVG white glyphs** — flag (Pursuit) / pulse (Active) / pause ‖ (On&nbsp;Hold) / check (Complete); Complete at 0.65 opacity (recessive); **z-order by importance** via `zIndexOffset` (Pursuit on top → Complete bottom; open site floats above its tier) so a settled pin never occludes a Pursuit. **Dead is hidden by default** (shown only when the user explicitly filters to Dead) and rendered as a faint hollow outline when surfaced.
- **Hit target + anchor (gotchas handled):** a **fixed 34×44 hit box** for every state (≥ the old ~32×41 largest) holds the smaller art bottom-centered — so shrinking the art never shrinks the tap target, AND the bottom-center anchor never drifts when a pin changes status/size. `riseOnHover` for overlap clicking.
- **Shape (resolved with owner):** the brief's "keep the existing flat-top hexagon shape" was a **voice-to-text artifact** — owner confirmed he never said hexagon. First shipped keeping the old gabled building silhouette (B161), then mocked up 5 candidate shapes (`ui-audit/mockup-marker-shapes.mjs`); owner chose the **FLAT-TOP SHIELD** (flat top edge → straight sides → a point at the bottom that lands on the exact spot): body `M14,35 L5,22 L5,10 L23,10 L23,22 Z`. `statusGlyph` was re-parameterized to draw each glyph **centered on the head** (cx,cy = 14,16) so the symbol sits dead-center regardless of glyph; verified by `getBBox` (pursuit 14.5/15.85, active 14/16, onhold 14/16, complete 14.2/15.5).
- **One judgment call (flagged to owner):** "Hide Dead by default" was applied to the whole Dead site (pin + zoomed-in plan), the simplest coherent reading; trivially scoped to pin-only if desired.
- **Deduped — NET-NEW, a redesign of (not a duplicate of):** **B161** (the building-marker shape + the now-fixed hollow-dashed Pursuit treatment — its shape is preserved, its inverted-salience treatment replaced), **B234** (the shared status token set — extended in place), **B163/B236** (the progress-arc `progress_pct` encoding — untouched, a SEPARATE encoding deliberately not drawn here). No new open item overlapped.
- **Verified (V100):** new `ui-audit/verify-b365-markers.mjs` → **19/19** headless (chromium-1228, 0 page errors) — Dead hidden (4 markers not 5); correct coral/blue/amber/gray fills; size tiers 21>18.9>17.2>15.1; white halo + flag/pulse/pause/check glyphs present; **each glyph centered on the head (getBBox ~14,16)**; Pursuit z-index above Complete (737>437); fixed 34×44 hit box. Screenshots confirm the flat-top shield + crisp centered glyphs + clean halos over both bright and dark tiles. **1062 unit tests pass, lint 0 errors, build green.**

### B364 — Mobile: pinch-zoom crash ("null is not an object … .mid") + multi-tab banner falsely nagging logged-out users `[App Shell / Site Planner / Doc Review]` (bug)  *(owner-reported 2026-06-21 from a mobile screenshot: opened on phone, "moved around for a sec" → Site Planner error boundary fired; **separately** a "open in another tab" banner appeared though he wasn't signed in and shouldn't carry cross-session state.)*
`[x]` **Fixed + verified 2026-06-21 (branch `claude/mobile-session-state-bug-omeec4`).**
- **Crash root cause:** the two-finger pinch handler (`applyPinch`, B331) read `pinchRef.current.mid` *inside* the `setView` updater. On mobile a finger can lift between scheduling the update and React running the updater — `reseedPinch` nulls `pinchRef.current` — so the deferred updater dereferenced null (`null is not an object (evaluating '…​.current.mid')`) and the workspace's error boundary showed "Site Planner hit an error and couldn't load." **Fix:** snapshot `pinchRef.current` into a local before `setView` in **both** `SitePlanner.jsx` and `doc-review/DocReview.jsx`, so the updater uses the captured baseline and can't hit null.
- **Multi-tab banner root cause / scope:** the B313 same-project-in-another-tab warning fired for **logged-out** sessions too, where it's just a false mobile nag (the banner exists to protect saved *cloud* work, not anonymous device-only browsing). **Fix:** gated to signed-in accounts only — new `accountActive` prop on `AppHeader` (defaults off) plumbed `Shell (!!user) → SitePlannerApp/SitePlanner/DocReview/Scheduler → AppHeader`; presence is fed a null project and the banner is suppressed when logged out. Logged-out = fresh, quiet.
- **Tests:** `test/multiTab.test.js` (10) still green (pure protocol unchanged); `ui-audit/verify-multitab.mjs` rewritten to assert the new behavior (two logged-out tabs on the same project → **no** banner in either) — **3/3 (V99)**. build green.

### B362 — Bump-out (dog-ear) resize doesn't persist; reverts to the 55′×60′ default on any host refit `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as coworker-chat "NEW-1" 2026-06-21, confirmed live on project **Jacintoport** — cloud site `smqdxst8pf3g`, bump-outs `e8986`/`e8987` both stuck at default 60×55. First filed **B357**; renumbered **B362** — a concurrent `main` (#268/#269) took B357–B361 (Markup header de-clutter + Scheduler) while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID. **Folds in** the long-deferred triage item "building bump-outs aren't clamped when the host shrinks" — now closed here.)*
`[x]` **Fixed + verified 2026-06-21 (branch `claude/festive-newton-90t0zh`, PR #271).**
- **Repro:** select a building bump-out, resize it, then resize/edge-drag/numerically-resize the host → the bump snapped back to 55′×60′. **Root cause:** a dog-ear stored no size of its own — `dogEarGeom` always recomputed w/h from the constants `DOGEAR_W`/`DOGEAR_D`, and `refitChildren`→`fitDogEar`→`dogEarGeom` ran for every dog-ear on each host resize, discarding the user's dimensions.
- **Fix:** extracted the bump geometry to a pure, unit-tested **`lib/dogEar.js`** (`dogEarGeom`/`dogEarSize` + the defaults). A resized bump now **records its span along the dock wall + its projection** (`along`/`proj`) on its `dogEar` tag (captured in `refitChildren` the moment the bump is the resized element); `fitDogEar` re-anchors **position + host angle only**, preserving the stored size. The along-span is **CLAMPED to the wall — never reset** — when the host shrinks past the corner (closes the deferred "not clamped" item), and **springs back** when the host grows again. Knock-on correctness: the **dock-door layout** now avoids a bump by its actual span (not a flat 55′), and the **yield panel** says "N bump-outs · sizes vary" instead of falsely claiming "55′×60′" once a bump is resized.
- **Schema:** `SITE_MODEL_VERSION` 6→7; the new `along`/`proj` fields ride inside `els`, lossless/idempotent through `createSiteModel` (absent ⇒ the 55′×60′ default, so every existing bump is unaffected).
- **Tests:** new `test/dogEar.test.js` (5) — default 55×60 + flush-at-corner, the `dogEarSize` inverse, **the exact repro (resize bump → resize host → size preserved)**, clamp-then-spring-back on host shrink, host-rotation carry. Coordinated with B363 (resize re-syncs angle *without* resetting size). **lint 0 · 1066 tests · build green · `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact.** Live: `ui-audit/verify-b362-b363.mjs` 6/6 (V98).

### B363 — Bonded children (bump-outs, court, sidewalk) keep a stale rotation when the host is re-angled `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as coworker-chat "NEW-2" 2026-06-21, confirmed live on **Jacintoport** — host `e8984` at rot 0° but all four bonded children (`e8985` court, `e8986`/`e8987` bump-outs, `e8988` sidewalk) at 359.035°, the whole assembly ~1° off the building. First filed **B358**; renumbered **B363** — `main` #268/#269 took B357–B361 in flight.)*
`[x]` **Fixed + verified 2026-06-21 (branch `claude/festive-newton-90t0zh`, PR #271).**
- **Root cause:** a bonded child's rotation was only copied from the host at create/refit time (`dogEarGeom`/`makeStrip`/`oppTrailerGeom` set `rot: host.rot`); the only thing that re-copied it was `refitChildren`, which runs on host **resize only**. So any state where child rot ≠ host rot — a host placed at a parcel-bearing angle, children added, the host later straightened by a path that didn't carry them — was left visibly off-angle until the next resize.
- **Fix (1) — derived invariant, re-applied on ANY host geometry change.** A bonded box child's angle is now a derived value: `host.rot` + its fixed quarter-turn offset (0/90/180/270 — sidewalks/courts/bump-outs share the host angle; side-parking/wall-trailers sit at a +90/180/270 turn). A shared pure `bondedChildRot`/`quarterOffset` (`siteModel.js`) + a `resyncBondedRot` pass is now folded into **every** host-geometry path — resize (`refitChildren`) **and** rotate (`rotateAssemblyTo` *and* the rotate-handle drag) — so a child can no longer be stranded off-angle (previously only resize re-synced, and only some child types).
- **Fix (2) — one-time repair in migrate.** `normalizeBondedRotations` runs inside `createSiteModel` (the migrate path → fires on every load), re-anchoring a drifted child to the host's **current** frame: its angle snaps to `host.rot + offset` **and** its centre is rotated about the host centre by the stale delta (a host straightened without its children leaves their *positions* stale too, not just the angle value). **Idempotent + identity-preserving** for already-correct data; safe because a bonded box child is only ever at a quarter turn, so any other angle is drift, not intent (points-based children skipped). This **repairs Jacintoport and any other already-diverged project the moment it's opened**, and persists on the next save.
- **Coordinated with B362:** `refitChildren` captures the bump size **before** the rotation resync, and resync only touches `rot` — so re-syncing a child's angle never resets a resized bump.
- **Schema:** `SITE_MODEL_VERSION` 6→7 (shared with B362).
- **Tests:** new `test/bondedRotation.test.js` (6) — the quarter-turn offset math, **the full Jacintoport repair (rot AND position re-anchored)**, idempotency + identity-preservation on correct data, points-children skipped, version-bump guard. **lint 0 · 1066 tests · build green.** Live: `ui-audit/verify-b362-b363.mjs` 6/6 (V98) — drifted assembly straightens on load, user-sized bump keeps 80×70 across a save/load round-trip.

### B358 — Truthful save "cloud" chip — kill the "Not saved" cry-wolf `[Doc Review / Markup]` (bug)  *(parallel-branch handoff "NEW-2" 2026-06-21; minted **B358**)*
`[x]` **Fixed + verified 2026-06-21 (branch `claude/hopeful-dirac-aqjlqb`).** The owner's "the cloud for files is fucked up" was the save badge in **`ReviewsBar`** (the handoff guessed `ProjectBreadcrumb` — the breadcrumb only ever shows an at-risk ⚠; the actual badge is in ReviewsBar, confirmed against the tree). It rendered **"Not saved" with nothing open / nothing to save** — a flag that cries wolf trains the eye to ignore the one state that matters; it also had no `conflict` state (B314 conflicts fell through to "Not saved"). Replaced with a **truthful little cloud chip** driven by one pure `chipFor(status, signedIn, idle)`: **idle (nothing to save) → no chip at all**; **saving** → cloud-↑ + "Saving…" (pulsing amber); **unsaved** → cloud-↑ "Unsaved"; **conflict** → cloud-✕ "Sync conflict" (loud red, never silent); **saved OR signed-in** (cloud-backed, mirroring the Site Planner's "Synced ✓") → calm green cloud-✓ "Saved"; **signed-out with content** → honest "On this device" (a monitor glyph — saved here, can't sync), not a false "Not saved". Colors are theme tokens (legible in light/dark per B341). Headless (logged-out): empty Markup shows **no** save chip; once a PDF is open it reads "On this device". The signed-in "Saved"/`saving`/`conflict` states (sandbox blocks sign-in) are locked by `test/reviewsBadge.test.js` (7 truth-table tests). `components/ReviewsBar.jsx`. **NB:** the separate **"Cloud off"** pill (Shell `authControl`) is a *different* indicator — it only appears when Supabase isn't configured for the build (so it shows in the sandbox preview); on a cloud-configured planyr.io it's the account/Sign-in pill. Left as-is per the handoff's "don't conflate"; if it's visible in production, the cloud env vars aren't wired into that deploy (a config item, not this code).

### B356 — Invisible site-name in the header + a whole-app sweep so it can't happen elsewhere `[App / Theming]` (bug)  *(owner-reported 2026-06-21: "I can't see the project name here … it's gray text on their gray background … go through the entire site and check the rest so this doesn't happen"; filed **B355** but renumbered **B356** — a concurrent `main` (#265, lettered plan concepts) took B355 while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID)*
`[x]` **Fixed + headless-verified BOTH themes 2026-06-21 (branch `claude/gallant-mccarthy-k6sqmr`).** Root cause was the B341 theme-flip trap again: the Site Planner **site-name button hardcoded white text** — `hdrTab(12.5, "#fff", 600)` — on chrome that now themes light, so white-on-near-white was invisible. `contrast-audit.mjs` couldn't catch it because it only checks the **token pairs defined in `index.css`**, and this colour was a literal passed into a style helper (invisible to a `color:` grep, too).
- **Headline fix:** site-name → `PAL.chromeInk` (theme-aware). The same trap also hit the **signed-out "Sign in" avatar** (white "›" on the light pill → `var(--chrome-text)` on `var(--chrome-bg)`) and the **"current" marker** in the site/plan switcher menus (plain accent on the soft-accent fill = 3.8:1 → a new theme-aware `accentStrong`, 7.3:1 light / bright in dark). Also made `ModuleLoader` theme-aware (was `#6b7280` on a hardcoded `#f6f8fa`, 4.26:1).
- **Whole-app sweep (the owner's real ask):** new `ui-audit/contrast-sweep.mjs` walks the **rendered DOM** of every workspace in **both themes**, reading each text node's computed colour vs its effective (first opaque ancestor) background, compositing alpha, applying the AA floor by size/weight. Catches colours set ANY way (helpers, inheritance) — which static analysis cannot. It found exactly the avatar + "current" issues; all now green.
- **Dark-theme hardening:** the sweep + a contrast calc showed **every hardcoded semantic colour** (`#b45309` amber, `#b3361b`/`#b91c1c` red, `#15803d` green, `#0e7490` teal, `#7c3aed` purple, `#1d4ed8` blue) fails AA on a **dark panel** (2.2–3.4:1) while passing on a light one. Added theme-aware **`--success-text` / `--danger-text` / `--info-text`** tokens (+ palette.js mirror; `--warn-text` already existed) and rerouted the semantic TEXT that sits on **themed** panels (SitePlanner inspector, DocReview takeoff + drop-zone, LayerPanel, SiteAnalysis findings, MapFinder status menu) to them. **Left untouched (correct):** fixed-light-banner text, **fixed-`#fff` panels** (Stitcher + Project Files/Library drawers — self-consistent + readable; their not-theming-to-dark is a separate cosmetic item), and SVG/map data-colour tables. **SiteReviewModal** (a fixed-dark modal) had its own too-dim subtitles (`#4a6080` 2.5:1) lightened to AA on its dark bg.
- **Guards:** the 3 new tokens are registered in `contrast-audit.mjs` (8 new pairs, all PASS both themes) so a palette edit can't silently re-introduce a low-contrast pair; `contrast-sweep.mjs` is the runtime net for the helper/inheritance class the static audit can't see.
- **Verified (V96):** `contrast-sweep.mjs` → **0 low-contrast elements** in planner / site-menu / Markup / Schedule, **light AND dark**; `contrast-audit.mjs` all pairs PASS; **1041 unit tests**; lint **0 errors**; build green; screenshots show "Katy Logistics Park" clearly visible in both themes.

### B354 — Markup yield panel miscounts redline annotations as "uncalibrated measurements" `[Doc Review / Markup]` (bug)  *(owner chat 2026-06-21 "keep going" — Markup-tool stress test; minted **B354** — next free after B353)*
`[x]` **Fixed + verified 2026-06-21 (branch `claude/stitch-tool-stress-test-1tvw5b`).** Stress-testing the Markup yield panel turned up a real miscount. The panel warns **"N measurement(s) on uncalibrated sheets are excluded"** from `rollup(markups, calByPage)` — but `rollup` was handed the WHOLE markup list (measurements **and** redline annotations: rect / cloud / line / arrow / text), and any non-measurement kind on an *uncalibrated* sheet fell into `measureValue`'s generic branch (`calibrated:false`) and incremented `uncal`. So drawing a redline cloud or adding a text note on an uncalibrated sheet made the panel falsely warn "1 measurement(s) … excluded" when **zero** measurements were made (and could mislead a reviewer into thinking a real takeoff was dropped). `rollup` now tallies **only** the measurement kinds (`distance/perimeter/area/count`, derived from the existing `MIN_MEASURE_PTS` so there's one source of truth) and skips everything else (and null entries) outright. Totals were already correct (redlines never matched the area/perimeter/distance branches); only the `uncal` warning was wrong. `lib/takeoff.js`. **New `test/markupRollupStress.test.js` — 6 adversarial tests** (redlines don't inflate `uncal`; redlines on a calibrated sheet aren't summed; a true uncalibrated measurement still counts; all four measure kinds total correctly; null/unknown-kind entries don't crash; a non-finite page calibration excludes the measure). Existing 16 takeoff tests still green; full suite **994 tests**, lint 0 errors, build clean. Pure-logic fix — no live-browser verification needed.
