### B303 — Undo / redo for Document Review markups + calibration `[Doc Review / Markup]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1" 2026-06-20 owner chat; provisionally B283, renumbered **B303** — concurrent `main` consumed B283–B302; batch B303–B307)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/stoic-faraday-th9mp8`).** Repro: place/delete/move a markup or measurement, press Ctrl/⌘-Z → nothing happened; the workspace had no history at all, so a mis-edit was unrecoverable. **Fix:** **Ctrl/⌘-Z undo, Ctrl/⌘-Shift-Z + Ctrl-Y redo** in BOTH `DocReview.jsx` (single sheet) and `Stitcher.jsx` (stitched set), plus on-canvas **↶ / ↷** buttons (disabled when there's nothing to undo/redo).
- **Pattern reused, not reinvented:** mirrors the Site Planner's `pushHistory` — `pastRef`/`futureRef` of editable-state snapshots taken **by reference** (DocReview `{markups, calByPage, calInfo}`; Stitcher `{measures, ftPerUnit}`), with a `histKey` signature so `undo` **skips frames identical to the current state** — the **B32/B105 lesson** that a stray push can't make Ctrl-Z look like a no-op. `pushHistory()` fires only on a REAL mutation; the background stated-scale auto-scan (B267) deliberately does NOT push. History resets when the document context changes (open new PDF / load / new review).
- **Covers `main`'s viewer edits too:** a markup **move** (B293, committed on pointer-up) and a **text create/edit/delete** (B293 inline editor) each push one frame, so the new editing affordances are undoable as well as plain draws.
- **Poly-vertex placement:** mid-draw, Ctrl-Z (and Backspace/Delete) step back the **last placed vertex** of a polygon/area/count draft before falling through to full undo / delete-selection.
- **Verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-b303-b307.mjs`): draw a rect → Ctrl-Z removes it → Ctrl-Shift-Z and Ctrl-Y each restore it; undo disabled before any edit; same proven in the Stitcher.

### B304 — Manual Calibrate validates input (no more silent mis-calibration) `[Doc Review / Markup]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-2" 2026-06-20 owner chat; provisionally B284, renumbered **B304**; batch B303–B307)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/stoic-faraday-th9mp8`).** Repro: Calibrate → click two points → at the length prompt type a non-decimal form (e.g. **"1/8"** or **"1:240"**) → `parseFloat` returned **1** and the sheet calibrated to a wrong scale with NO warning, silently poisoning every downstream measurement; gibberish ("abc") silently did nothing. **Root cause:** `parseFloat(window.prompt(...))` stops at the first non-numeric char, and the invalid branch `return`ed with no feedback.
- **Fix:** replaced `window.prompt` with an **inline on-canvas entry box** (honoring the owner "no dialog boxes" rule, like `main`'s B293 text editor) backed by a new tested parser **`parseFeet`** (`lib/parseLength.js`). It validates the WHOLE string: accepts plain feet (`120`, `120.5`, `120'`), **feet-and-inches** (`38'-7 3/4"`), and explicit fractional feet (`12 1/2 ft`); **rejects** scale ratios (`1:240`), bare ambiguous fractions (`1/8`), non-numeric junk, and zero/negative — each with a clear inline message. A bad entry keeps the box open to fix; a blank cancels. Applied in BOTH `DocReview.jsx` and `Stitcher.jsx`.
- **Dedup:** distinct from **B267/B268** (auto-calibrate / scale cross-check) — the **manual-entry** path they don't cover. Clears the **calibration** half of the B155/B156 "no dialog boxes" note; `main`'s B293 already converted the **text** prompt, so only ParcelDrawing's calibrate prompt remains under B155.
- **Verified:** unit — `test/parseLength.test.js` (7 cases incl. the exact "1/8" / "1:240" / "abc" bugs). Headless — the inline box opens (no prompt), **rejects "1/8" and stays uncalibrated**, rejects "1:240" as a ratio, and **accepts "100" → sheet calibrated** (single sheet + Stitcher).

### B305 — Markup toolbar overcrowds; header buttons wrap into uneven multi-line labels `[Doc Review / Markup]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-3" 2026-06-20 owner chat; provisionally B285, renumbered **B305**; batch B303–B307)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/stoic-faraday-th9mp8`).** Repro (confirmed live at 1568px wide): the header's "Open another…", "Stitch sheets ▸", "Library" buttons wrapped their labels onto 2–3 lines at uneven heights; the single toolbar row was too crowded and worsened as the window narrowed. **Fix (the B117/B118 density treatment):** every toolbar button now carries **`white-space: nowrap`** (labels never break mid-word) + tightened padding; the three file-action buttons are condensed (`Open…`, `Stitch ▸`, `📁 Library`) with full-text `title`s; sections are grouped with thin dividers (file · tools · undo/redo · zoom). `DocReview.jsx` + `Stitcher.jsx`.
- **Verified headless:** the Open / Stitch / Library buttons compute `white-space:nowrap` and render as a **single 25px line** (≤34px) at 1440px — no wrapping. Screenshot `screens/b303-b307.png`.

### B306 — Sheet paging: Prev/Next buttons + keyboard `[Doc Review / Markup]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-4" 2026-06-20 owner chat; provisionally B286, renumbered **B306**; batch B303–B307)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/stoic-faraday-th9mp8`).** Repro: on a 32-sheet set the only way to change sheets was clicking each entry in the left list — no Prev/Next, and arrow / PageUp / PageDown didn't flip sheets. **Fix** (`DocReview.jsx`): a **‹ N / total ›** pager above the sheet list, plus **← / → and PageUp/PageDown** keyboard paging (gated so they don't fire mid-draw or mid-calibrate-entry), and the sheet list **auto-scrolls to keep the current sheet in view** (`scrollIntoView`). A shared `goToPage` keeps the current zoom (matching `main`'s viewer behaviour) and drops any in-progress draft/selection.
- **Verified headless:** Next advances 1/4→2/4; → / ← page 2/4→3/4→2/4; the indicator + active-sheet highlight track.

### B307 — Measurement labels sit at the path midpoint / true centroid `[Doc Review / Markup]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-5" 2026-06-20 owner chat; provisionally B287, renumbered **B307**; batch B303–B307)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/stoic-faraday-th9mp8`).** Repro: a Distance label rendered on the first endpoint (`pts[Math.floor((len-1)/2)]` resolves to `pts[0]` for a 2-point line); an Area label sat at the vertex average, which can fall outside a concave (L-shaped) region. **Fix** (new pure helpers in `lib/takeoff.js`): **`midOfPath(pts, closed)`** anchors distance/perimeter labels at the true **arc-length midpoint**; **`centroidOf(pts)`** anchors area labels at the **area-weighted centroid**, and when that lands outside a concave shape it drops to the midpoint of the widest interior scanline span so the label stays **inside**. Wired into `DocReview.jsx` (distance/perimeter/area) and `Stitcher.jsx` (area). Coexists with `main`'s B296 (the label's 1-dp numeric format) — B307 is the label's POSITION.
- **Verified:** unit — `test/takeoff.test.js` (midpoint of a 2-pt line + an L; closed wrap-around; square centroid; concave-L centroid proven interior by ray-cast). Headless — a horizontal distance label renders at **x≈454** (midpoint ≈450), not ≈250 (pts[0]).
### B300 — Stitcher alignment has no degenerate-baseline guard; coincident clicks fling the sheet with a garbage transform `[Doc Review / Stitch]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1" 2026-06-20 owner chat; first filed B288 then renumbered **B300** — concurrent `main` consumed B288–B299; batch B300–B302)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/admiring-hypatia-xjv8a1`).** Repro (numerically verified): in Stitch, aligning a sheet means clicking two matching points; if the two clicks on the moving sheet (or the two reference points) land on ~the same spot, `solveM`'s `lb = Math.hypot(vb) || 1` **masked the zero baseline** and returned an extreme similarity transform (e.g. `solveM(b1==b2, A1, A2 100 apart)` → ×100 scale, e/f ≈ −500), throwing the sheet far off-canvas at huge scale — silently, and Stitch has no undo. **Fix:** extracted the pure stitch geometry (`fwd`/`inv`/`solveM`/`sheetBBox`) out of `Stitcher.jsx` into a unit-testable **`lib/stitchGeom.js`**, and added **`alignBaselinesDegenerate(b1,b2,A1,A2)`** + `MIN_ALIGN_BASE`, which rejects an alignment whose moving-sheet baseline `|b2−b1|` **OR** reference baseline `|A2−A1|` is below a small threshold (mirrors DocReview's Calibrate "line too short" guard). The align commit checks it **before** `solveM`: on a degenerate baseline it shows the banner ("Those two points are too close together — pick two points farther apart…") and restarts the alignment at step 0, leaving the sheet **untouched**; only a healthy baseline applies the transform (and now also stamps the sheet `aligned:true`, see B301).
- **Verified:** 8 unit tests (`test/stitchGeom.test.js`, incl. the runaway-scale case the guard blocks + `solveM` scale/rotation recovery + `fwd`/`inv` round-trip) and **headless on the built app** (`ui-audit/verify-b300-b302.mjs`, chromium-1228): a degenerate Align shows the banner and the sheet's `<g transform>` is **unchanged** (not flung); a real Align still succeeds. lint 0 · build green; DocReview lazy chunk still splits (stitchGeom rides inside it).
> **Dedup (batch B300–B302):** net-new — no existing item covers the stitch alignment math. NOT main's single-sheet-viewer **B288–B296** (zoom/pan/markup-edit) nor its auto-filing **B299** (server-side title-block read), all different surfaces; distinct from **B181/B182/B183** (the *map* placement cascade) and **B130/B131** (parking). Shares `lib/stitchGeom.js` with B301.

### B301 — Measuring over a not-yet-aligned sheet silently uses the composite scale → wrong quantities `[Doc Review / Stitch]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-2" 2026-06-20 owner chat; first filed B289 then renumbered **B301**; batch B300–B302)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/admiring-hypatia-xjv8a1`).** Repro: add a second sheet (it drops at identity scale, offset to the right) and draw a Distance/Area over it **before** pressing Align — the measurement applied the single composite calibration (ft per world unit, defined by sheet 1), so if that sheet's real scale differed the reading was **silently wrong** (and even at a shared scale its position/rotation could be off). **Fix:** each placed sheet now carries an **`aligned`** flag — the first sheet *is* the world frame (auto-aligned `true`); every later sheet starts `false` and flips to `true` only when its Align completes (B300's commit path). Unaligned sheets are **flagged visually** — an amber dashed "⚠ Not aligned — click Align" overlay on the canvas, plus a "⚠ Not aligned — measurements may be off" chip + amber-emphasized Align button in the Placed-sheets list. Committing a Distance/Area whose points fall over an unaligned sheet (**`measureOverUnaligned`** / `sheetContains` in `lib/stitchGeom.js`) raises a **warning banner** ("Heads up: that measurement is over a sheet that isn't aligned yet — Align it first…"). **Warn, not block** (the app's "surface it loudly, let the user decide" principle). The flag is persisted in the stitch snapshot and restored on load — older saves default their non-base sheets to aligned, so nothing already-saved is falsely flagged.
- **Verified:** unit tests for `sheetContains` + `measureOverUnaligned` (warns only over an `aligned:false` sheet; never over the base or with no sheets) and **headless**: a fresh 2nd sheet shows the canvas overlay + the panel chip, a measurement over it shows the warning, and a successful Align clears both. lint 0 · build green.
- **↑ Superseded by B316 (2026-06-21, owner call "don't let it measure on uncalibrated things"):** the **warn** became a **hard block** — a Distance/Area point over an un-aligned sheet is now refused at click time (`blockedOverUnaligned`, nothing commits), and the chip reads "Not aligned — Align before measuring." `measureOverUnaligned`/`aligned`-state unchanged. See B316 / V83.

### B302 — Degenerate 2-point Area (0 sf) and 2-point Perimeter (single segment) are committable `[Doc Review / Markup]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-3" 2026-06-20 owner chat; first filed B290 then renumbered **B302**; batch B300–B302)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/admiring-hypatia-xjv8a1`).** Repro (numerically verified): `finishDraft` committed Area/Perimeter at ≥2 points, but a real polygon needs ≥3 — a 2-point Area saved as **0 sf** (shoelace) and a 2-point Perimeter drew closed yet measured only the single segment (10 ft for a 10-unit span at 1 ft/u, not the 20 ft a closed loop implies), leaving meaningless zero/half entries in the takeoff list. **Fix:** added **`MIN_MEASURE_PTS` + `canCommitMeasure(kind,n)`** to `lib/takeoff.js` (area/perimeter ≥3, distance 2, count 1 — matching what `polyArea`/`pathLength` actually need) and gated **both** finish paths on it — Enter/`finishDraft` and (after merging main's B291 phantom-point fix) double-click/`onDbl` — so a 2-point Area/Perimeter is a no-op (the draft is cleared) whichever way you finish, consistent with the existing count min-point guard. Other kinds (distance/rect/cloud/calibrate) are unaffected.
- **Verified:** unit tests for `canCommitMeasure` (the ≥3 / 2 / 1 contract) + the degenerate-geometry rationale (2-pt area = 0; a 2-pt "closed" path = one 10-unit segment, not 20; a real 3-pt loop closes 3+4+5=12) and **headless**: a 2-point Area finished by Enter or double-click commits nothing and the takeoff stays "No measurements yet", while a 3-point Area commits one polygon. lint 0 · build green.
> **Dedup:** minor severity (clutter, not corrupted totals — a 0-sf area contributes 0 to the rollup), filed with B300/B301 but a separate surface (`takeoff.js` / single-sheet Markup). Complements main's **B291** (which stripped the double-click's phantom points) by also enforcing the ≥3 minimum on that finish path.

### B299 — Auto-filing: drop a drawing → it reads the title block → matches a project → files itself `[Document Review / Server + Files]` (feature)  *(owner HANDOFF 2026-06-20; first built as B270, renumbered through a very hot `main` that consumed B270–B298 — incl. a different **B270** (Project Files drop-zone queue) and a different **B297** (account profiles) — so it landed at the real next free ID **B299** at merge time)*
`[x]` **Built + wired + tested this session (branch `claude/sleepy-archimedes-gts4wa`).** The auto-filing **backend tranche**: drop a PDF → a server-side title-block read → match to one of the named projects → auto-route + auto-name, with a "needs filing" tray for anything it can't confidently match. Server-side because the read uses an **API key that must never reach the browser** (KEY DECISIONS) — it lives in the `/server` compute layer (Cloud Run), distinct from Supabase. Status mirrors the convert (B238) / Drive (B207) backends: **code complete, fully unit-tested, wired through the UI, gated dormant** until the owner provisions Cloud Run + `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` + `DOC_FILING_URL`.
- **Title-block reader** `server/filing/titleBlockReader.js` — mirrors the client `titleReader.js` request shape (model `claude-opus-4-8`, adaptive thinking, a `json_schema` output, the PDF as a base64 `document` block) but runs **server-side** and calls the Messages API over **raw `fetch` with an injectable `fetchImpl`** (like `server/convert/aps.js`), so the Cloud Run image stays dependency-free and the read is unit-testable without a key. **One read, two payoffs:** the same pass captures the FILING fields (project / number / address / parcel / discipline / sheet # / title / revision / date) AND the PLACEMENT-readiness facts (scale callout + bar, north arrow, drawn boundary, stated coord system, labeled dimensions) in the shape of `src/shared/placement/placementFacts.js`. Pixel-geometry (scale-bar length in px, dimension endpoints) is deliberately left to the later CV step (B268/B183) — the read captures presence + printed values, never guessed geometry. `parseStatedScaleFeetPerInch` handles engineer's (`1"=40'`) + architectural (`1/4"=1'-0"`) scales, NTS→null.
- **Matcher** `server/filing/matcher.js` (pure) — scores each project on parcel/account (exact) → job number (exact) → address (token overlap) → name (token overlap), combined noisy-or; **never auto-guesses** (a misfiled drawing is worse than an unfiled one). A confident SINGLE project → `matched`; **no / multiple / low-confidence** → `needsFiling` with a reason (`no-readable-identifiers` / `no-match` / `ambiguous` / `low-confidence`). Thresholds tunable via env. `scoreProject` is transparent (lists the signal it matched on). Auto-name `server/filing/naming.js` mirrors the canonical `reviewStore.composeTitle` "<Project> - <Item> - YYYY.MM.DD".
- **Service + HTTP** `server/filing/filingService.js` (read → match → decision + the index row) + `server/filing/server.js` (`POST /file` body = PDF bytes, `X-Planyr-Projects` header = base64 JSON; `GET /health`) — honest status codes (200 real decision / 400 / 413 / 422 unreadable / 503 not-configured), **never a 200 with a junk decision**. `Dockerfile` (no native binary, no npm install — built-ins only) + `README.md`. The reader/service/server are injectable end-to-end (mirrors `dwgConvert.test.js`).
- **File-facts index (Supabase Postgres, NOT /server)** — `src/workspaces/doc-review/db/file_facts.sql`: `public.file_facts` (one small row per filed drawing: project / discipline / sheet / revision / date / match confidence / needs-filing / placement jsonb), RLS private-by-default identical in shape to `doc_reviews`, indexed `(user_id, project_id, discipline, doc_date desc)` for the north-star "map → project → discipline → latest set" without re-reading the PDF. Client I/O `reviewStore.upsertFileFacts/listFileFacts` (degrade gracefully if unmigrated) + pure helpers `lib/fileIndex.js` (`toFactsRow`, `mergeFactsIntoReviews` — surfaces captured placement on the drawer's review rows).
- **capturePlacementFacts wired (deliverable #4)** — `src/workspaces/doc-review/lib/autofiling.js` is the real `createIndexProvider`: `capturePlacementFacts` + `autofile` ride the SAME server read. `backendReady` reflects `VITE_AUTOFILE_ENABLED` honestly (false by default → UI never claims "auto-detected" while dormant). Same-origin proxy `functions/api/file.js` (verifies the Supabase session, forwards to Cloud Run `DOC_FILING_URL`; 503 until set). The drawer drop handler auto-files when `backendReady`, else the **exact** prior manual path (a 404/503 is a graceful SKIP, like the Drive path) — **no regression**.
- **Verified — lint 0 · 602 tests (52 new: `test/docFiling.test.js` 37, `test/autofiling.test.js` 15) · build green; doc-review lazy-chunk split intact.** Headless on the built app (`ui-audit/verify-b299-autofiling.mjs`): the Project Files drawer opens, the new `autofilingProvider`/`fileIndex` imports evaluate in a real browser, **0 page/console errors**, auto-filing dormant by default (no spurious "it files itself" behavior). The signed-in drop→read→file round-trip + the live read are the deploy-gated checks (sandbox blocks sign-in + no key) — logged as **VERIFICATION V74**.
- **Dedup:** this is the backend that fills the `createIndexProvider.capturePlacementFacts` seam B180/B181 stubbed and the auto-filing roadmap item; it WRITES THROUGH the Drive substrate (B207) and feeds the placement cascade (B182/B183). Distinct from B266/B267/B268 (the in-Markup sheet-label/scale siblings of the read pass) — those share the title-block read principle but run browser-side on the open sheet; this is the filing index. **Owner to-do (deploy, when ready):** `gcloud run deploy` `server/filing/` + set `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` (server-side) + point `DOC_FILING_URL` at it + set `VITE_AUTOFILE_ENABLED=1` + run `db/file_facts.sql` once.

### B297 — First/last name capture at signup + a real `profiles` table `[Auth / Backend]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; first labeled B271, renumbered **B297** — concurrent `main` consumed B271–B296)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/eloquent-edison-6anmlb`).** Names are now persisted in a queryable **`public.profiles`** table (one row per `auth.uid()`), not just in auth `user_metadata` — the scalable foundation for the B2B direction (org/role/prefs later). The signup form already collected First/Last/Org; that path is unchanged (still seeds `signUp({ options: { data } })`), but a DB **trigger** now copies those into the table so there's one queryable source of truth for display.
- **Migration (idempotent, run once in the Supabase SQL editor):** `src/workspaces/site-planner/db/profiles.sql` — the `profiles` table (`id uuid pk → auth.users on delete cascade`, `first_name`, `last_name`, `org`, `updated_at`); **RLS private-by-default** (the same select/insert/update own-row shape as `public.sites`/`public.doc_reviews`, `auth.uid() = id`, no cross-user reads, no delete — the row lives/dies with the user); a `handle_new_user()` **SECURITY DEFINER trigger** on `auth.users insert` that inserts the matching row from `raw_user_meta_data` (the trigger route avoids the client-side follow-up-insert race — the row always exists before the user can read it); and a **backfill** that seeds rows for all existing users (null names are fine — the UI falls back, see B298). `on conflict (id) do nothing` throughout so re-running is safe.
- **Client I/O + hook (additive, reuses the existing anon client + session — no new keys):** `src/workspaces/site-planner/lib/profile.js` (`loadProfile`/`saveProfile`, mirrors `cloudSync.js` shape; throws on a real fetch error so "no row" ≠ "offline"; `saveProfile` also best-effort syncs the name into auth `user_metadata` so the table and the auth record never disagree and the offline fallback stays fresh) and `src/shared/profile/useProfile.js` — the `useProfile(user)` hook returning `{ profile, loading, displayName, firstName, org, initial, reload, save }`, with a stale-fetch guard (a slow load can't show the previous user's profile) and an optimistic local update on save so the pill refreshes instantly.
- **Verified — lint 0 · 572 tests (562 + 10 new) · build green.** The never-blank display chain is pure-extracted (`displayNameFor`/`firstNameFor`/`orgFor`/`initialFor`) and unit-tested in `test/profileDisplay.test.js` (profile wins over metadata; First Last → first → last → metadata → email; whitespace-only trims to email; empty only when there's no user). The actual cloud round-trip (real profiles table read/write while signed in) needs a signed-in click-through — the sandbox proxy CORS-blocks auth — logged as **VERIFICATION V73**.
> **Dedup:** builds on the existing email/password auth (Supabase Phases 2–4) and the `AuthPanel` signup form (which already had the name fields). Distinct from the Site Model `status` reuse (B14) — this is per-*user* identity, not per-*project* lifecycle. The deferred `planarfit:* → planyr:*` localStorage rename is untouched (separate item).

### B282 — Opening a file from the global Project Files panel no-ops on the first click when launched from another workspace `[Doc Review]` (bug)  *(owner-reported 2026-06-20, repro'd in the signed-in session; arrived as "NEW-1"; first filed B270 then renumbered **B282** — concurrent `main` consumed B270–B281 (incl. a different B270, the Project Files drop-zone queue) while this was in flight, so B282 is the real next free ID. "NEW-1" is only a scratch label — B180/B206/B266/B270 also "arrived as NEW-1".)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/wonderful-galileo-abbbus`).** From the Site side, opening the global **🗂 Files** panel (with a project like Jacintoport open) and clicking a filed document (e.g. the MEP set) switched to the **Markup** tab but landed on the empty **"Open or drop a construction PDF"** placeholder — the document did **not** open; it stayed empty even after a multi-second wait, with **no console errors** (silent). The breadcrumb also reset to "Select a project". Clicking the **same file a second time** (now that Document Review was mounted) opened it correctly. 
- **Root cause (confirmed via the repro).** Document Review is a **lazy-loaded workspace** — the Shell renders only the active workspace (`React.lazy`/`Suspense`), so DR's code doesn't mount until you first enter the tab. The **global** Project Files drawer lives in the Site Planner (`SitePlanner.jsx`), and its open handler was `onOpenReview={() => onShellSwitch?.("doc-review")}` — it **switched workspaces but threw away the clicked review row entirely**. So in the same tick the app switched to DR *and* dropped the open request; DR mounted fresh and booted to its default/resume state, never opening the clicked file. The second click worked because DR was by then already mounted and its **own** in-workspace drawer wires `onOpenReview={openReview}` (the real handler). (The in-workspace path was never broken — only the cross-workspace one.)
- **Fix — persist the open-intent across the mount, mirroring the existing `navIntent` pattern.** New **`docIntent`** channel in `Shell.jsx`: `openReviewInDocReview(row)` stashes a **token-stamped** `{ kind:"open-review", row }` and *then* switches to `doc-review`; the Shell passes `docIntent` + `onOpenReviewInDocReview` to every workspace (parallel to the `navIntent`/Dashboard plumbing). The Site Planner's global drawer now calls `onOpenReview={(row) => onOpenReviewInDocReview?.(row)}` (threaded `SitePlannerApp` → `SitePlanner`), handing the **whole review row** up. `DocReview` consumes the pending intent in a mount/update effect (`openReview(row)`), guarded by a **module-scoped `lastConsumedDocToken`** (same technique as `SitePlannerApp`'s `lastConsumedNavToken`) so a plain tab switch-back never re-fires the last open.
- **No race with resume.** DR's boot effect (resume-the-last-review) now **stands down** when a fresh open-intent is present at mount (captured once via `bootDocIntentRef`), so the two async loads can't fight and silently land the wrong file.
- **Breadcrumb carries through.** `markupProject` is **seeded from the fresh intent** at mount (handling both a `listReviews` row's `project_id` and a loaded record's `projectId`), and `openReview` re-confirms it after load — so the project context no longer flashes to "Select a project".
- **Can't fail silently again.** `openReview` is hardened: it wraps `loadReview` in try/catch and, when the row can't be loaded (removed row / cloud unreachable), shows a **visible dismissible error banner** ("Couldn't open …") with a **Browse Files…** retry, instead of the previous bare `if (!rec) return`.
- **Verified — lint 0 · 550 tests · build green; the DocReview / SitePlannerApp / ProjectFilesDrawer lazy chunks all still split (workspace isolation intact).** Headless smoke on the **built** app (`ui-audit/verify-new1.mjs`): Document Review **mounts and remounts cleanly** with the new `docIntent` prop + ref capture + intent effect + hardened `openReview` + error banner — **zero JS errors** on a fresh mount AND after an unmount/remount. The signed-in **first-click open** itself (global Files → click a real filed set → DR opens it on the *first* click, breadcrumb shows the project) is **auth-gated** — the sandbox proxy blocks sign-in and this build has no Supabase creds, so the panel can't list real files headless — logged for a live signed-in confirm on planyr.io as **VERIFICATION V70**.
> **Dedup:** net-new — the only cross-workspace "open a file into Document Review" handler is the global `ProjectFilesDrawer` rendered by `SitePlanner` (the in-workspace DR drawer + `ReviewsBar` + `ProjectLibrary` already call `openReview` directly and were unaffected). Distinct from **B180** (the Files tagged-index/saved-views feature this rides on) and from the silent-no-op family (**B82** calibrate, **B32** undo, the map-click open in B66) — those are unrelated surfaces. Reuses the **B191–B193** `navIntent` cross-workspace pattern rather than inventing a new mechanism. Distinct from the concurrently-landed **B270** (Project Files drop-zone + processing queue) — same `ProjectFilesDrawer` file, unrelated concern (file ingestion vs. cross-workspace open).

### B283 — Coverage detection engine + honest per-layer status states `[Site Planner / GIS]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1" 2026-06-20; minted **B283** — highest B# across both files was B273)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/busy-allen-ofgy9l`).** New **`lib/coverage.js`** engine answers, per layer, whether its DATA reaches the current view — so a layer that loads green but paints blank outside its region reads as "no data here," not "broken" (the COH water/sewer/storm root cause). Each layer is tagged **national | statewide | regional** (`LAYER_SCOPE`). For a **regional** layer the engine reads the service's own **`fullExtent` from the existing `?f=json` health probe** (`probeService` now captures it — **no extra request**), reprojects it to lat/lon, buffers it by the nearby radius (NEW-2/B284), and intersects it with the viewport → **`in` / `out` / `unknown`**. The three honest states (`displayCoverage`): **data-in-view**, **covers-region-but-empty-here**, **out-of-coverage**. National/statewide are **always in-coverage** (their empty/painted state still comes from the in-view query). **Fails open everywhere** — missing extent or errored probe → treated as available, never hidden.
- **Real reprojection (the crux):** services publish their extent in mixed SRs — verified live 2026-06-20 that **HCFCD/City-of-Houston use EPSG:2278 (Texas State-Plane, US ft)** while AGOL layers use **Web Mercator (3857)**. So the shared `src/shared/coordinates/index.js` stub's reserved **`projectToGrid`/`gridToProject`** are now **implemented** (Lambert Conformal Conic 2SP per EPSG GN 7-2), **validated against pyproj to <1e-4°**; `coverage.js` dispatches 4326 / Web-Mercator / 2278 and reprojects all 4 extent corners to safely enclose the conic footprint. This is a read-only screening use — the planner keeps its own per-site feet frame.
- **HARD RULE honoured + unit-tested:** coverage is a **picker-only** signal and **never** alters a layer's request bbox/where/extent. The request-spec builders live in a leaflet-free **`lib/layerRequest.js`** that takes **no coverage input by construction**; `test/coverage.test.js` asserts the COH request always carries its **full pinned sublayer set [0,1] and no where/bbox**, coverage-independent.
- **Wired** into the map finder + planner (recompute coverage on map move / view change, debounced, + when the nearby-range pref changes; regional extents prefetched once via the health probe and cached). **Tests:** `coverage.test.js` (27) + projection assertions in `coordinates.test.js` + `layerRequest.test.js` — **609 tests green**, lint 0, build green, lazy chunks intact. **Verified live headless** (`gis-verify/coverage-picker-verify.mjs`, V71): panning north out of Houston flipped **HCFCD (State-Plane path) + H-GAC ETJ (Web-Mercator path)** to "No data in this area," 0 JS errors.

### B284 — Coverage-aware layer picker: relevance modes + nearby range `[Site Planner / GIS]` (feature) — depends on B283  *(arrived as "NEW-2" 2026-06-20; minted **B284**)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/busy-allen-ofgy9l`).** The Layers panel (`components/LayerPanel.jsx`) now consumes B283's coverage. A **"Relevance"** control — **Show all / Dim / Hide** (**Dim** is the default) — plus an adjustable **"nearby range"** slider (default **2.5 mi**, the buffer fed back into B283) decide how out-of-coverage layers are presented:
- **Dim:** out-of-coverage layers sink to the bottom of their group, grayed, with a **"No data in this area"** caption — still one-click toggleable.
- **Hide:** they collapse behind a **"Show N layers with no local data here"** toggle (reveal shows them dimmed).
- A layer that is currently **ON is never demoted** (you always see what you've enabled). The mode + radius are **shared across both the map-finder and planner panels and persisted** (`coverage.js` prefs with pub/sub, `planarfit:relevance:v1`), so a change in one panel reflects in the other live.
- **List ordering/visibility ONLY — never the rendered map** (the map is driven by `overlays` + `syncOverlayLayers`, untouched). `normalizeMode`/`normalizeRadius` clamp + default; unit-tested. **Verified live** (V71): the control + slider render, Dim is default, and the dim/"No data in this area" treatment fires on a real pan out of region.

### B286 — Mapillary layer was inert — gated clearly as "needs setup" + excluded from the default set `[Site Planner / GIS]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-4" 2026-06-20; minted **B286**)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/busy-allen-ofgy9l`).** The layer fired zero requests + showed a red "failed"-style "Add a Mapillary token" message as shipped — it never worked. **Chose option (b): keep it, but gate it honestly** (not (a) bake a token — that violates the secrets rule and ships a shared rate-limited key; not (c) remove — its detections can be richer/fresher than OSM later, and the owner can have it gone with one word). ### B287 — Retry/backoff for transient 5xx on jurisdiction VECTOR services (City ETJ, County boundaries) `[Site Planner / GIS]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-5" 2026-06-20; minted **B287**)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/busy-allen-ofgy9l`).** Live 2026-06-20 the City ETJ (H-GAC FeatureServer) and County-boundaries (TxDOT/AGOL) layers threw intermittent **503s on their geojson queries**. **Deduped against the existing retry/backoff** and found the gap: raster tiles already retry via `withTileRetry` and the `?f=json` metadata probe via `fetchWithRetry`, but **esri-leaflet's FeatureLayer issues its own GeoJSON query with no retry** — so one transient blip dropped the whole vector layer to "failed." New **`attachFeatureRetry`** (`layers.js`) wires a pure **`featureRetryDecision`** policy (`layerRequest.js`) onto every `esriFeature` layer: on a `requesterror` it re-issues via `refresh()` with **exponential backoff** (400→800→1600 ms), holds the dot at "loading" while retrying, reports "failed" **only after `max` retries**, and resets on a successful `load`; a **hard 4xx is permanent** (no retry). The transient set (`429, 500, 502, 503, 504`) is now **one shared constant** (`TRANSIENT_STATUS`) across raster/metadata/vector. **9 unit tests** (`layerRequest.test.js`); lint 0 · 609 tests · build green.

### B279 — Production error telemetry → Supabase table `[Infra / Telemetry]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2" 2026-06-20 owner chat; filed **B279** in the B278–B281 Infra tranche — jumped past B271–B277 consumed by concurrent `main` + PR #217; batch comment lives in BACKLOG.md)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/trusting-hawking-1c4d6g`).** The app now self-reports runtime errors so silent production failures stop being invisible until someone stumbles on them. New **`src/shared/telemetry/clientErrors.js`**: three global sources — window `error`, window `unhandledrejection`, and Vite's `vite:preloadError` — plus the React **ErrorBoundary** (`componentDidCatch`) all funnel into one fire-and-forget sink that inserts a row into a new **`public.client_errors`** table via the EXISTING anon Supabase client (the "Supabase table, not Sentry" decision — no new vendor, no new keys). Installed in `main.jsx` before render; the Shell tags each row with the active workspace (`setTelemetryModule`).
- **Session-optional + no read hole (RLS):** `src/shared/telemetry/client_errors.sql` makes the table **INSERT-only** for `anon` + `authenticated` (no SELECT/UPDATE/DELETE policy), so an error **during login — before any session exists — still records**, and clients can write but can never read the table back (admins read via the dashboard / service role). `user_id` defaults to `auth.uid()` (null when anonymous); `WITH CHECK (user_id is null or user_id = auth.uid())` blocks forging another user's id. **Run the SQL once in the Supabase SQL editor** (idempotent; same pattern as `doc_reviews.sql`).
- **Fail-safe + storm guard:** every path swallows its own errors and never rethrows into the app (telemetry that throws is worse than none). `decideReport` (pure, unit-tested) suppresses an exact-duplicate signature within 10 s and caps sends to 20/min, so a render-loop error storm becomes a handful of rows, not thousands. Messages/stacks truncated (2 k / 8 k). NOT capture-phase, so blocked tiles / broken images don't spam it.
- **Build provenance:** `vite.config.js` bakes the short git SHA into the bundle (`__BUILD_ID__` define, read via a typeof guard → "dev" under dev/test) and stamps it on every row, so a report traces back to the exact deploy.
- **Dedup (the filing's own correction held):** the `vite:preloadError` listener it "pairs with" already existed and shipped (**B221** `installChunkReloadGuard`, `src/app/chunkReload.js`); this **adds** a telemetry write for that event through its OWN listener (chunkReload.js left untouched + pure). NET-NEW otherwise — no prior telemetry / Sentry item in either file.
- **Verification:** lint **0 errors** (only the pre-existing `SitePlanner.jsx`/`MapFinder.jsx` warnings); **587 tests** (12 new in `test/clientErrors.test.js` — storm-guard dup/rate/window, row shaping, message/stack extraction + truncation, signature); `npm run build` green, all three workspace lazy chunks intact, `__BUILD_ID__` fully replaced (no leftover token). **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-telemetry.mjs`, **6/6** on the built bundle via `vite preview`, re-run clean after merging the latest `main`): all three global sources captured with the correct `source` tag, a duplicate suppressed, build id baked in, and the page stays alive after firing synthetic errors (fail-safe). The live **cloud insert** (signed-in, after the one-time SQL) is the one auth-only path the sandbox can't exercise logged-out → logged in **VERIFICATION V69**.
> Independent of the B278 (Playwright) ID-collision concern; built + shipped this same session per the owner's "ship ship and then build whatever you need to." B278 / B280 / B281 stay Open (CI/secret-bound — see their `⛔ Verify-blocker` notes).

### B277 — Overlay visibility toggle (hide without deleting) `[Document Review / Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-4" 2026-06-20; minted **B277** — concurrent `main` consumed B270–B273 while this was in flight; batch B274–B277)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/peaceful-ride-k41y6e`).** Added a per-overlay eye / eye-slash toggle to the Site-plan overlay panel (`SitePlanner.jsx`) so a placed overlay can be switched OFF the map without deleting it — the standard layers-UI affordance (Bluebeam/ArcGIS/Photoshop). Distinct from B272's delete (hide ≠ delete): a hidden overlay stays in the panel, listed + recoverable.
- **Render:** the canvas overlay map skips an overlay with `visible === false` (returns null) — off the map, still in the panel with the eye-slash to bring it back. **Persistence:** `visible` rides in the overlay record (saved + cloud-slimmed + content-merged like every other overlay field), so a hidden overlay stays hidden across reload (and, signed in, across devices); it's also folded into the undo/redo signature so a hide/show is undoable.
- **Data shape was already reserved (B131):** `isOverlayPrintable = o.src && o.visible !== false` was shipped "forward-compatible with a future per-overlay hide," so hiding an overlay **also drops it from Print/PNG export automatically** (WYSIWYG) — no extra wiring. Inline `EyeIcon`/`EyeOffIcon` SVGs render crisply everywhere.
- **Verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-overlay-delete-hide.mjs`, the built app, logged-out): hide removes the overlay from the map but KEEPS it listed; the hidden state PERSISTS across reload (the record carries `visible:false`); show brings it back. lint 0 · 549 tests · build green; `SitePlannerApp`/`DocReview` lazy chunks intact.
> **Dedup:** B131 (print-overlay master toggle) reserved the `visible` semantics; this implements the per-overlay UI toggle it anticipated. Pairs with B276 (delete persistence) — same overlay surface, shipped together. (B314/B313, the data-integrity pair from the same batch, shipped this session too.)

### B276 — Overlay delete doesn't persist across reload `[Document Review / Site Planner]` (bug)  *(owner-reported 2026-06-20, "Jacinto Port"; arrived as "NEW-3"; minted **B276** — concurrent `main` consumed B270–B273; batch B274–B277)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/peaceful-ride-k41y6e`).** Deleting a placed overlay (the owner's "Jacinto Port" sheet) made it vanish, but it RETURNED on reload. **Root cause (as the backlog predicted):** the cross-copy reconciler `mergeSiteContent` (`siteModel.js`) **unions `sheetOverlays` by id**, so when the post-delete local copy (overlay gone) is merged with a copy that still has it — the cloud copy on the next `pullCloud`/`mergePulledSites`, or another tab via the `storage` fold — the deleted overlay is **resurrected**. Exactly the documented B126 union-merge trade-off ("a delete in only one copy can reappear once — per-item tombstones are the fully-correct future hardening"); `removeOverlay` only dropped it from local state, nothing recorded that the deletion was deliberate.
- **Fix — per-item tombstones (`deletedIds`), the B126 hardening, now built:** an additive Site Model field (`SITE_MODEL_VERSION` 5→6) holding ids the user deliberately deleted. `mergeSiteContent` unions the `deletedIds` from BOTH copies and **drops any tombstoned id from every unioned collection**, so a deletion wins over presence in either copy — across reload, tab-sync, and device-sync. `removeOverlay` records the tombstone; it's threaded through the save effect, the live/undo refs, the cross-tab `storage` fold, `applySnapshot`, and version-restore so it persists and undo correctly resurrects (the tombstone rolls back with the overlay). Bounded + deduped (≤5000 ids).
- **General but scoped:** the mechanism works for any collection (a tombstoned building stays deleted too) but is wired only at the overlay delete site for now; other delete handlers can adopt `setDeletedIds` trivially. **No regression:** collections not yet recording a tombstone keep the existing recoverable union behavior; `slimForCloud`/`slimForHistory` pass `deletedIds` through untouched (only inline rasters are stripped). **Composes with B297** (optimistic concurrency, shipped this session): a delete already rides the normal save, so it'll advance B297's version like any edit.
- **Verified:** unit — `test/storage.test.js` (6 new B276 cases: tombstone in either copy wins, set-union, no-regression on non-tombstoned items, generalizes to a building, end-to-end through `mergePulledSites`). Headless — `ui-audit/verify-overlay-delete-hide.mjs` (built app, logged-out): delete persists across reload and the record carries the `deletedIds` tombstone. lint 0 · **549 tests** · build green; lazy chunks intact.
> **Dedup:** net-new bug; the fix is the per-item tombstone B126 explicitly deferred. Distinct from B260 (overlay *scale* misread, done). Pairs with B277 (visibility), shipped together.
### B313 — Multi-tab open warning (same project open in another browser tab) `[App Shell]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2" 2026-06-20; minted **B313** — renumbered B275→B298→B313 as a very hot `main` reached B311; pairs with B314 + the already-live B276/B277)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/peaceful-ride-k41y6e`).** A non-blocking header banner now warns when the SAME project is open in another tab of the same browser — "This project is open in another tab. Editing it in more than one tab can conflict — work in a single tab to be safe." — so a two-tab clash isn't a surprise. Same-browser only; cross-DEVICE conflicts are B314's server guard.
- **How:** `src/shared/presence/multiTab.js` — a BroadcastChannel (same-origin cross-tab bus) presence tracker. Each tab announces its open project (`hello`/`here`/`update`/`bye` + a heartbeat); a pure `summarizePresence` reduces the live peer set into the banner state (conflict only when another tab is on the *same* project; stale peers pruned by TTL). Wired into the shared `AppHeader` via a `useMultiTab(projectId)` hook (BOTH workspaces get it); the banner clears the moment the other tab closes/navigates (its `bye`, or the TTL). Degrades to a silent no-op where BroadcastChannel is unavailable.
- **Verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-multitab.mjs`, 4/4, the built app, two real tabs in one browser context): Tab A alone shows nothing; opening Tab B on the same project raises the banner in BOTH; closing Tab B clears A's banner. Plus **10 unit tests** (`test/multiTab.test.js`) incl. a real two-instance BroadcastChannel round-trip (same-project → conflict; different project → present-but-no-conflict; clears on leave). lint 0 · build green; lazy chunks intact.
> **Dedup:** the VISIBLE companion to B127 (which made two same-browser tabs silently *converge*) — surfaces the situation, doesn't replace the merge. **Optional, deliberately not built:** the Web Locks single-active-editor *lock* (non-leader tabs go read-only) — the spec marked it optional; the banner is the required warning, the read-only lockout is an invasive follow-up. Pairs with B314 (the cross-device half).

### B314 — Reject stale saves (optimistic concurrency on the save path) `[Platform / Persistence]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1" 2026-06-20; minted **B314** — renumbered B274→B297→B314 as a very hot `main` reached B311; pairs with B313)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/peaceful-ride-k41y6e`); migration RUN by owner 2026-06-20 → goes ACTIVE on deploy.** Two sessions editing the same project no longer silently last-write-wins: a save carries the `version` it last synced, and the DB applies it ONLY if the stored version still matches (a single atomic conditional UPDATE), bumping it. A stale write (another session advanced the row) is **REJECTED as a conflict**, not applied — the Site Planner shows a loud blue "this project was changed in another session — reload before saving" banner with a **Reload** button. No silent clobber; work is never lost (the edit is saved on-device, and the reload union-merges it via mergeSiteContent, then re-pushes the combined result).
- **Reusable primitive (foundation for the deferred multi-user feature):** `src/shared/cloud/optimisticUpsert.js` — a pure `casUpsert` compare-and-swap over `(user_id, id, version)`, used by BOTH `public.sites` (cloudSync.js) and `public.doc_reviews` (reviewStore.js). Version tokens are tracked per-tab in the cloud layer (populated on list/load, advanced on each write, cleared on delete / user-switch), so a conflict propagates back as a typed `{ conflict:true }` the UI turns into the reload prompt. Doc Review surfaces it on its save badge (the persistence hook gains a `conflict` state).
- **Graceful degradation = merge-safe:** before the migration ran, the conditional write returned "column version does not exist" and the client fell back to a plain upsert (today's EXACT behaviour) — so saving never regressed; the guard was simply dormant. (The detector requires the error name the *version* column, so doc_reviews' optional library columns can't be mistaken for it and wrongly disable the guard.)
- **Verified:** **16 unit tests** (`test/cloudConcurrency.test.js`) cover the whole matrix — conflict (0 rows), success (+version), degrade (un-migrated), brand-new insert, unique-violation→conflict, never-throws, and the not-the-version-column guard. The live cloud conflict path needs sign-in (the sandbox blocks auth logged-out), so it's logged for a signed-in click-through (VERIFICATION V79). lint 0 · build green; lazy chunks intact.
> **✅ MIGRATION RUN (owner, 2026-06-20):** `src/workspaces/site-planner/db/optimistic_concurrency.sql` was run in the Supabase SQL editor (added the `version` column to `sites` + `doc_reviews`). The guard goes ACTIVE on this deploy. Composes with B276's tombstones (a delete advances the version like any write).

### B271 — Canvas could get stuck unclickable behind a frozen grab/hand cursor when a pointer gesture was interrupted `[Core / Site Planner + Doc Review]` (bug)  *(owner-reported 2026-06-20 via chat, with a screenshot of the "Claude is debugging this browser" banner; arrived as "NEW-1"; minted **B271** — real next free ID after concurrent `main` consumed B270)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/gifted-lamport-miamoc`).** Owner hit a state where the whole app went unclickable — a hand cursor over everything, clicks doing nothing — while every other website kept working. It coincided with a browser devtools/remote-debugger session attaching to the tab (the on-screen "Claude is debugging this browser" banner), but the fragility is **ours**: Planyr was the only page that locked up, so a latent bug in our pointer handling is the real cause (the attachment merely exposed it).
- **Root cause.** The planner canvas (`SitePlanner.jsx`) starts a pan/drag by capturing the pointer (`setPointerCapture`) and setting `panning` + `drag.current`, and relied **only** on `onPointerUp` (`onUp`) to release capture and clear that state. But the browser fires **`pointercancel`** (not `pointerup`) when a gesture is interrupted — a devtools/remote-debugger session attaching, an OS gesture takeover, or the window losing focus mid-drag — and the canvas had **no `onPointerCancel` handler and no blur/visibility recovery**. So the cleanup never ran: `panning` stayed `true` (cursor stuck on the select-mode grab/grabbing hand) with pointer-capture still held → the canvas swallowed every click. Other sites don't hold global pan/drag state, which is exactly why only Planyr broke. The same capture-pan pattern (same latent lockup) existed in the Doc Review **Stitcher** and the **ParcelDrawing** canvas.
- **Fix — four independent recovery paths where there were zero** (`SitePlanner.jsx`, `doc-review/Stitcher.jsx`, `site-planner/components/ParcelDrawing.jsx`):
  1. **`onPointerCancel` on each canvas** → an `abortGesture()` that releases pointer-capture (via `e.pointerId`) and clears `drag.current` / `panning` / the in-progress marquee + draw drafts (it **aborts**, never commits a half-finished gesture).
  2. **Window `blur` + `visibilitychange`(hidden) recovery** → same teardown, **plus** it drops the Space hold-to-pan flag (`spaceRef`/`spacePan`) so a missed Space key-up can't leave the hand cursor on. Mirrors the existing Shift-reset-on-blur effect.
  3. **Escape** now also tears the gesture down (release capture + clear `drag`/`panning`/`spacePan`) — a manual safety hatch on top of the draft/menu reset it already did.
  4. **`onBgDown`/`onUp` bookkeeping** — record the captured pointer id (`capturePidRef`) so blur/Escape can release a capture they didn't see start, cleared on normal release.
- **Verified — lint 0 · 543 tests · build green; lazy chunks (`SitePlannerApp`/`DocReview`) intact.** New headless test `ui-audit/verify-pointer-recover.mjs` drives a **real** pointer on the **built** app: a pan shows `grabbing`; **window blur** mid-pan recovers the cursor to `grab`; a **`pointercancel`** mid-pan recovers to `grab`; the canvas is still interactive afterward (a fresh pan re-engages); no uncaught errors. Before the fix, both interruptions left `grabbing` stuck (the lockup).
- **Dedup:** folds into the established pointer-capture discipline already in `onUp` (`setPointerCapture`/`releasePointerCapture`), not a parallel mechanism. The "ghost portal overlay" hypothesis was investigated and **disproved** as the cause: the full-canvas inline-editor catchers (`numEdit`/`editCallout`) already commit-and-clear on pointerdown and are bounded by their own state — the stuck pointer-capture / stuck-pan path is what produced the lockout. Secondary "main-thread stall" hypothesis tracked separately as **B272** (investigated; no actionable bug; low priority).

     processing queue). That base "NEW-1" was filed in the OTHER chat and is blind to this file — it was
     nowhere in this repo's history (grep across all refs: no "processing queue"/"persistent drop

     ("items pasted from another chat are blind... assign the real next B#") I minted it. It first took

     free ID **B270** (highest B# across both files is now B269). The owner's instruction was to fold
     Amendments A & B into NEW-1's spec when assigning its B# — done below: the B270 entry IS the

### B270 — Project Files: persistent drop-zone + processing queue (multi-file ingestion + persistent upload tray) `[Site Planner / Document Review — Project Files]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1" from a parallel chat — only Amendments A & B reached this session; minted **B270**, the real next free ID after concurrent `main` consumed B246–B269)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/quirky-bardeen-xje4nv`).** Turned the Project Files drop zone (the shared `ProjectFilesDrawer`, opened from Row 1 across workspaces) from a one-file-at-a-time loop that reported errors through a `window.alert` (a KEY-DECISION violation) into a **persistent processing queue with an upload tray**. Pure, browser-free model + derived view in **`src/shared/files/uploadQueue.js`** (`QUEUE_STATUS`, `makeQueueItem`/`makeQueueItems`, `splitQueue` (the derived two-group view), `hasPendingDemote`, `runPool` (concurrency pool), `isAcceptedFile`; **12 unit tests**, `test/uploadQueue.test.js`). UI wiring in `ProjectFilesDrawer.jsx` (`UploadTray` + `QueueRow` + the ingest/pipeline/demote logic); demote slide/fade in `index.css`.
- **Folded spec — Amendment A (multi-file ingestion is first-class).** Drop, the native file picker (`multiple`), AND clipboard paste all funnel through one `ingest()` that iterates the file list and creates **one independent queue item per file**, each with its own `uploadId`, run through a small **concurrency pool** (3 at a time) — so dropping 8 files yields **8 independent concurrent rows**, not one batch row and not a serialized chain. **Mixed types in one action:** PDFs enter the pipeline; unsupported types get a clear **per-file rejection row** (`rejected`, with a Dismiss ×) — never silently discarded.
- **Folded spec — Amendment B (persistent tray, not a vanishing toast).** Filed items do not disappear from under the user. On success a row goes to a calm muted **`done`** state (green check, reduced weight); after a ~3s confirmation beat it **demotes** from the active **PROCESSING** group into a collapsible **"Recently filed · N"** group via a subtle slide/fade — never an abrupt removal. The trail **collapses by default once it has more than ~3 entries** and has a **Clear** affordance. `needs_filing` (filed but unrouted — a **Triage** button jumps to the holding area's one-click confirm) and `failed` (a **Retry** button) **never auto-dismiss** — they stay in the active group until the user acts. **Net:** active group = in-flight + exceptions (live to-do); recently-filed = an auditable, clearable trail. The two groups are a **derived view over one queue array** (filter by status + a `filedAt` timestamp), not two lists — the demote is a status/timestamp transition, exactly as the implementation note specified.
- **Graceful degrade kept:** an oversize (>50 MB) or upload-failed file still files the work layer and the row carries a non-fatal "re-drop on open to view" warn (it is `done`, not `failed`); a Drive-copy failure is a soft warn too. "Drive not enabled yet" stays silent (B207 best-effort).
- **Verification:** lint clean on the changed files (the 13 repo warnings are all pre-existing in `SitePlanner.jsx`); **549 tests** (537 + 12) green; `npm run build` green; the doc-review/`ProjectFilesDrawer` lazy chunk split still holds (28 kB chunk). Real-browser headless: (a) the existing `verify-files-refile.mjs` still PASSes (drawer mounts, **0 JS errors** — the new imports/components load), and (b) drove a **mixed 3-file pick** through the real component → **"PROCESSING · 3"**, two PDF rows + one **"Not a PDF" rejection row** with Dismiss, Retry buttons, **no `window.alert`** (screenshot captured). The `done`→Recently-filed demote / >3 collapse / Clear need a *successful* cloud filing (= sign-in, which the sandbox blocks logged-out) — that path is unit-tested (`splitQueue`/`hasPendingDemote`/`RECENT_COLLAPSE_AT`) and logged for a signed-in click-through in VERIFICATION (**V66**).
> **Dedup — build on what's shipped, don't fork:** this upgrades **B180**'s drop zone (the saved-views drawer) and reuses **B217**'s "needs filing" holding area + one-click confirm (Triage routes there — no second filing UI). **Auto-file-by-title-block** (read title block → match a project → auto-route/auto-name; low-confidence → holding area) is **NOT** this item — it stays the **backend tranche** (B180 ⏳ + the auto-filing roadmap item), stubbed behind `createIndexProvider`; B270 is the browser-only ingestion/queue surface it will feed. Filing still files under the active project (or the holding area) until that lands.

### B265 — Doc Review (Markup) PDF render is blurry — honour devicePixelRatio `[Doc Review / Markup]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-2" 2026-06-20; renumbered **B265** as concurrent `main` consumed B246–B264; batch B265–B269, the other four filed Open: B266/B267/B268/B269)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/friendly-euler-hw8v1t`, PR #205).** Sheets in Markup rendered soft/illegible — note text unreadable at fit-to-page, only marginally better zoomed — because `renderPageToCanvas` (`src/workspaces/doc-review/lib/pdf.js`) sized the canvas backing store to `(scale × base)` with **no devicePixelRatio factor** and gave the canvas no explicit CSS size, so on a HiDPI/Retina display the browser **upscaled a 1×-density bitmap** to fill 2× physical pixels = blur. (Same HiDPI class as the Site Planner's B169/B170 basemap fix — different surface: the PDF.js canvas, not Leaflet tiles.)
- **Fix:** the page now renders the backing store at `scale × dpr` (`dpr = min(window.devicePixelRatio, 2)`) while the canvas's **on-screen (CSS) size stays at the logical `scale×` size** (`canvas.style.width/height`), so the dense bitmap is sampled down → crisp text. A new `backingScale()` caps the backing store to a **~24 MP budget** (drops dpr toward 1× on a huge E-size sheet at deep zoom) so the denser render can't OOM, and **never goes below 1×** (never worse than before). Zoom already re-renders at the new scale (true re-rasterization); this makes every render dpr-aware.
- **Overlay geometry unchanged by construction:** `renderPageToCanvas` still returns `dims.w/h = floor(base × scale)` — byte-identical to before — and that's what both the wrapper box and the markup SVG overlay bind to, so measurements/markups land exactly where they did.
- **Verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-new2-dpr.mjs`, the REAL built viewer driven at two pixel densities with a generated 1-page PDF): at **deviceScaleFactor 2** the backing store is **2.000×** the CSS size (1054→2108 px) = crisp; at **deviceScaleFactor 1** it's **1.000×** (unchanged); the **on-screen size is identical across both densities** (1054×1364) → overlay geometry provably unaffected. lint 0 · 543 tests · build green; DocReview + pdf lazy chunks intact. The crispness *gain* only manifests on real HiDPI hardware (headless DPR-forcing proves the 2× mechanism); logged for a live retina eyeball as **VERIFICATION V65**.
> **Dedup:** net-new for the Doc Review canvas — **B169/B170** (basemap HiDPI/retina) and the map-finder over-zoom fixes are the *Site Planner basemap-tile* siblings of the same principle, not this surface. The Stitcher's `renderPageToImage` is a separate path (fixed 2× + a placed-image transform), intentionally left as-is. Filed alongside **B266/B267/B268/B269** (sheet labels, auto-calibrate, scale cross-check, sample-fixture cleanup) which stay Open — this was the cleanly-fixable, verifiable one of the batch.

### B260 — Dropped site-plan overlay placed 10–30× too large when its printed scale is misread → the drawing's title block blankets the map ("file name all over the map") `[Site Planner / overlay]` (bug)  *(owner-reported 2026-06-20 with a screenshot of "Jacinto"; arrived as "NEW-1"; minted **B260** — concurrent `main` took B246 (dock-zone build-out, PR #204) and B247–B259 (Scheduler backlog) while this was in flight, so B260 is the real next free ID after B259)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/sweet-wozniak-txzr3e`).** Owner dropped a landscape drawing onto the planner and a huge rotated string — the sheet's title block, ~`BV-255-2024-LD1 … ARCH ASSET FOR …` — covered nearly the whole aerial; only the parcel (`26.33 ac`) looked right.
- **Diagnosis (corrected the hand-off's guess).** It is **NOT** a world-scaled *text label*: every label path in the planner is screen-space or px-capped — element labels `11·ls`, parcel acreage chip `12·ls`, callouts are boxed + capped at their own `size`, all markup/measure labels are fixed px, and the overlay's name **placeholder** is a hard-coded `fontSize={13}` (confirmed in a headless seed: the placeholder text stays 13 px even when its dashed rect is huge). The giant string is the rasterized overlay **IMAGE** itself. `addOverlayFile` auto-applied a scale note read off the sheet (the B73 `trueScale` path → `ftPerPointForScale(detectedScale)`) with **no sanity check on the resulting size**. A landscape sheet commonly prints a **vicinity / key-map scale** (e.g. 1″=600′) next to the plan scale (e.g. 1″=30′), and `parseScaleNote` returns the **first in-range match**, so the vicinity scale can win → `ftPerPx` 10–30× too big → `imgW·ftPerPx·ppf` renders the sheet (and its title block) enormous, spilling far past the viewport. (The drawing's white paper is knocked to transparent, so on a dark aerial the only thing that reads is the dark title-block text — which is why it looks like "just the file name, splattered.") **Reproduced headless:** a seeded overlay at the misread 1″=600′ rendered **14279×9519 px** on a 1440×900 view.
- **Fix 1 — guard the auto-scale (root cause).** New pure, browser-free `chooseOverlayScale()` in `lib/overlayScale.js`: trust the read scale **only** when it lands the sheet at a sane on-screen size (**≤4× / ≥0.04× the viewport width**); otherwise fall back to the existing "size to fit" (~60% of the view) and report a `too-big`/`too-small` reason. The read scale is **still stored** on the overlay, so the panel's "Read from sheet: 1″=X′ **[Apply]**" still offers it as a one-click when the user wants it. `addOverlayFile` now routes through it and, on a rejected scale, flashes an **honest, actionable** note ("…its printed scale would place it far too large — sized it to fit instead; set the exact scale or 'Trace a length' in the Site-plan overlay panel"). No silent mis-place.
- **Fix 2 — one-click rescue.** New **"Size to view"** button in the Site-plan overlay panel: resizes the selected overlay to ~60% of the current view and recenters it — recovery for an already-splattered overlay (the owner's existing "Jacinto" file) or any manual scale slip. Distinct from "Fit view" (which zooms the canvas), with tooltips on both to disambiguate.
- **Verified — lint 0 · 538 tests · build green; lazy-chunk split intact.** `chooseOverlayScale` has **7 new unit tests** (`test/overlayScale.test.js`: trusts a correct 1″=30′, rejects a misread 1″=600′ as too-big, rejects a deep-zoom tiny render as too-small, falls back with no/non-standard scale, the fit fallback ≈ 60% of the view, NaN/zero-divide defense). Headless on the **built** app (`ui-audit/verify-overlay-fix.mjs`): **(A)** dropping an image runs the real import path → overlay lands **535 px** wide on a 1440 px view (sane, not splattered); **(B)** a seeded splattered overlay (**14279 px**) shrinks to **535 px** with one "Size to view" click (before/after screenshots). **Honest gap:** PDF rasterization can't run in the sandbox Chromium (pdf.js `getOrInsertComputed` is unsupported there), so the PDF scale-read path is covered by the unit tests + the image-path E2E rather than an end-to-end PDF drop — logged for a real-browser confirm as **VERIFICATION V63**.
- **Dedup:** distinct from **B148** (oversized world-space *summary banner* — a genuine screen-vs-world text bug) and builds on **B73** (the overlay scale tooling this hardens). The hand-off's "world-scaled label, scaled to the geometry's bounding box" hypothesis was investigated and **disproved** — no label path produces it; the cause is overlay-image scaling. The "Place on map" cascade (`shared/placement/placeOnMap.js`, B182) remains a stub (`onPlaceOnMap` only closes the drawer) and emits no label, so there is **no** second "auto-place emits a bogus label" item.

### B247 — Scheduler Export modal: Header/Cover fields drop focus after every keystroke `[Scheduler / UI]` (bug)  *(orig "B3/M4" in the owner's Planar backlog; provisionally B246, renumbered **B247** — concurrent `main` took B246 (dock-zone build-out, PR #204) while this was in flight, so B247 is the real next free ID after B246)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/zen-bohr-7xgk6q`).** In Export → "Header / Cover", typing in Exhibit / Title / Prep. by / Prep. for / Date / Conf. tag dropped focus after each character (one keystroke at a time). **Cause:** `Field` (and `Toggle`/`SegBtn`/`Row`) were defined *inside* `PDFExportModal`, so every render minted a new component identity → React unmounted the live `<input>` and mounted a fresh one, taking focus with it. **Fix:** hoisted `Field`/`Toggle`/`SegBtn`/`Row` to module scope (all props-only — no closure over modal state) above `PDFExportModal`; their JSX usages are unchanged (now resolve to the stable module-scope identity). `SHdr` was deliberately left inside the modal — it closes over `setSecOpen`/`secIsOpen`, so hoisting it would need prop-threading for zero user benefit (perf-only). **Verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-scheduler-bugfixes.mjs`, V62): typed "ALTA & Topo Survey — Phase 2" character-by-character into the Title field — full value intact, focus retained, 0 console errors.

### B248 — Scheduler "Export Report" (HTML) doesn't escape user strings `[Scheduler / export]` (bug)  *(orig "B6½")*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/zen-bohr-7xgk6q`).** The older `exportHTML` path still did raw template interpolation, so a task named "ALTA & Topo Survey" or "Budget > $1M" (or any `<`/`>`/`&` in name/owner) corrupted the downloaded HTML report. `buildPDFHtml`/`buildGanttSVG` already used the module `escapeHtml` helper; this was the last raw path. **Fix:** wrapped every interpolated user string in `exportHTML` — project name, task id, task name, start/end dates, the status label, and owner — in `escapeHtml(...)`. Numbers (duration, %) left as-is.

### B249 — Deleting a custom status crashes views that still reference it `[Scheduler / status]` (bug)  *(orig "B1")*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/zen-bohr-7xgk6q`).** Create a custom status → apply to tasks → delete it, and several views went blank (the % Done cell, the HTML export) because the deleted key was dereferenced as `HEALTH[t.health].dot` with no fallback. **Fix, two halves:** **(a) Reassign on delete** — `removeOption` now walks every project's tasks and sets `health: "gray"` ("Not Started") on any task still carrying the deleted key *before* filtering the status out (same `setData`), so no task is ever left pointing at a missing key. **(b) Defensive lookups** — guarded the two genuinely-unguarded sites with `(HEALTH[…] || HEALTH.gray)` (the `exportHTML` row and the % Done cell), matching the `|| HEALTH.gray` pattern already used in ~10 spots. The project-header lookup (`HEALTH[projHealth(cur)]`) was already safe — `projHealth` only ever returns base keys.

### B250 — JSON import skips the normalization/migration pipeline `[Scheduler / import]` (bug)  *(orig "B4")*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/zen-bohr-7xgk6q`).** `importJSON` did `setData(parsed)` raw, skipping the migration the cloud/seed **load** path runs — so an old or partial backup could load with predecessors in the old shape, missing settings, and un-cascaded dates. **Fix:** route the import through the *same* pipeline as load: `ensureContacts(normalizeIds(ensureHolidays(normalizeToV6(parsed))))`, then rebuild `HOLIDAY_SET` and run `cascadeDates → rollupParentDates` per project (mirrors the seed-load branch exactly). The pre-import `pre-import` snapshot is preserved. A current backup re-imports byte-identically (the migrations are idempotent); an old/partial one loads cleanly with defaults filled in.

### B251 — New/renamed custom status renders one beat late `[Scheduler / status]` (bug)  *(orig "B5/M3")*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/zen-bohr-7xgk6q`).** Adding or renaming a custom status often didn't show in pickers until you clicked around. **Cause:** `HEALTH`/`HK`/`HDARK` are module-level mutable globals rebuilt by `rebuildHEALTH(...)` inside the `[data]` effect; the rebuild mutates the globals but doesn't itself re-render, so the render that processed the change read stale values. **Fix (the low-risk option A):** track a `prevHealthKey` ref of the serialized `customHealth`+`healthLabelOverrides`; after `rebuildHEALTH`, when that key actually changes, bump a small `setHealthTick` once to force a re-render that re-reads the fresh globals. Keyed so it fires only on real status-config changes, and loop-safe (the tick isn't a `[data]` dependency, so it can't re-trigger the effect) — mirrors the existing holiday-recascade guard in the same effect. **Verified headless** (V62): boots clean, no "Maximum update depth" loop, 0 console errors.

### B252 — Undo history holds 50 full board snapshots `[Scheduler / perf]` (task)  *(orig "P3")*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/zen-bohr-7xgk6q`).** Every edit pushed a full deep copy of `data` onto the undo stack, capped at 50 (~50× the board's JSON held in memory). **Fix:** lowered the cap to 20 (`slice(-19)`) — undo still works through many steps, memory footprint cut ~60%. (The bigger "snapshot only the active project / store inverse diffs" options stay deferred under B256/roadmap; not needed yet.)

### B253 — "Today" stays fresh across midnight / tab-left-open `[Scheduler / dates]` (bug) — already resolved  *(orig "B7")*
`[x]` **Already done in current code; verified 2026-06-20, no change needed.** The owner's doc predated the fix. `NOW` is now a live module value refreshed on `focus`, `visibilitychange`, and a 60s `setInterval`, each bumping a `todayTick` that forces the re-render that re-reads it; `computeDisplayHealth` (overdue/due-soon) and the Gantt "today" line read `NOW`; `NotesModal` stamps `toShortDate(NOW)` / `parseFlexDate(dateStr) || NOW` at open time. So the today line, overdue colouring, and new-note date all roll over without a reload. Filed for the record so the old finding is closed.

### B254 — Split-view Snap/Free chip lingers ~5s after releasing the divider `[Scheduler / UI]` (bug?) — resolved as won't-change  *(orig "B9"; minted **B254**)*
`[x]` **Resolved 2026-06-20 (no code change — owner decision).** The owner's doc suspected the `setTimeout(() => setDragging(false), 5000)` (public/sequence/index.html) was a 500ms typo. **Inspected first:** the chip is an *interactive* Snap/Free toggle (fixed portal, top-right); the ~5s keeps it clickable after a drag so you can flip snap mode for the next drag without re-grabbing the divider — i.e. the delay serves a real purpose, not an obvious typo. Raised it to Michael; he said **"don't worry about the chip thing"** → leave the 5s as-is. Closed so it isn't re-raised. No change shipped.

### B261 — Add an explicit "Group" tool (Bluebeam-style, no content lock) `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1" 2026-06-20; minted **B261** — highest B# across both files was B246, so B261–B264 are the real next free IDs)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/eager-keller-1ueisx`).** A deliberate Group replaces the old implicit drag-to-bond. A persistent group = a shared **`groupId`** on ≥2 els/markups (additive Site-Model field; rides `els`/`markups` losslessly, no migration). It is DISTINCT from the temporary multi-selection (marquee / Shift-click; evaporates on the next click) AND from the building-host **`attachedTo`** assembly (a rigid child→host bind with resize-refit).
- **Commands:** select ≥2 → **Group** (toolbar **⊞ Group**, the element context menu's "Group selection (N)", or **Ctrl+G**) stamps a fresh `groupId`. **Ungroup** via toolbar **⊟**, context menu, or **Ctrl+⇧G**. **Duplicate group** (Ctrl+D on a group, or context "Duplicate group") clones every member + each member's attached children with remapped ids and a fresh shared `groupId`; a LONE paste/duplicate strips `groupId` (added to `ORPHAN_TAGS`) so a single copy starts standalone.
- **Grouping means "they stay together," nothing more** (owner clarification 2026-06-20): a single click on any member selects the WHOLE group, and move / copy / delete / arrow-nudge then act on all of them — basically how a building + its attached features already travel together, extended to arbitrary peers (e.g. a road + an easement). A dashed enclosing box labelled "⊞ Group" marks it as one unit. **There is deliberately NO whole-group resize** — scaling everything at once "isn't how you plan buildings" (site elements are real feet). To resize a piece, drill into it (below). (An earlier build added uniform group-resize handles; removed per the owner — `startGroupResize`/`scaleMarkup` deleted, the box is now a pure indicator.)
- **No content lock:** double-click a member to "drill in" (`drillId`) and edit it in place (resize / retype / restyle) WITHOUT ungrouping; right-click still opens the actions menu; members keep their own properties. Grouping happens ONLY from the explicit command — never from a plain drag or click.
> **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-b261-b264.mjs`): group two elements → "⊞ Group" box renders with **no resize handles** → dragging one member moves **both** (108px each) → Ungroup removes the box → members move independently again; **0 page errors**. lint **0 errors** · **537 tests** · build green; `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact. Logged **VERIFICATION V64**.
> **Dedup:** no prior open Group item. Supersedes the *bonding* half of the B114 snap/bond work (the Shift-drag→`attachedTo` bond is removed — see **B262**). The owner-mentioned "earlier split-snap item" was the B114 family (already done), not a separate open item; the still-open **B115** (keyboard-shortcuts pass, owner-gated) listed the now-removed ⇧-drag bond gesture — its shortcut table is updated here.

### B262 — Keep snap as pure alignment only (no relationship) `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2" 2026-06-20; minted **B262**)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/eager-keller-1ueisx`).** Removed the implicit drag-to-bond entirely: the Shift-drag → `alignSnap` → `attachedTo` path, the green "+" attach hint, and the bond-on-drop in `onUp` are gone, and the now-unused `alignSnap` / `flushContact` / `isAxisRect` helpers + `canAttach` / `bondTarget` / `bondRot` were deleted (net −2 lint warnings). Dragging an element now only MOVES it; with snap on, the ambient flush-snap (`edgeSnapCenter`) only ALIGNS position (grid + flush against neighbours, AutoCAD-style) and never creates a group or attachment. The building-host `attachedTo` assembly (docks / parking / sidewalks) and the explicit "Attach to…" command are unchanged.
> **Self-verified headless** (V64): with snap ON, dragging a building flush against a parking field then away leaves the parking untouched (Δ=0px — no bond).
> **Dedup:** pairs with **B261** (grouping moved to the explicit Group tool); narrows **B114** (the snap toggle + Alt-bypass stay; only the bond half is removed).

### B263 — Snap pref is silently global & sticky across sessions/projects `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-3" 2026-06-20; minted **B263**)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/eager-keller-1ueisx`).** Snap was persisted in `localStorage` (`planarfit:snap`) and re-applied on every load, so it could be ON without the user enabling it this session ("I never clicked snap"). It's now a **per-SESSION** pref: it defaults **OFF** every time the app opens, is remembered only within the current browser-tab session (`sessionStorage` — survives plan/project switches this session, resets on a fresh tab/session), and `loadSnapPref` retires the old global `localStorage` key on read. The toolbar pill makes state explicit (**"Snap off"** / **"Snap 10′ on"** with a green dot) and its tooltip clarifies snap only aligns position — it never groups or bonds (so with **B262** no group/bond-type move can fire from this flag).
> **Self-verified headless** (V64): a fresh session → button reads "Snap off" and no global `localStorage` key exists; toggling on writes `sessionStorage` only.

### B264 — No way to delete a single plan; only "delete site + all plans" `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-4" 2026-06-20; minted **B264**)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/eager-keller-1ueisx`).** Added a per-plan delete to the **Plan ▾** menu: each plan row carries a **✕** that arms an inline **"Delete '<name>'? Delete / Cancel"** confirm (no `window.confirm` — honours the no-dialog-edits rule). The **last** plan in a site never shows a ✕ (removing the whole site stays the map/finder's job). App-side `deletePlan` removes just that plan; if it was the plan currently open it switches to a sibling. A new `deletedSelfRef` suppresses EVERY save path for the plan being deleted (the debounced autosave, the leave/unmount `persistOrDrop`, the `beforeunload`/visibility flush, and `flushSite`) so the unmounting planner can't immediately re-write the row we just deleted.
> **Self-verified headless** (V64): a 2-plan site → ✕ shows the inline confirm → Delete removes one plan (the **current** plan was deleted → it switched to the sibling and did NOT resurrect) → the lone remaining plan has no ✕; **0 page errors**.

I can get the first row, but I should be able to get [more]… mimic how the dockside stuff is set up, but for the employee side. Also… when I press plus, I've lost my sidewalk." Wired to **both** the on-canvas non-dock "＋/−" pair (per side, with a live title: "Add a 5′ sidewalk" → "Add a parking row" → "Add another parking row") **and** the panel **Car parking** row (applies to every non-dock side).
