### B244 — Resilient county parcel fetch with TxGIO statewide fallback `[Site Planner / parcels]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1" 2026-06-20; minted **B244** — concurrent `main` took B239–B243 (Schedule stale-chunk hardening, brand icons, dock-zone fixes, PDF download) while this was in flight, so B244/B245 are the real next free IDs after B243)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/focused-darwin-8gkesb`).** When a county's own appraisal-district endpoint is down, parcel selection now degrades gracefully instead of hanging. Trigger was the 2026-06-19 FBCAD outage: `gis.fbcad.org/serverarcgis2` returned 503 then **total timeouts on every path** (layer, `/rest/services`, `/rest/info` — the whole ArcGIS server unresponsive), so a Fort Bend click **froze the tab ~45s** with no answerer. What shipped:
- **Hard timeout (the freeze fix).** `fetchJson` in `lib/arcgis.js` now wraps every county GIS request in an **`AbortController` with an 8 s cap** (`PARCEL_FETCH_TIMEOUT_MS`) — an indefinite hang becomes a prompt, typed `timeout` failure so the fallback can take over. Covers **every** parcel surface automatically (map click-select, address-search select, in-planner identify) since they all route through `fetchJson`/`queryAtPoint`.
- **Per-source circuit breaker.** New `lib/sourceHealth.js` (pure, injectable clock, **7 tests**): after **3 consecutive failures** a source's breaker **opens for a 5 min cooldown** (`recordSourceResult`/`isSourceOpen`/`sourceCooldownMs`), then auto-resumes (half-open) so a recovered server is picked back up without a reload. `filterHealthyCandidates` drops an open primary from the click's candidate list **but never the statewide source** — so we stop re-hammering a dead host while coverage always survives. A success resets the streak (a blip never trips it). Wired into `MapFinder.handleClick` + `selectParcelAt`: candidates are health-filtered before the query and `identifyParcelDetailed`'s new per-source outcomes feed the breaker.
- **Fallback chain (primary → TxGIO statewide).** B137 already appended the statewide TxGIO layer (`feature.geographic.texas.gov/.../stratmap_land_parcels_48_most_recent`) as a universal click candidate; this makes the chain *robust* (timeout + breaker above) and adds the **search-side** fallback: `lib/parcelQuery.js` `lookupParcels` tries the county's own CAD and, on a typed outage, retries the TxGIO layer **scoped to that one county**.
- **County-scoped statewide search.** `lib/counties.js` `statewideFallbackFor(county)` returns the TxGIO layer + `county='<NAME>'` scope (HARRIS / FORT BEND; Chambers already rides TxGIO so it has no separate backup). The shared, injection-safe `buildParcelWhere` (`parcelQuery.js`, **10 tests**, ports the B47 identifier guard) ANDs the scope **only when the layer actually has a `county` field** (self-healing for a pasted single-county URL) so an ID/address search can never match a like-named parcel in another county. Click-to-select is a point query and needs no scope.
- **Honest source labeling.** When a hit comes from the statewide layer while a real CAD existed for that spot, MapFinder now shows an amber **"Statewide backup source — <County> county's own parcel server is unavailable; … may lag county updates"** notice (a click banner + a badge in the address-search info card). The county name is read from the parcel's own `county` attribute (`findAttr(attrs, /^county$/i)`), title-cased.
- **Field mapping / normalization.** `lib/appraisal.js` `APPR_FIELDS` extended to cover TxGIO's column names (`legal_area`/`gis_area` → Acreage, `mkt_value` → Total value, `stat_land_use` → Land use, `year_built` → Year built) so a backup parcel surfaces the **same curated rows** as one from its home county (`test/appraisal.test.js`, **6 tests**). FBCAD's *native* field names can't be captured/mapped yet — its server is down — so that mapping is the one explicitly-deferred sliver (the generic detectors already read TxGIO's `prop_id`/`situs_addr`/`owner_name` fine).
- **Verified — lint 0 · 532 tests · build green; lazy-chunk split intact.** **Live headless run (`gis-verify/fbcad-outage-fallback-verify.mjs`):** with `gis.fbcad.org` intercepted as 503 (the real outage), a Sugar Land / Fort Bend click **selected the real TxGIO lot (prop_id 40594, county "FORT BEND") in 1.2 s** — HCAD answered empty, FBCAD's 503 never froze the click — and the **"Statewide backup source" notice rendered** (`gis-verify/fbcad-outage-fallback-verified.png`). Logged **VERIFICATION V61**; no owner action.
> **Dedup vs B137:** B137 made TxGIO a *queryable candidate* so a Fort Bend lot *can* be answered (coverage). B244 is the **resilience layer on top** — the timeout that stops the hang, the breaker that stops re-hammering, the honest backup labeling, the search-side county-scoped fallback, and the TxGIO field normalization. Also distinct from **B233** (which added the "source unavailable ≠ no-parcel-here" split — B244 *feeds* that split with typed failures, see B245) and **B36e** (AbortControllers on *evidence* fetches, a different, busy-gated path). **Note (honest):** the search-side fallback lives in the canonical `runLookup` seam, which the in-planner lookup panel doesn't currently mount (the live search is the map address box, a point query that's inherently single-parcel) — the mechanism is built + unit-tested at the seam so it's correct if/when that panel returns.

### B245 — Validate the ArcGIS response BODY, not just the HTTP status `[Site Planner / parcels]` (bug) — prereq for B244  *(arrived as "NEW-2" 2026-06-20; minted **B245** — next free ID after B244)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/focused-darwin-8gkesb`).** ArcGIS routinely returns **HTTP 200 with a JSON `{error:…}` body** (e.g. 499 Token Required) for a failed query; the old `fetchJson` did already throw on `j.error`, but it threw a *generic* `Error`, so a caller couldn't tell a **server failure** from a healthy **"no parcel at this point."** Now `lib/arcgis.js` throws a typed **`ParcelFetchError { kind, status, unavailable:true }`** classifying every failure — `timeout` (aborted), `http` (non-OK status), `arcgis` (200 + error body), `network` (fetch/CORS throw) — while a **healthy empty feature list still returns `null`, never an error** (no-parcel-here is a valid answer, not a failure). `identifyParcelDetailed` already separated `responded` vs `errors` for the B233 "unavailable vs none" card; it now also returns **per-source outcomes** (`sources:[{county, ok, hit, error}]`) so the B244 circuit breaker can mark exactly which source failed. `humanizeError` gives each `kind` its own plain wording. This is the prereq that makes B244's fallback trigger reliably (a 200-with-error-body now *counts* as a failure, not a masked success). **Tests:** `test/arcgis.test.js` extended (+7: empty→null, 200+error→`arcgis`/499, 503→`http`, network→`network`, the timeout-abort path via fake timers, per-source split, humanized wording). lint 0 · 532 tests · build green.
> **Dedup:** extends **B233** (typed "couldn't reach any service" vs "no parcel here") from the address-search card down into the fetch layer, and reuses the same body-parse principle the layer **`probeService`** (`lib/layers.js`) already applies (HTTP 200 + `.error` = failed) — now applied to the parcel **query** path and surfaced as a typed error. Folded into the B244 ship (one branch); kept as its own item because it's the reusable classification primitive every parcel surface now leans on.

### B243 — Replace browser print with a Planyr-composed PDF download (no print dialog, white background, exact page size) `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; minted B228, renumbered **B243** — concurrent `main` took B228–B242 (dock-zone stack, DWG service, map-finder search, brand icons, …) while this was in flight, so B243 is the real next free ID after B242)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/eloquent-mendel-jioa4q`).** Owner reported (3 screenshots) that **Print** opened a blank `about:blank` window and the output carried a browser date/time header (top-left), an `about:blank` URL (bottom-left), a `1/1` page number (bottom-right), a cream page background, and Letter-sized content floating in a corner of a Tabloid sheet. **Inspected first (as asked):** the path ALREADY did the hard part — `printPDF` composed the WHOLE sheet (title block + plan + B197 buildings table + metrics) as ONE SVG at the exact declared page size (B200) — and the ONLY defect was the final DELIVERY: `window.open("","_blank")` + `win.print()` handed that sheet to the **browser's** print dialog, which injects the header / `about:blank` / page number (none strippable by CSS or code), and the cream was `PAL.paper` (`#f4f1ea`, the on-screen page colour) bleeding into the sheet fill **and** the plan-clone background rect.
- **Fix = keep the composition, replace the delivery with a real PDF we build ourselves.** New pure, dependency-free writer `src/workspaces/site-planner/lib/imagePdf.js` (`jpegToPdf`): assembles a one-page PDF (catalog → pages → page → image XObject → content stream → Info) at an **exact physical size** (`MediaBox = inches × 72 pt`), embeds the page raster with `/DCTDecode` (the JPEG bytes verbatim, no re-encode), with a **byte-accurate xref** and binary-safe assembly (builds a `Uint8Array`; the JPEG never passes through a UTF-16 JS string). No jsPDF/pdf-lib — zero bundle weight, matching the `printSheet.js` pure-lib pattern; unit-tested in `test/imagePdf.test.js` (10 tests: xref offsets land on each object, MediaBox in points, DCTDecode dims, paren/backslash title escaping, bad-input guards).
- **`printPDF` → `exportPDF`** in `SitePlanner.jsx`: the old `window.open`/`win.print()` machinery is **gone**. It now forces **white** paper (new `paper` arg to `buildExportSvg` for the plan-clone bg + `pal:{…PAL,paper:'#ffffff'}` for the sheet — the two cream sources), inlines the aerial with `dropOnFail=true` so a CORS-blocked image can't taint the canvas (the vector plan still exports), rasterizes the composed sheet at **300 DPI** (`PDF_DPI`, capped by `PDF_MAX_PX = 22M` px — Tabloid@300 ≈ 16.8M, under the cap), fills the canvas white first (JPEG has no alpha), JPEG-encodes at q0.92, wraps with `jpegToPdf`, and **downloads** `"<date> <project> - <plan>.pdf"` (B201 naming). Generating the PDF ourselves is the mechanism that removes the injected chrome; the declared page size kills the Letter-on-Tabloid float. Raster (vs a vector SVG→PDF converter) is deliberate: the plan uses `feDropShadow` filters, which the browser renders faithfully into the raster but most SVG→PDF converters drop — full WYSIWYG fidelity over crisp-vector-text, and 300 DPI keeps text crisp for print anyway.
- **UI:** File ▾ item → **"Download PDF / pick frame…"**; the print-frame toolbar action → **"Download PDF"** (+ tooltip); a **"Preparing PDF…"** pill (new `exportingPDF` state + a `spin` keyframe in `index.css`) replaces the old blank "Preparing print…" window. The two `exportPNG` alerts that said "use Print to PDF" now say "Download PDF". Paper/orientation (Letter/Tabloid × landscape/portrait) and the **B131** overlay toggle are unchanged.
> **Self-verified headless** (**V60**, logged-out, against the built `dist/`): **(1)** real app — `ui-audit/verify-pdf-download.mjs` drove File ▾ → Download PDF / pick frame… → Download PDF and captured the ACTUAL file: `2026.06.20 Mesa Logistics - Plan 1.pdf`, a valid `%PDF`, **numPages 1**, page **exactly 792×612 pt**, **ZERO pop-up windows**, **0** errors. **(2)** pipeline — `ui-audit/verify-pdf-export.mjs` ran the exact raster→JPEG→`jpegToPdf` path for Letter (792×612) and Tabloid (1224×792), each a valid 1-page PDF that paints an image; all four paper corners white, **no cream field** (≤1 stray warm pixel = JPEG chroma-edge artifact), the **building drop-shadow + aerial `<image>` survive** the raster, table/metrics crisp at 300 DPI (`live-download-page.jpg`, `pdf-export-letter.jpg`). lint **0** · **496 tests** · build green (re-verified after merging the latest `main`); existing `verify-print-live.mjs` still passes with the renamed menu item; `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact.
> **Dedup:** NO existing open item covered this. **B131** (overlay-in-print toggle — done) is PRESERVED (the `printOverlay` checkbox still gates the placed overlay in the export). **B50** (export/print robustness) is partly SUPERSEDED for the print path: its "don't strand a blank Preparing… window on a serialization throw" guard is moot now that there's no window; PNG export keeps its own try/catch + alerts, untouched. **B159/B160** are the *Scheduler* Gantt PDF/Print export (a different module/app), not this Site Planner path. The single-SVG sheet composition (**B200**) + buildings table (**B197**) + filename (**B201**) are reused unchanged — only the final delivery step changed.

### B242 — On-building "＋ / −" controls for the whole dock stack + uniform panel rows `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(owner-reported, chat — "bring my plus buttons back to the building… plus and minus next to each other for every one of them, except the bump-outs." ### B239 — Schedule module still dead-ends after a deploy: harden stale-chunk recovery (cache-busting reload + chunk-aware ErrorBoundary) `[App Shell / Deploy]` (bug) — follow-up to B221  *(owner-reported 2026-06-20, chat: "my scheduling module not working… this is obviously a huge deal"; minted B228, renumbered **B239** — concurrent `main` took B228–B238 (dock-zone stack, Bluebeam vertex editing, map-finder batch, two-backend doc note) while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID after B238)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/optimistic-brahmagupta-ubw407`).** The owner still hit the Sequence/Schedule module on the workspace error screen with `Failed to fetch dynamically imported module: …/Scheduler-<hash>.js` **even though B221 had shipped** the stale-chunk auto-reload. **Confirmed the module itself is NOT broken** (headless `ui-audit/diagnose-scheduler.mjs` scenario A: the embedded Gantt renders **44 task rows** the moment its chunk loads — the earlier "blank iframe" reading was just measured before the in-browser Babel transpile of the ~692 KB `/sequence/` doc finished). The residual failure was two gaps in B221's *recovery path*, both fixed here:
- **The recovery reload wasn't guaranteed-fresh.** B221's auto-reload (and the boundary's manual reload) used a plain `location.reload()`, which the browser can satisfy from its OWN cached copy of the stale `index.html` — so the reload lands right back on the previous build's deleted chunk → second `vite:preloadError` → cooldown → dead-end. The no-cache `public/_headers` can't retro-fix an `index.html` a long-lived/returning tab already hard-cached. **Fix:** new `reloadFresh()` in `src/app/chunkReload.js` navigates to the same path with a throwaway `?_r=<ts>` query — a **distinct cache key** the browser MUST fetch from the server — via `location.replace` (no back-button trap), so it always pulls a fresh `index.html` and the current chunk names; `stripReloadParam()` tidies the param off the address bar on the recovered load (called at guard install). The `vite:preloadError` guard now calls `reloadFresh` (loop-guard/cooldown unchanged).
- **The ErrorBoundary's PRIMARY button was a no-op for this error.** "Try again" just `reset()`s → re-renders the same lazy import → re-requests the same dead chunk → fails identically (the dead-end the owner kept hitting). **Fix:** `ErrorBoundary.jsx` is now chunk-aware via a shared `isChunkLoadError()` (matches the dynamic-import failure phrasings across Chrome/Firefox/Safari + the SPA-fallback "expected JS, got text/html" MIME error). For a chunk error it reframes the screen as **"A new version of Planyr is ready"** with a single PRIMARY **"Reload to update"** (cache-busting) button — your work is saved. Genuine render crashes keep the Try again / Reload page pair (both reloads now cache-busting too).
- **`public/_headers` unchanged** — already correct from B221 (no-cache HTML, immutable hashed `/assets/*`); it's the *forward* guarantee, while `reloadFresh` is the *escape hatch* for tabs that cached the old HTML before it took effect.
- **Verified:** lint **0 errors** · **443 tests** (`test/chunkReload.test.js` 4→11: `isChunkLoadError` cross-browser matrix, `reloadFresh` cache-key/replace, `stripReloadParam`) · build green; `dist/_headers` still lands at the deploy root and all three lazy chunks emit hashed under `/assets/`. **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/diagnose-scheduler.mjs` + `ui-audit/verify-chunk-reload.mjs`, **all green** on the built bundle via `vite preview`): **(A)** a normal Schedule click mounts the iframe and renders 44 task rows; **(B)** a chunk that 404s once then recovers → the guard cache-busting-reloads and lands in the module; **(C)** a permanently-missing chunk surfaces the **"A new version of Planyr is ready"** screen (no reload loop), and clicking **"Reload to update"** performs a real cache-busting reload — captured nav trail `"/" → "/?_r=<ts>" → "/"` (the param added, then stripped). `verify-chunk-reload.mjs` still **3/3** (reload-once, cooldown holds, re-arms).
> **Owner note:** nothing to configure — the fix ships with the next deploy. Because `reloadFresh` cache-busts, even a browser still holding the *old* `index.html` escapes on the first recovery instead of dead-ending. Logged **VERIFICATION V58**.
> **Dedup:** a hardening of **B221** (same stale-chunk-after-deploy family — NOT a new bug class, and explicitly NOT a Scheduler/iframe logic bug, which was ruled out by the 44-row render). Distinct from the render-crash path the ErrorBoundary already handled (B205-era). No change to the lazy-chunk split or the iframe app.

### B238 — Scaffold the DWG→DXF conversion service in /server (LibreDWG primary, APS fallback dormant) `[server]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; provisionally B228, renumbered **B238** — concurrent `main` took B227–B236 while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID after B237)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/kind-johnson-oqzqco`).** Stood up the conversion **compute** service as a new `server/convert/` workspace alongside the existing /server storage/oauth scaffold — a tiny, dependency-free Node HTTP service that turns a **DWG** into a **DXF**, targeting **Google Cloud Run** (scale-to-zero). Endpoints: `POST /convert` (body = DWG bytes → DXF bytes, `X-Convert-Engine` header) and `GET /health`. Engine policy (`convertService.js`): **LibreDWG primary** (`libredwg.js` — spawns `dwg2dxf`, treats LibreDWG's error *bitmask* correctly: a non-empty DXF + non-critical code is success-with-warning, a critical code or no output is failure) → **Autodesk APS Model Derivative fallback** (`aps.js`) only when **`APS_ENABLED`** is on. **APS is DORMANT by default** (account not provisioned): real 2-legged auth is implemented + the full Model-Derivative pipeline is documented inline as a provisioning fill-in, but every dormant/unconfigured path returns a clear `{ok:false}` — never a throw, never a false success. **When LibreDWG fails and APS is off, the HTTP layer returns an explicit error (422), never a 200 with a junk body** — the same no-silent-failure contract as the storage adapter (it **reuses `server/storage/result.js`**, no parallel result type). Status map: 200 (DXF) · 400 (no/empty body) · 413 (over `MAX_UPLOAD_BYTES`) · 422 (unreadable drawing) · 503 (engine binary missing). All config via **server-side env only** (`config.js`: `PORT`, `LIBREDWG_BIN`, `CONVERT_TIMEOUT_MS`, `MAX_UPLOAD_BYTES`, `APS_ENABLED`, `APS_CLIENT_ID/SECRET`) — never a `VITE_` var, never committed. **Dockerfile** is a production-correct multi-stage build: stage 1 compiles **LibreDWG 0.13.4 from source** (it isn't in the Debian/Ubuntu repos), static-linked so stage 2 (`node:22-bookworm-slim`, non-root `node` user) carries just the ~MB `dwg2dxf` binary; no npm install (Node built-ins only).
> **Verified this session — built the image and ran the container for real.** `GET /health` → 200 `{ok,service:"dwg-convert",engine:"libredwg",apsFallback:false}`. `POST /convert` with two **real** sample drawings: **example_2000.dwg** (582 KB) → **200**, a valid `AutoCAD Drawing Exchange Format, version 2000` DXF (1.27 MB), `X-Convert-Engine: libredwg`; **example_2013.dwg** → **200**, valid DXF. **Failure path (the important one):** garbage (non-DWG) bytes with APS off → **422** `{"ok":false,"error":"DWG→DXF conversion failed in LibreDWG and the APS fallback is disabled (APS_ENABLED is off): …"}` — explicit, never a silent success; empty body → **400**; `GET /convert` → **405**. **+26 unit tests** (`test/dwgConvert.test.js`: config/APS-dormant parsing, LibreDWG success/warning/critical/spawn-fail/no-output, the engine-policy matrix incl. "APS never consulted when off", APS guard + auth shape, and the live HTTP server's status codes). lint **0 errors** · **462 tests** · `vite build` green; **isolation confirmed — `grep` of `dist/` finds zero conversion-service code** (the public bundle never imports `/server`).
> **Follow-on (NOT this item):** actual `gcloud run deploy` waits on the GCP project being provisioned in the Google Cloud Console; the service + Dockerfile are proven locally now. The Dockerfile's `CURL_INSECURE` build-arg exists ONLY to build behind this repo's sandbox TLS-inspecting proxy (CLAUDE.md); production/Cloud Build omits it → full TLS verification.
> **Dedup / inspect-first:** checked before writing — `/server` already held the B206–B209 Drive storage adapter + the B207 Google OAuth helper, so this is **additive** (`server/convert/` only); no existing /server code changed. The browser/Supabase side calls this over the network in the backend tranche (distinct from the Supabase user-data backend).

### B237 — Record the two-backend architecture in CLAUDE.md `[infra]` (task)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; provisionally B227, renumbered **B237** — concurrent `main` took B227–B236 while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID after B236)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/kind-johnson-oqzqco`).** Reconciled the existing **"Two backends — don't conflate"** section of `CLAUDE.md` **in place** (no duplicate section) so the data layer and the compute layer can never be confused: **(1) Supabase — the data/auth/storage layer (BUILT):** cloud Postgres, email/password auth, RLS, cloud save/load; the frontend talks to it **directly with the anon key**, which is safe in the browser **because RLS protects it** (a request only ever sees the signed-in user's own rows); the permanent home for user data. **(2) `/server` on Google Cloud Run — the compute layer (built in-repo, not yet deployed):** scale-to-zero containers running **DWG→DXF conversion** (LibreDWG primary → APS Model Derivative fallback, dormant behind `APS_ENABLED`) and **Google Drive auto-filing + bytes I/O** (the file-facts index itself lives in Supabase Postgres; the one-time OAuth *consent* callback is a thin same-origin Cloudflare Pages Function, the heavy compute is Cloud Run). Documented that **all third-party secrets (APS key, Google credentials, Supabase service-role key) stay server-side only, walled off from the public Cloudflare Pages deploy**; the only Supabase key that reaches the frontend is the RLS-protected **anon** key. The two layers talk **over the network** — Supabase the permanent data home, `/server` additive compute added in the backend tranche.
> **Also fixed a stale contradiction** surfaced while reconciling: the Workflow section still said *"Deploy = GitHub Pages (production)"* and *"Cloudflare Pages is optional and deferred"* — both false since the Pages-pipeline retirement (already recorded as DONE near the end of CLAUDE.md). Updated to **Cloudflare Pages = production (planyr.io)**, with per-branch previews noted as the separate optional Cloudflare concern, so the doc no longer contradicts itself about where the public deploy (the thing `/server` is walled off from) actually lives.
> **Dedup:** the section already existed — this **enriched it in place** (Cloud Run / scale-to-zero / LibreDWG→APS detail + the Cloudflare-Pages walling), it did not add a second copy. Doc-only change: lint 0 · 462 tests · build green (unaffected).

### B236 — Per-layer GIS data-age / source-vintage stamp `[Site Planner / GIS]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-5"; minted **B236** — concurrent `main` took B225–B231 while this was in flight, so B232–B236 are the real next free IDs)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/tender-goldberg-ax4n5w`).** Each GIS layer now shows a low-visual-weight **"as of: &lt;source vintage&gt;"** line in `components/LayerPanel.jsx` (rendered when the layer is on), kept **deliberately distinct** from the existing **"refreshed Xm ago"** cache-age stamp by the layer name — the two are never conflated. The vintage is the source's **own** effective/publication date or maintenance cadence, from a curated, central `LAYER_VINTAGE` map + `layerVintage(id, cfg)` in `lib/layers.js` (a per-config `vintage` override wins; else the map; else `null`). **Honest by rule:** per-panel / per-area datasets say what actually varies ("Effective date varies by FIRM panel", "Survey date varies by NWI project area", "LiDAR collection varies by county (USGS 3DEP)"); continuously-maintained registries say "continuously updated / current edition"; **any layer with no entry renders "vintage unknown" (italic) — never a fabricated date** (same family as "source unavailable ≠ not present"). **Scope:** source-vintage only; the "last refreshed" half rides the planned GIS-cache SWR work and is NOT built here.
> **Dedup:** the **standalone, ship-now** version of the data-age surfacing already specced inside **B96** (GIS layer cache, stale-while-revalidate) — when caching lands, fold the vintage stamp + the refreshed-age stamp into one surface rather than duplicating. **Self-verified headless** (**V57**, `ui-audit/verify-b232-b236.mjs`): toggling FEMA on shows "as of: Effective date varies by FIRM panel". lint 0 · 448 tests · build green; lazy chunk split intact.

### B232 — Address search doesn't recenter the map on "Go" `[Site Planner / map]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; minted **B232** — concurrent `main` (PRs #188/#189/#190/#191) took B225–B231 (building feature-buttons / Yield donut / dock-zone stack / Bluebeam vertex editing) while this was in flight, so B232–B236 are the real next free IDs)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/tender-goldberg-ax4n5w`).** Confirmed the impl note first: the geocode handler (`goAddress` in MapFinder.jsx) **already** flew the camera, so the bug was the **geocoder itself**, not unwired plumbing. The old code called OSM Nominatim with only `countrycodes=us` and **no viewport bias**, which routinely returns nothing for a bare house-number street address ("19630 Crossbranch") — so the map silently stayed put. Replaced with `geocodeAddress(q, center)`: tries the **Esri World Geocoding Service** `findAddressCandidates` first (keyless single lookup, the same ArcGIS family the app already uses for imagery/parcels, far better at exact US street addresses) **biased to the current map center** via `&location=`; falls back to **Nominatim biased to a ~0.6° viewbox** around the center. On a hit, `flyTo([lat,lon], 18)` — parcel-level zoom. Failure stays honest (the "couldn't find that address" toast).
> **Dedup / scope:** a separate failure path from B233 — this is the **geocode→camera** half; B233 is the parcel identify/select/info half. **Self-verified headless** (**V57**): "19630 Crossbranch Dr, Katy, TX" → Go recenters the map on the parcel (not a no-op).

### B230 — Replace always-visible "+" midpoint handles with Shift-click / right-click vertex insertion (Bluebeam-style) `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; provisionally B221, renumbered **B230** — concurrent `main` (PRs #184/#186/#188/#189/#191) took B221–B229 (lazy-chunk recovery, Schedule fixes, building-button gating, Yield-panel redesign, dock-zone stack) while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID after B229; the implementing commit + the PR still say "B221")*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/funny-franklin-hrk815`).** The permanent "+" midpoint handle that every editable edge used to carry is **gone in every state** (selected, moving, all of them); editing now follows the Bluebeam model. Built **once in a shared vertex-editing layer** so all editable geometry inherits it — **detention ponds, parcels, polygon elements, measurement polygons/lines, markup poly/line, and easement paths** — not per element type.
- **Shared core (new):** `editablePath()` resolves the current selection to a uniform `{ layer, id, pts, closed, min }`; `hitEditPath()` returns the nearest vertex / nearest edge within a **screen-pixel** tolerance (9px vert / 11px edge → zoom-independent grab radius); `insertVtx()` and `deleteVtx()` are single dispatchers keyed by `layer` (parcel/el/measure/markup/ease), each using functional `setState` so they always act on current state. Wired through **three capture-phase handlers** on the canvas `<svg>` (`onPointerDownCapture` / `onContextMenuCapture` / `onPointerMoveCapture`) so the same interaction reaches every layer **before** its own handlers, **without overlaying any new hit target** — a normal click/drag/select is untouched.
- **Add a vertex:** **Shift+click an edge** (away from a corner) drops a control point exactly at the click point on that segment; **right-click an edge** → portal "Add control point". **Delete a vertex:** **right-click a vertex** → portal "Delete control point"; **Delete/Backspace** removes the active control point. Deletion is blocked below the geometry minimum (**3 for a polygon**), and the menu item reads "(min reached)" + disables there.
- **Discoverability:** a faint **candidate-insertion dot** snaps to the nearest point on the edge under the cursor on **edge-hover during edit**, and brightens while **Shift** arms the insert — replacing exactly what the permanent "+" advertised, without the clutter. The **active control point** (the Delete target) renders inverted.
- **Kept:** the square corner handles (the real vertices) — shown only when selected, drag behavior unchanged. The five `add*Vertex` "+" handlers and the per-handle Shift-click-delete branches were removed (superseded). **Tie-break rule:** a **corner always wins over its adjacent edges** (`hitEditPath` returns both at a corner; a vertex right-click deletes, never adds), mirroring the insert rule `edge && !vertex` — this was the one real bug found in headless testing and fixed before merge.
- **Portal menu:** the Add/Delete-control-point menu is `createPortal`-mounted at `document.body` (z 6000/6001) so it can never be clipped or trapped behind the canvas / tool-rail stacking contexts; it reuses the app's existing `menu`/`menuPanel`/`menuItem` styling.
> **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-b221-b222.mjs`, logged-out, live Harris aerial, a polygon detention pond in a parcel): after selecting the pond — **0** "+" midpoint handles, **4** square vertex handles; **Shift+click an edge → 4→5** vertices with the candidate dot shown while Shift held; **edge-hover (no shift) shows the dot**; **right-click a vertex → portal "Delete control point" → 5→4**; **Delete key → 4→3**; repeated deletes **stop at 3** (polygon min guard). **0 console errors.** Screenshots `ui-audit/screens/b221-pond-selected.png` + `b221-after-edits.png` eyeballed (squares only, no plus marks). Logged **VERIFICATION V56**. lint **0 errors** · **436 tests** · build green; `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact.
> **Dedup:** AMENDS the now-done Bluebeam-editing items **B141** (editable vertices on the measurement tools) + **B147** (markup/shape vertex-edit for lines/polylines/polygons), which had introduced the "+" midpoint handle, and addresses the clutter **B215** flagged (the "+" stacking at the edge midpoint). Distinct from the open **B155/B156** (whole-shape interior hit-testing + hover highlight) — those select/hover a shape; this inserts/deletes control points on the already-selected shape.

### B231 — Restyle the detention pond to a modern "Cartographic" water-body treatment `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; provisionally B222, renumbered **B231** — next free ID after B230; concurrent `main` took B221–B229; the implementing commit + the PR still say "B222")*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/funny-franklin-hrk815`).** The detention pond no longer reads as dated clip-art. The decorative wavy-line water hatch, the saturated outline (which read as the Markup-accent orange — the wrong signal for water), and the monospace label are all replaced with a modern cartographic water-body style (how Mapbox / ArcGIS Pro render water). Implemented as a **named, reusable style token** so future water/basin features inherit it; **scoped to the pond element type** (never auto-applied to other polygons).
- **Token (`lib/planStyle.js`):** the pond `TYPE` is now `{ fill:"#5B97A5", stroke:"#2C5D6B", weight:2, cartoWater:true }` (replaced the old `water:true` wavy-hatch flag); `elStyle` exposes `cartoWater`. One token, reusable.
- **Fill (`renderElPx`):** a **radial steel-teal gradient** `#grad-water` (added to `<defs>`) that **deepens toward the center** — `#2F6675` at the middle → `#5B97A5` at the edge — at ~80% opacity, so a pond reads as water *with volume*, not a flat cutout. The old `pat-water` wavy pattern is deleted. Applies to both the polygon and rectangular pond branches.
- **Outline:** `#2C5D6B`, **2px at a constant screen-pixel width** (the canvas is drawn in pixel space, so the stroke never hairlines when zoomed out nor fattens when zoomed in); **3px when selected**. **No orange anywhere on the water body** — selection is signaled by the thicker teal stroke + the (transient, orange) editing handles, not a colour change on the feature itself.
- **Label:** switched monospace → **Inter** (the app's proportional UI sans), **dark slate `#0E2E36` with a white casing/halo** (always, so it stays legible over busy aerial), two lines kept — name above ("Detention Pond" / "Existing Detention Pond"), area sub-line below ("0.47 ac · 20,272 sf") — centered on the centroid (or the existing baseline anchor in expansion mode). Threaded through the shared LOD/label renderer via a per-candidate `carto` flag, so **only the pond label changes**; every other element label stays mono.
- **Map overview:** `MapFinder.jsx` resolves element fills through the same `elStyle`, so the map's pond pins inherit the flat steel-teal fill + teal outline automatically (no wavy, no orange) — no second code path; the expansion baseline ghost stroke was recoloured to match.
> **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-b221-b222.mjs`): `#grad-water` exists with stops **`#2F6675` → `#5B97A5`**; **no `#pat-water`**; the pond fill uses `url(#grad-water)`; the **`#2C5D6B`** outline is present; the label uses **Inter** + fill **`#0E2E36`** reading "Detention Pond / 2.14 ac · 93,100 sf". Screenshot `ui-audit/screens/b221-pond-selected.png` eyeballed — steel-teal body with a deeper center, crisp teal edge, haloed sans label, no hatch, no orange. **0 console errors.** lint 0 · 414 tests · build green.
> **Dedup:** AMENDS the pond rendering from **B132/B139** (expansion baseline + ghost) and **B140/B157** (on-map pond area labels — the two-line name+area is preserved). Distinct from **B219** (cartographic restyle of the map *furniture* — north arrow + scale bar); this is the *water body* itself.

### B239 — Restore the per-zone "＋" to add trailer parking / buffer from the selected court (regression from B228/B229) `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(owner-reported, angry — "I literally can't add the 50 foot trailer parking anymore. I lost that ability." Filed provisionally as B230, but concurrent `main` took B230–B238 while this was in flight, so renumbered to the real next free ID **B239**.)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/practical-faraday-9mmfch`).** B229's panel reorg **removed the "＋ 50′ trailer parking (far side)" button** that lived on a selected truck court and replaced it with a depth-only editor — so selecting the court no longer offered any way to add the trailer parking. Worse, the building-level "＋" advances **every dock side together at the min level**, so on a cross-dock building with a court on only ONE side it stays stuck adding *courts* to the empty side and never reaches trailer parking on the side that has a court. Net effect: the owner could not add the 50′ trailer parking at all. **Fix (`SitePlanner.jsx`):** the selected dock-zone panel (court / trailer / buffer) now shows, beside the inline depth field, a **"＋ Add <next outward zone>"** button (court → "＋ Add trailer parking", trailer → "＋ Add buffer") that adds the next zone **on that one dock side** via `addZoneOnSide`, plus a **"－ Remove <this zone>"** (cascades to outer zones). This restores the exact per-side "＋" workflow that existed before B228/B229, independent of the other dock side; the building-level unit "＋/−" stays as the grow/shrink-everything convenience.
> **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-dock-zones.mjs` regression — all checks still pass — plus a focused repro: cross-dock building with a court on the RIGHT only → select the court → "＋ Add trailer parking" appears → adds trailer on the **right side only** (count 1, not both) → select the trailer → "＋ Add buffer" → adds buffer; **0 page errors**). lint **0 errors** · **481 tests** · build green; `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact. Logged **VERIFICATION V55** (updated).

### B228 — Building-anchored dock-zone stack with LIFO +/− `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; provisionally B221, renumbered **B228** — concurrent `main` took B221–B227 (PRs #186 lazy-chunk reload, #188 B225/B226 feature-button visibility, #189 B227 yield panel, #184 B222–B224 Schedule) while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID after B227)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/practical-faraday-9mmfch`).** The building footprint is now the control hub for the dock-side site elements: a single **"+"** adds the next zone **outward** from the dock face, a single **"−"** peels the **outermost** one off (LIFO). Fixed outward order **truck court → trailer parking → buffer**; "+" walks out (court → trailer → buffer), "−" walks in (buffer → trailer → court).
- **Reused, not duplicated:** the court stays the existing `truckCourt` paving strip and trailer parking the existing far-side `forCourt` striped row — the change unifies their geometry under one pure layout and adds the buffer. **Buffer is the new zone** — a sage `landscape` clear strip (buffer/setback) bonded to its trailer via a new `forTrailer` tag, labelled "<d>′ Buffer".
- **One geometry source:** `src/workspaces/site-planner/lib/dockZones.js` (`DOCK_ZONES`, `zoneDepthDefaults`, `layoutZone`) positions all three zones flush-outward from the building face, full wall length, trailer rotated so its stalls run along the wall. Used by add / remove / inline depth-edit / **building-resize** (the rewritten `refitChildren` re-lays the stack), so depths survive a resize and outer zones always stay flush. **12 unit tests** (`test/dockZones.test.js`): order, configurable defaults, flush-outward stacking (gap-free, no overlap), vertical-side rotation, building rotation.
- **Editable depths inline** (US survey feet, EPSG:2278), defaults **135 / 50 / 15** and **user-configurable** in **Setup → Dock zones** (`settings.truckCourtD/trailerParkD/bufferD`) — not hardcoded.
- **Creation rerouted through the building "+":** trailer parking + buffer now add from the building panel (and the on-canvas court "+" → trailer "+" → buffer "+" chain). **Car parking** is **also** added from the building panel but occupies the **ends (non-dock short sides)** and is tracked as its **own element outside** the LIFO stack, with its own remove. **[assumption flagged for Michael: should car parking instead join the LIFO removal order? — shipped as a separate control.]**
- **Both long sides:** zones **mirror to every dock face with doors** (cross-dock = both); the "+"/"−" operate on the whole dock-zone set as a **unit** (one "+" advances every dock side; "−" peels the outermost off every dock side). **[assumption flagged for Michael — shipped this way.]**
- **Bump-outs are NOT in this stack** — a footprint modifier, behaviour unchanged; only relocated in the panel (B229).
- **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-dock-zones.mjs`, logged-out, cross-dock building): "+"×3 → 2 courts / 2 trailers / 2 buffers, outward order court→trailer→buffer, "+" disabled at full; inline buffer depth 15→40 grew the band with outer zones staying flush; building resize 600→760 kept all zones attached, full-width and flush; "−"×3 peeled buffer→trailer→court; car-parking-ends added a field; **0 page errors**. lint **0 errors** · **448 tests** · build green; the `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk split still holds. Logged **VERIFICATION V55**.
> **Dedup:** NOT B71 (per-element trailer curb 6″→12″) or B78 (stall-layout freeze guard); orthogonal to main's B225/B226 (those size-GATE these feature buttons — visibility; this is the zone stack the buttons drive). Reuses the court (`truckCourt`/`makeStrip`), far-side trailer (`forCourt`/`oppTrailerGeom`) and bump-out (`dogEar`/`placeDogEars`) machinery; the orphaned old one-shot helpers (`addTruckCourt`, `addStripSide`, `makeOppTrailer`, `TRUCK_COURT_D`) were removed.

### B227 — Redesign Site Yield panel: composition donut, identity icon, grouped rows, semantic palette `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; provisionally B225, renumbered **B227** — concurrent `main` (#188) minted B225 + B226 (building feature-edit-button visibility) while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID after B226)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/jolly-turing-n8rmzy`).** Presentational reskin of the Site Yield panel — **no engine / data-model / RLS / persistence change** (it stays per-user/private, reading the exact values the planner already computes). New self-contained `YieldPanel` component (+ a scoped `YIELD_PAL` semantic palette) replaces the old generic `<Section title="Site yield">` in `SitePlanner.jsx`; the generic `Section` and every other panel are untouched. Layout top→bottom: **(1)** a header row = a **parcel-with-footprint identity glyph** (terracotta lot outline `#C0532E` + filled footprint + a half-opacity outbuilding) in a 32 px soft `#F6E7DD` tile + the tracked "SITE YIELD" label + a collapse chevron (its own `useState`, mirroring `Section` — collapse/expand preserved). **(2)** the three existing KPI cards (Site ac · Building abbreviated "227k" · Coverage %), card `#F2ECE1`, tabular-mono. **(3)** a new **composition donut + legend**: how the site partitions into Building / Paving / Open-green / Detention, derived from engine OUTPUTS only — `buildingPct = coverage`, `pavingPct = max(0, impervious% − coverage%)`, `detentionPct = detentionSf/siteSf×100`, `openPct = 100 − the rest (clamp ≥0)` — so the four always sum to 100 and the ring closes. SVG (~100 px, 13 px stroke): faint `#ECE3D5` track + four `stroke-dasharray` arcs, group rotated −90° to start at top, butt caps, contiguous (`dashoffset = −Σ earlier arcs`); center = site acreage over "acres". Legend beside it always renders the **Detention row even at 0 %** with a muted hollow zero-state swatch (`#DCE5EB`/`#C2D2DC`) — zero ≠ absent. **(4)** a hairline divider. **(5)** **grouped detail rows** (Land·sage / Building·terracotta / Parking·taupe / Stormwater·blue), each a semantic dot + tracked label over label-left/mono-value rows, all wired to live values; the prior extras are preserved in their natural group (bump-out sub-line + inactive-parcel note under Land/Building; the easement encumbrance readout as a subordinate trailing "Easements" block). **One semantic colour = one meaning** across the donut arcs, the legend swatches, and the group dots. Out of scope by request: the headroom/limit bars + scheme-compare view (set aside in chat).

Those are *numbers*; this was a *presentation* pass over the same values, so no metric or persisted field changed.

### B226 — Show feature-edit buttons only on the selected/hovered building `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; minted **B226** — next free ID after B225)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/lucid-heisenberg-mjhpw3`).** **Dedup finding:** the per-building feature-add buttons ALREADY rendered only on the *selected* building (gated on `sel.kind==='el' && el.id===sel.id`), never "on every building in view" — so that half of the arriving ask was already true. Implemented the rest as the requested SINGLE visibility rule: the buttons render for exactly ONE building — `featActiveId =` the selected one, else (in select mode) the one HOVERED — and only when the **B225** footprint-size gate passes. Net rule: **buttons visible iff (footprint large enough on screen) AND (building selected OR hovered).** **Hover** (`SitePlanner.jsx`: new `hoverElId` state + a block in `onMove`) is computed **position-based** (the topmost building whose footprint bbox contains the cursor), NOT via SVG `onPointerEnter/Leave` — because the buttons sit INSIDE the footprint, an enter/leave trigger would flicker the buttons off the instant the cursor moved toward one; the position test keeps the hover alive. It only runs while idle in select mode with **nothing selected** (selection otherwise drives the buttons), so there's no per-frame churn once you've clicked. Hover previews the add-buttons only — resize/rotate grips stay selection-only.
> **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-b225-b226.mjs`, logged-out): with nothing selected, the not-hovering baseline = **0** buttons, hovering the building reveals its **8** (`b226-hover.png` shows the add-buttons with NO selection grips → pure hover), and moving off hides them (**0**). So the buttons appear on the ONE active building only, gated by the same size rule. Logged **VERIFICATION V53**. lint 0 · 414 tests · build green; `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact.
> **Dedup:** same render condition as **B225** (folded into one rule, per the arriving note "Combine with NEW-1 into one visibility rule"). Sibling of **B156** (hover-highlight the markup under the cursor) — that's the markup-layer version; this is the building-handle case, position-based for the same flicker reason. Distinct from selection hit-testing (**B155**).

### B225 — Hide building feature-edit buttons when the on-screen footprint is too small (anti-cluster) `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; minted **B225** — highest B# across both files was B220, so this is the real next free ID)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/lucid-heisenberg-mjhpw3`).** Zooming OUT on a building with feature-add buttons shrank its footprint while the fixed-pixel +/− buttons (truck-dock / sidewalk / bump-out / parking-row — each inset ~22px inside a wall, r=9) stayed full size, so the cluster grew larger than the footprint and spilled past the edges into an unreadable pile (the owner's screenshot). **Fix (`SitePlanner.jsx`):** each feature-add button is now gated on the building's RENDERED on-screen footprint size in PIXELS (`el.w/el.h * view.ppf`) against a tunable module const `FEAT_BTN_MIN_PX = 72` (≈ the ~22px inset + 9px radius clearance on each side, plus a small legibility margin — opposite buttons overlap below ~68px). The gate is **per-axis**: a wall's inset +/− needs its PERPENDICULAR on-screen dimension ≥ 72px (top/bottom gated on height-px, left/right on width-px); the corner bump-outs need BOTH axes. So a long/narrow on-screen footprint keeps its long-side buttons and drops only the cramped short-end ones — the overlap case the arriving note flagged ("also check") is handled inherently, no collapse-menu needed — and a fully-small footprint drops ALL of them (no spill). Applied to all three feature-add node groups (`sideAddNodes`, `courtAddNodes`, `parkingAddNodes`). **Resize/rotate grips are intentionally NOT gated** (still usable on a small building — the spec says "only the editable feature buttons are suppressed"); the map's **Building Pin + Progress Arc live in `MapFinder.jsx`** (a different component) and are **untouched**, so they stay visible at every zoom level, as required.
> **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-b225-b226.mjs`, logged-out, 400′×300′ cross-dock building): swept the wheel zoom from large to tiny; at every non-ambiguous step the drawn button count matched the rule predicted from the measured footprint px — **8** while large (494×370 … 127×95px), **2** (long-side sidewalks only) at **81×60px** (height < 72 ≤ width → per-axis collision handling), **0** once tiny (≤ 64×48px). Screens `b225-zoomed-in.png` / `b225-partial-longside.png` / `b225-zoomed-out.png`. Logged **VERIFICATION V53**. lint 0 · 414 tests · build green; `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact.
> **Dedup:** distinct from **B149** (LOD tiering — which *dimensions/labels* draw at a given zoom) and **B121** (label-overlap engine) — those govern annotations; this governs the *interactive edit handles*. Combined with **B226** into ONE visibility rule (size-gate AND selected-or-hovered). Reuses the **B30** precedent of pixel-projected (not feet-based) thresholds.

### B224 — "Schedule-assembling" themed loading animation, reusable engine across modules `[Scheduler]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-3"; provisionally B220, renumbered **B224** — concurrent `main` (#183, #185, #187) took B218–B221 while this was in flight, so the real next free block was B222–B224)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/awesome-pascal-zlb19p`).** A reusable, per-module themed loader replaces the bare "Loading workspace…" text. New `src/shared/ui/ModuleLoader.jsx` (one animation engine) + pure, unit-tested theming `src/shared/ui/moduleLoaderTheme.js` (skin + label) over the shared `src/shared/ui/moduleAccent.js` (`MODULE_ACCENT` extracted to a React-free module; `AppHeader` re-exports it for back-compat). **Schedule skin** = a Gantt building itself: zebra row bands fade in top→bottom (the real banding tints), ghost task bars wipe in left→right staggered (~100 ms/row) in the accent **`#7F77DD`**, milestone diamonds pop at bar ends, and a soft vertical **playhead** sweeps left→right; the assemble loop fades at its boundary so it repeats seamlessly, then **cross-fades** (not a hard cut) into the real Gantt. **Site Planner skin** = a parcel outline **stroke-drawing itself** + building footprints fading in + a north-arrow, in the Site accent **`#1D9E75`** — same engine, different grammar. **Accessibility:** honors `prefers-reduced-motion` (drops the cascade + sweep for a static skeleton + gentle pulse). **Threshold:** holds invisible for ~250 ms so fast loads never flash it. **Wired** as the Shell `Suspense` fallback (themed by active module — covers the chunk-fetch phase) AND as a cross-fading overlay in `Scheduler.jsx` over the iframe until its first `planar:nav-state` (covers the heavy iframe boot — the actually-slow phase), with a 9 s safety timeout so it can never stick.
> **Self-verified headless** (**V52**, `ui-audit/verify-loader-prefetch.mjs`): on Schedule nav the loader shows (`role="status"`, `aria-label="Assembling schedule…"`, 12 elements in `#7F77DD`, SVG present — `loader-schedule.png`) then cross-fades to the iframe; with `prefers-reduced-motion` the cascade + playhead are dropped (**0 animated bars, no playhead** — `loader-reduced-motion.png`). +5 tests in `test/moduleLoaderTheme.test.js` (per-module skin/accent, fallback, threshold). **Dedup:** the loader reuses `MODULE_ACCENT`, so it can never drift from the tab/brand colors. **Pairs with B223** (that shrinks the wait; this covers the residual). lint 0 · 419 tests · build green; lazy chunk split intact.

### B223 — Speed up Schedule module load `[Scheduler]` (task)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; provisionally B219, renumbered **B223** — concurrent `main` (#183, #185, #187) took B218–B221)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/awesome-pascal-zlb19p`).** Profiled first: the Schedule tab embeds the standalone Gantt app (`public/sequence/index.html`, ~692 KB) in an iframe, so the dominant navigation cost is **doc-fetch** (downloading + parsing that HTML each visit), not the trivial `Scheduler.jsx` chunk, and not layout/paint. **Shipped the prefetch (the measured win):** new `src/app/modulePrefetch.js` — `prefetchModule(id)` warms a workspace's lazy chunk (same dynamic-import specifier Vite already code-splits) **and, for Schedule, injects `<link rel="prefetch" href="/sequence/">`** so the iframe doc is cached before the click. Wired two triggers: **idle** (`prefetchOnIdle(["scheduler","doc-review"])` via `requestIdleCallback` in `Shell.jsx`, after first paint) and **hover-intent** (`ModuleTab`'s `onMouseEnter` in `AppHeader.jsx`). Lazy-loading still gates the first boot — nothing prefetches until idle. **Confirmed already-satisfied (no change needed):** both `GridView` and `GanttView` already **virtualize** (row windowing by scroll, `startIdx`/`endIdx` + slice), `GanttView` already `useMemo`s its dep-line/month/year layout, and the app already paints from an inline `__PLANAR_DATA__` seed before the Supabase sync (so the cloud round-trip is off the critical first paint and the silent-failure save guard is intact).
> **Self-verified headless** (**V52**, `ui-audit/verify-loader-prefetch.mjs`): the `/sequence/` prefetch link is injected after boot-idle; no boot console errors. **Pairs with B224.** lint 0 · 419 tests · build green; `Scheduler` (1.79 kB) / `DocReview` / `SitePlannerApp` chunks stay separate.

### B222 — Row color fill hides Gantt bars `[Scheduler]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; provisionally B218, renumbered **B222** — concurrent `main` (#183, #185, #187) took B218–B221)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/awesome-pascal-zlb19p`).** Applying a row color fill made the task bars on that row disappear from the Gantt. **Root cause was a color collision (b):** in `GanttView` (`public/sequence/index.html`), `task.rowColor` was overloaded — the same field that paints the row background (`rowBg`) was also the bar fill via `task.rowColor || <neutral>` for **leaf bars, summary brackets, AND milestone diamonds** — so a fill repainted every on-row datum its own color and it vanished into its own background. **Fix:** each datum now keeps its **own identity hue independent of the row fill** — leaf bars + milestone diamonds = neutral gray `#94a3b8`, summary brackets = depth-navy — and carries a **hairline edge** (`#475569`, a slate darker than the fill) so it stays legible on any fill; notably the **solid/complete leaf bar gained a 1px border** (it was borderless and was the one that fully disappeared on a matching fill). The row fill is now pure background decoration. **Paint order verified + documented** (z-index): row fill (row `<div>`, z auto, bottom) → grid/today/dependency lines (z2–4) → bars/milestones (z5, data layer) → bar + name labels (z6–7, top). Holistic: covers bars, diamonds, links, and labels.
> **Self-verified headless** (**V51**, `ui-audit/verify-rowfill-bars.mjs`, logged-out seed): with a leaf task seeded a row fill, the fill paints the row bands (`rowBands:2`) with **zero bar-sized collisions** (`barCollisions:0`); the bar keeps `#94a3b8` + the `#475569` 1px edge (`rowfill-bars-crop.png` shows the marker clearly on the tinted row). **Dedup:** distinct from B210–B212 (the prior Gantt tranche — brackets / status-as-fill / columns). The PDF/Print export path (`buildGanttSVG`) already paints bars neutral gray/navy and never reads `rowColor` for bars — no collision there, left untouched. lint **0 errors** · **419 tests** · build green; lazy chunk split intact.

### B221 — Lazy workspaces fail to load after a deploy: "Failed to fetch dynamically imported module" (stale content-hashed chunk) `[App Shell / Deploy]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; provisionally B218, renumbered **B221** — concurrent `main` (PR #183) took B218 (dead header controls) + B219 (map-furniture restyle) and a parallel session took B220 (map-finder over-zoom) while this was in flight, so B221 is the real next free ID after B220. The branch's first commit + the PR were opened as "B218". Deduped against the PDF.js `import()` items (B72/B67/B180 lazy-load a heavy library on first use — unrelated to the stale-chunk-after-deploy failure here).)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/cool-ptolemy-2lb1js`).** Root cause confirmed as the standard Vite stale-chunk-after-deploy problem (NOT a logic bug inside DocReview, and NOT a broken/partial build — the build is green and all three workspace chunks emit cleanly under `/assets/`): an already-open tab is holding the *previous* deploy's `index.html`, which references content-hashed filenames like `/assets/DocReview-<oldhash>.js`; once Cloudflare serves the new build those files are gone, so switching into a not-yet-loaded workspace 404s and throws the user onto the workspace error screen. A hard reload fixes it because it re-fetches the current `index.html` (and its new hashes). Fix, applied globally so it covers **every** lazy route (Site Planner, Document Review, Sequence), not just DocReview:
- **Auto-reload-once on dynamic-import failure** — `src/app/chunkReload.js` (`installChunkReloadGuard`, wired in `src/main.jsx` before render) listens for Vite's `vite:preloadError` window event and reloads the page once. **Loop guard:** the time of the last auto-reload is stamped in `sessionStorage` (`planyr:chunkReloadAt`); a second preloadError within a 10 s cooldown does **not** reload — a genuinely-missing chunk (a broken/partial deploy) falls through to the existing `ErrorBoundary` instead of reload-looping. The stamp self-expires so a *later, separate* deploy re-arms a fresh one-time recovery — deliberately more robust than a boolean flag cleared on mount, which would either race the reload (auto-loop if the default workspace's chunk is the missing one) or reload on every click of a truly-broken module (never letting its error show). The pure decision (`shouldReloadAfterPreloadError`) is unit-tested.
- **Cloudflare cache headers** — `public/_headers` (copied verbatim to `dist/_headers` at the deploy root): `/assets/*` (the content-hashed, immutable build files) get `Cache-Control: public, max-age=31536000, immutable`; the HTML entry points (`/`, `/index.html`, `/sequence/`) get `Cache-Control: no-cache` so a new deploy's asset hashes propagate on the next load instead of being pinned behind a hard-cached HTML.
- **Verified:** lint 0 errors · **418 tests** (incl. the new `test/chunkReload.test.js`, 4) · build green; `dist/_headers` lands at the deploy root and the three lazy chunks (`DocReview-*`, `Scheduler-*`, `SitePlannerApp-*`) emit hashed under `/assets/`. **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-chunk-reload.mjs`, **3/3** against the built bundle on `vite preview`): a first `vite:preloadError` reloads the page; a second within the cooldown does NOT (no loop); pushing the stamp past the cooldown reloads again (re-armed).
> **Owner note:** the `_headers` cache rules take effect automatically once Cloudflare redeploys (on merge to `main`); nothing to configure. **Dedup:** distinct from the PDF.js `import()` lazy-loading in B72/B67/B180 (those defer a heavy library until first use — a feature), and from B205-era ErrorBoundary work (that catches *render* crashes; this catches *chunk-fetch* failures and recovers before the boundary is reached).

### B220 — Esri imagery shows "Map data not yet available" placeholder on over-zoom (map finder) `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; minted B218, renumbered **B220** — concurrent `main` PR #183 took B218 (dead header controls) + B219 (map-furniture restyle) while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID after B219. The implementing commits on this branch still say "B218".)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/quirky-mayer-s3n0pm`).** On the Site Planner **map finder**, zooming in past the area's native imagery ceiling with Esri selected filled the whole canvas with gray "Map data not yet available" tiles while street labels still rendered on top. **Root cause (confirmed):** Esri World Imagery serves those placeholder tiles as **HTTP 200** (not errors), so Leaflet's error-tile fallback never fires; on a retina/HiDPI display `detectRetina` (added in B170 for sharpness) fetches one zoom level **higher** than the display zoom (zoomOffset +1), so a plain `maxNativeZoom: 19` let deep zoom request **z20** = the placeholder. **B182 already fixed this exact bug, but only on the planner-canvas backdrop** (`SitePlanner.jsx` GEO_BASEMAP detail layer's `detailMaxNative`); the **map-finder** layer (`MapFinder.jsx`) got `detectRetina` from B170 but **never the matching clamp** — an incomplete original fix across the two call sites, not a refactor revert. **Fix (`MapFinder.jsx`):** the imagery `L.tileLayer` now clamps `maxNativeZoom` to `L.Browser.retina ? bm.maxNative - 1 : bm.maxNative` for **every source in the Imagery dropdown** (Esri 19→18, USGS 16→15 on retina), keeping `maxZoom: 21` so Leaflet **upscales** the deepest real tile past native instead of fetching placeholders. The labels/reference overlay (World_Transportation) is capped at `maxNativeZoom: 19` so it can't diverge above the imagery at deep zoom (the "labels float over gray" tell). Durable code comments left at the `BASEMAPS` config + both layer sites so a future restructure can't silently drop them. **Verified headless** (`gis-verify/mapfinder-overzoom-verify.mjs`, the map finder driven deep over a Katy parcel at DSF 1 and DSF 2): max imagery tile zoom requested = **z19 at both densities** (was z20 on retina), max labels zoom = **z19**, **0** placeholder/past-native responses — logged **VERIFICATION V50**. lint **0 errors** · **414 tests** · build green; lazy chunks intact.
> **Dedup:** RECURRENCE/completion of **B182** (done — planner-canvas placeholder fix) across the second call site; builds on **B170** (detectRetina) + **B169** (blur diagnostic). Distinct from **B171** (gated high-res-source eval — correctly NOT triggered; the imagery source isn't the problem) and **B162** (label zoom gating).

### B219 — Professional cartographic restyle of the map north arrow + scale bar `[Site Planner]` (task)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; minted **B219** — next free ID after B218)*

### B216 — Harden edge-run setbacks for IRREGULAR parcels: concave inward placement + gentle-curve grouping `[Site Planner]` (bug/task) — follow-up to B214/B215  *(owner-requested edge-case pass 2026-06-19; minted **B216** — highest B# across both files was B215, so this is the real next free ID)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sharp-edison-7gdn3y`).** Edge-case testing on irregular parcels (L-shapes, flag lots, curved frontage, dense survey boundaries, triangles) surfaced two issues, both fixed. **(1) Concave inward placement (refines B215):** the setback pill / boundary-dim fan chose the inboard side by stepping *toward the parcel centroid* — but on a concave / L-shaped / flag-lot parcel the centroid can sit in a notch (or outside the polygon), so a pill was thrown to the WRONG side (outside the lot). Replaced with a **point-in-ring test** (a small step that must land INSIDE the boundary) via a new `inwardScreenNormal` helper (computed in feet, mapped to screen), used by the per-side pill, the per-segment pill, AND the run-length dimension — correct on any shape. **(2) Gentle-curve grouping (refines B214):** `edgeRuns` now chains each edge to the **PREVIOUS** edge's bearing (was the run's FIRST edge), so a gently curved frontage (a few degrees per segment) or survey noise on a nominally-straight line groups into **ONE** side (one setback, one pill, one dimension) instead of many; a genuine corner still breaks the run, and a TIGHT curve (each segment turning beyond tolerance) correctly stays per-segment.
> **Tests:** +2 `edgeRuns` unit tests (gentle-curve groups; tight-curve splits — **14** in `test/edgeRuns.test.js`). New headless harness `ui-audit/verify-edge-runs-irregular.mjs` (L-shape, flag lot, tight + gentle curved frontage, dense 12-vertex survey boundary, triangle) — **19/19**: every setback pill lands inside the lot (the concave fix), every run-length dim outside, no NaN, and the shallow arc groups to 4 sides (not 17). lint **0 errors** · **411 tests** · build green; the original **B213–B215 acceptance still 7/7** (the chain change keeps the 3-segment-east-side case at 4 sides). Verified **V48**. **Dedup:** not a new feature — hardens the B214 run-grouping + B215 fan placement for irregular geometry; same canonical `pc.setbacks` model.

### B215 — Stacked/occluded dimension labels at shared parcel-edge anchors (boundary dim + setback pill + "+" all at the edge midpoint) `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-3"; minted **B215** — next free ID after B214)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sharp-edison-7gdn3y`, commit `cc735e9`).** The parcel-edge boundary dimension, the setback value pill, and the add-vertex "+" handle no longer stack at the same edge midpoint. Each logical SIDE now gets **one run-length dimension placed OUTBOARD** of the edge (`parcelEdgeLabels` rewritten over `selRuns` + `runLabelAnchors`), and the **setback value pill is placed INBOARD** (toward the setback line it describes) — fanned ~25 px apart along the edge normal, so neither occludes the other. The add-vertex "+" stays at the segment midpoint (it is the add-vertex handle, not a stack-expander) and now reads clearly once the dims move off it. No setback-line *length* label is ever drawn (the only length label is the boundary/run dimension), so there is nothing redundant to suppress.
> **Dedup / dependency:** built **with B214** — run-grouping collapses the per-segment dimension stack into one label per side; B215 adds the boundary-vs-setback inboard/outboard fan that run-grouping alone does not. Distinct from **B121** (element NAME/area label overlap, `labelLayout.js`) and **B149** (zoom LOD) — those are the centred element-label pool; this is the parcel-edge dimension/setback/handle pool. Self-verified headless (**V47**, `ui-audit/verify-edge-runs.mjs`): 4 run-length dims (one per side), each fanned 25 px from its pill.

### B214 — Edit setback across a multi-segment side in one action (edge "runs") `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; minted **B214** — next free ID after B213)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sharp-edison-7gdn3y`, commit `cc735e9`).** New pure, unit-tested `src/workspaces/site-planner/lib/edgeRuns.js` groups a parcel's **contiguous near-collinear edges** (±7° of the run's first-edge bearing, wrap-around-aware) into **runs** = logical sides, so a side a survey digitized as ~10 segments reads as ONE side. On the selected parcel the on-canvas setback editor shows **one pill per side**; editing it applies the value across **every segment of the run at once** via `setRunSetback`, writing the **canonical per-edge `pc.setbacks` array** (what `setbacksOf`/`constraintsOf`/`developableArea` read — no parallel store) which `offsetPolygon` already miters into one continuous setback line. A **"By side / Per segment" toggle** (shown only when a side has >1 segment) plus **Alt-click a side pill** give the single-edge override for notches/jogs. The run also drives the single run-length dimension (B215). Easement `restrictsBuildings`/`restrictsPaving` flags already feed the same model via `exclusionZonesOf`, so both setbacks and easement exclusions reach the (stubbed) `developableArea` verdict engine — structurally integrated.
> **Dedup:** reuses the contiguous-edge-run idea already shipped for parcel-edge easements (`buildParcelEdgeStrip` + `easeEdges`), here auto-grouped by bearing and applied to setbacks. Distinct from **B146** (interactive ELEMENT dimension callouts). **+12 unit tests** (`test/edgeRuns.test.js`). Self-verified headless (**V47**): selecting a parcel with a 3-segment east side shows **4 pills (S, E-run, N, W), not 6 edges**; "Per segment" → 6; toggling back → 4.

### B213 — Inactive parcel still shows its setback line, acreage label, and edge/boundary dimensions (active-state not inherited by anchored elements) `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; minted **B213** — first filed as B206, then twice renumbered as concurrent `main` (PR #175 then PR #177) took B206–B212 in the same window; this Site-Planner trio landed at the next free block **B213–B215** to keep IDs unique)*

### B211 — Task status as fill treatment (hollow / partial / solid) `[Scheduler / Gantt]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; minted B195, renumbered **B211** — concurrent `main` took B194–B209 while this was in flight)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sharp-keller-wphsna`).** Task status moved **off the color channel onto a single continuous fill treatment** in both Gantt render paths (on-screen `GanttView` + the PDF/print `buildGanttSVG`). Every task bar keeps **one identity hue** (the existing task **gray `#94a3b8`**, or an explicit per-task `rowColor` override); status reads as **0→100% complete**: **not started (0%)** = hollow rounded pill (outline in the hue, required else invisible); **in progress** = partial fill (solid portion = `percentComplete`, lighter remainder behind it, thin outline around the whole); **complete (100%)** = solid fill. A **min-width floor** keeps a 0% bar from collapsing to a sliver. Fill fraction derives from `percentComplete` (Complete → solid regardless). The **red / paused / overdue** signal stays in the **row background + the table** (untouched), so status never collides with the navy hierarchy. Milestone diamonds follow the same monochrome language (gray, filled when complete, hollow otherwise).

### B210 — Summary bars as depth-stepped brackets `[Scheduler / Gantt]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; minted B194, renumbered **B210** — concurrent `main` took B194–B209 while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sharp-keller-wphsna`).** Replaced the heavy solid summary bars (a thick slab + barely-visible triangle endcaps) with a thin **bracket**: a navy horizontal **span** with **straight-down vertical legs** at each end (no triangles), in both render paths (`GanttView` + `buildGanttSVG`). WBS nesting depth is encoded by **three cues that step together, top-of-tree strongest** — **darkness** (navy `#2B3340` → `#46506A` → `#6E7790` → tint), **span thickness** (7/5/4/4 px), and **leg length** (a fraction of row height) — the ramp **stops deepening at ~4 levels** (the table's indented name carries depth from there). The summary **name centers just above the span** in the bar's own level-navy (no thick fill to print white onto); no per-level label indentation (bars are date-positioned). An explicit `rowColor` override still wins.
> **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-sequence.mjs`): DOM probe finds **36 navy bracket elements** (≈ a dozen brackets × span+2 legs); a detail screenshot confirms the shape — label above a thin span with a straight-down leg, **no triangle**. 0 runtime errors. lint 0 · 352 tests · build green.

### B203 — Schedule project picker showed Site Planner projects; scheduling projects inaccessible `[Scheduler / Header-Nav]` (bug) — CRITICAL  *(owner-reported 2026-06-19; minted **B203** — concurrent `main` (#169–#172) took B194–B202 while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID after B202)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/elegant-bohr-16zcag`).** Owner: in the **Schedule** module the Row-1 project picker listed **Site Planner** sites, and his scheduling projects (Goose Creek, Kilgore - Grand Port / "Grandport", Eight South a.k.a. vSAN, Pursuits, Papadopoulos) were unreachable.
> **Diagnosis first (the silent-data-loss rule) — data was NEVER lost.** The Schedule workspace embeds a separate scheduler app in an **iframe** (`public/sequence/index.html`); that app stores ALL projects as one cloud record (`hs-v1`) in its **own** Supabase project (`ksetjztkplttbcehyicv`), cloud-first with the baked `__PLANAR_DATA__` only as a first-run seed. Inside the iframe the scheduler **hides its own header** (`.in-iframe .app-header{display:none}`), which is where its project picker + Dashboard/Projects toggle lived. The B191–B193 shared breadcrumb that replaced it reads `listProjects()` → the **Site Planner** site store and routes every action into the Site Planner — so Schedule showed Site projects and couldn't open scheduler ones. A wiring bug, not a data bug.
> **Fix — make the Row-1 picker module-aware via a postMessage bridge** (no second store, no schema change): the embedded scheduler now emits its OWN nav state (project list + active project + section) to the shell (`planar:nav-state`) and accepts select / dashboard / new-project commands back (`planar:nav-*`), same-origin-targeted. `ProjectBreadcrumb` accepts an optional **controlled `projects`** list (falls back to `listProjects()` when omitted, so Site/Markup are unchanged); `Scheduler.jsx` feeds in the iframe's projects and posts commands to it instead of bouncing into the Site Planner. Opened directly (not in the shell) the scheduler keeps its native header — no regression.
> **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-schedule-picker.mjs`, **8/8**, logged-out with the scheduler cloud blocked → it fell back to its seed, which still flowed through the bridge): Site crumb "Map" lists Site projects; Schedule crumb "Dashboard" lists the SCHEDULER's projects (Goose Creek / Grand Port / Bee Sand) and **not** the seeded Site projects; selecting a project switches it inside the iframe; the Dashboard crumb opens the scheduler's reports view. 381 tests (full suite, post-merge with `main`) · lint 0 · build green. **NOTE for the owner:** the headless run is offline/logged-out so it showed the scheduler's 3 *seed* projects; the live signed-in/online app will list his real set (the bug never touched that cloud record).
> **Dedup:** direct follow-up to **B191–B193** (the shared breadcrumb) — fixes their Site-only assumption for Schedule; reuses the same `AppHeader`/`ProjectBreadcrumb`, adds only the module-aware list + the iframe bridge. Paired with **B204** (module-contextual home label).
