     real next free IDs B197-B202 at merge time per the permanent-ID rule. The implementing
     commit 8e19081 + branch name predate the renumber; the diff itself is unchanged. -->

### B197 — Print buildings/site data table `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; minted B197)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sweet-hypatia-itdlvu`, commit `8e19081`).** The printed sheet now carries a **BUILDINGS** data table anchored on the right, next to the title block: one row per building (row keyed by the building's stable `el.id`), columns **name / sf / clear height / slab**. Clear height + slab are read from the building's stored properties (B198) — never recomputed in the print routine — and the table is part of the single-SVG composition (B200), so it scales with the sheet. Built in pure `lib/printSheet.js` (`buildBuildingTableSvg`); headless-rendered (`ui-audit/verify-print-sheet.mjs` → `ui-audit/screens/print-sheet.png`). 15 printSheet tests.
> **Dedup:** distinct from B131 (overlay-in-print toggle); reuses B198's effective-property selector for the values.

### B198 — Auto-assign clear height & slab thickness as building properties by square footage `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; minted B198)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sweet-hypatia-itdlvu`, commit `8e19081`).** `clearHeight` + `slabThickness` are now first-class building properties (available to any module), auto-assigned from the building's footprint sf via an **editable per-plan rule** (`settings.buildingRules`) plus an **optional manual override** stored on the element (`clearHeightOverride` / `slabThicknessOverride`; override wins, auto recomputes on sf change when unset). Upper tier inclusive at each boundary — `<140k → 32'/6"`, `[140k,600k) → 36'/7"`, `>=600k → 40'/7"` — so a 250,000 sf building defaults to 36'/7" with no input (verified). New pure module `lib/buildingProps.js` (12 unit tests); additive el/settings fields (no migration). Surfaced + editable inline on the selected-building inspector and in the print Options flyout (B199).

### B199 — Print options interface: edit global defaults and per-building overrides `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-3"; minted B199)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sweet-hypatia-itdlvu`, commit `8e19081`).** The print-frame toolbar gained an **Options ▾** flyout (portal-mounted `AnchoredMenu`, so it escapes the toolbar's stacking context): (a) edit the **global size rules** from B198 (thresholds + their clear-height/slab values, with Reset to defaults) and (b) **override** clear height + slab per building (name editable too), with **auto vs set** surfaced and a one-click revert-to-auto. Editing globals changes defaults for un-overridden buildings; a per-building override pins that building. Live-smoke verified (`ui-audit/verify-print-live.mjs`, 0 runtime errors).

### B200 — Print zoom: building/site plan doesn't scale with title block, not a cohesive PDF `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-4"; minted B200)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sweet-hypatia-itdlvu`, commit `8e19081`).** Root cause: the plan was a nested SVG but the title block + metrics were HTML flow around it — two layout systems, so the print scale slider could scale the chrome while the plan held a fixed size. Fix: the **whole sheet is now ONE `<svg>`** (`lib/printSheet.js` `buildPrintSheetSvg`) — title block, the plan (nested `<svg>` keeping its own viewBox), the buildings table (B197) and the metrics share one viewBox and **one scaling transform**, so every layer scales together at any zoom and prints as one cohesive page (`@page margin:0` + intrinsic-inch SVG = exactly one page; inset border clears the printer edge). The on-canvas print frame now matches the printed plan box (WYSIWYG). Headless-rendered: one root SVG, nested plan, letter-landscape 11in viewBox. 15 tests.

### B201 — Print filename format `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-5"; minted B201)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sweet-hypatia-itdlvu`, commits `8e19081` + follow-up).** Exported PDF (document title → Save-as filename) and PNG use **`YYYY.MM.DD {Project} - {Plan Name}`** — e.g. `2026.06.19 Cypress Logistics - Plan 1` (or `… - Scheme A` once the plan is renamed). Date = today at export, project = the active site name, **trailing piece = the plan's own label** (`planLabel`). Filesystem-illegal characters are stripped from project + plan (the ` - ` separator and date dots preserved); a blank plan name just drops the tail. `lib/printSheet.js` `sheetFileName`/`sanitizeFilename` (tested).
> **Owner decision (2026-06-19):** the trailing identifier is the **plan name**, not an incrementing number — so the filename always tracks whatever the plan is named (today "Plan 1", later e.g. "Scheme A") and won't drift or surprise. (Superseded the initial incrementing-sheet-number default; the per-session counter was removed.)

### B202 — "Preparing print" hangs before producing file `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-6"; minted B202)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sweet-hypatia-itdlvu`, commit `8e19081`).** The stall was the image-inlining step: aerial/overlay `<image>` fetches ran one-by-one with **no timeout**, so any fetch that hung through the TLS-inspection proxy blocked prep for up to ~60s. Fix: each fetch is now **time-boxed** (`AbortController`, 8s) and they run **in parallel**, so worst-case prep is ~8s and a hung image is dropped (PNG) or keeps its remote href (print loads it natively). Added prep **timing instrumentation** (`console.debug` marks for inline + ready) so any future stall is diagnosable rather than a mystery.

### B196 — Scale bar + north arrow as DOM overlays so they're always fully visible (B173 follow-up) `[Site Planner / UI]` (bug)  *(owner re-reported on the live site 2026-06-19 — "scale still not fully shown, nor the north cardinal direction"; minted B196 — highest B# across both files was B195)*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/kind-meitner-uy2qeh`). **B173 pinned the app to the viewport (no page scroll) but left two residual defects** the owner still saw: (a) the on-screen scale bar + north arrow were drawn *inside the canvas SVG*, anchored to its coordinate space (`buildScreenFurnitureSvg` at `vh − 40`), so they rode the canvas and could still clip on a short/odd viewport; (b) the north arrow sat directly under the green **"Scaled · county GIS" calibration pill** (a higher-z DOM element at `left:12, bottom:40`) — so only the "N" peeked out, the arrow body hidden (the exact "north not shown" symptom). **Fix:** lifted both into **DOM overlays anchored to the VISIBLE canvas corners** — new `screenFurniturePlates()` in `lib/sheetFurniture.js` returns the scale bar + north arrow as standalone plates; `SitePlanner.jsx` renders them as two absolutely-positioned `<svg>`s at `bottom:40` (`pointerEvents:none`, `zIndex:7`, `data-export="skip"`), immune to canvas size. Relocated the two colliders: calibration pill `left:12 → 56` (beside the arrow), zoom controls `bottom:78 → 100` (above the scale bar). Also kept the planner root `minHeight:600 → 0` (belt-and-suspenders with B173's `index.css` `100dvh`+`overflow:hidden`, so a sub-600px window clips nothing). The **export** furniture path (`buildSheetFurnitureSvg`) is untouched — export parity preserved. **Self-verified headless at 1600×800 AND 1600×540:** page overflow 0; the "FEET" (scale) and "N" (north) labels both `getBoundingClientRect` fully inside the viewport at both heights; corner screenshots show the scale bar clear below the +/−/⤢ zoom stack and the north arrow beside (not under) the calibration pill. lint 0 errors · 257 tests · build green · `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact.
> **Reconciliation:** B173 (DONE, stays) fixed the page-scroll via viewport pinning and judged a portal overlay unnecessary; the owner's live re-report proved the furniture *placement* (in-SVG + pill overlap) was the remaining cause. B196 implements exactly the "fixed overlay anchored to the canvas corner" mechanism B173's note had set aside. B172/B174/B175 (tabs / header −20% / parcel checkbox) shipped independently on `main` and this branch's duplicates of them were dropped during the merge in favour of `main`'s versions.

### B195 — Trailer-parking label stays inside its polygon at every zoom level `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; minted B190, renumbered **B195** — concurrent `main` (#164/#168 + sibling branches) took B189–B193 while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID after B193)*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/cool-babbage-mpc9sd`). Zooming out grew the trailer label *relative to its shrinking strip* until it overflowed: the label was sized in fixed **screen** pixels (floored at `ls≥0.34`), so it stayed roughly constant while the strip got smaller on zoom-out — "fit logic exists but the limits are off." **Fix:** a trailer label is now sized as a **fraction of the strip's real-world extent** (EPSG:2278 feet → screen px via the current pixels-per-foot, `view.ppf`), so it scales WITH the area and stays contained by construction. The text runs along the strip's **long** side and the line-stack across its **short** side, each with its own fit bound (the smaller governs — this matches `stripLabelRot`, the B186/B188 helper that aligns the label to the long axis). The font is **floored** at a legible minimum (`minPx`, below which a too-small ≈2-spot strip takes *controlled overflow* rather than going illegible) and **capped** at the normal label size so it never balloons when zoomed in. The shared label engine `lib/labelLayout.js` gained a **`noLeader`** option: a trailer label that still can't fit overflows **in place** (centred on the strip), instead of being leadered out, and the engine now **prefers dropping a line to fit inside** before accepting that overflow. Per-label font metrics (`fs`/`lh`/`charW`) are threaded through the candidate → layout → render path; every non-trailer label keeps the existing global metrics (defaults unchanged). **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-trailer-label.mjs`): across five zoom levels the label stays **inside** the strip — shape **397×55px → 102×14px**, label/shape height ratio **0.50** (capped when the shape is large) **→ 0.96** (floored when small), `inside=true` at every step; `verify-new1to5.mjs` confirms a vertical strip still rotates correctly and other label types are untouched. **2 new `labelLayout` tests** (noLeader overflow-in-place; drop-a-line-to-fit). 354 tests (full suite, post-merge with `main`) · lint 0 · build green.
> **Dedup:** extends the **B121** shared label LOD + collision engine (`labelLayout.js`) and complements **B149** (zoom-out decluttering) — area-relative sizing is added *on top of* that one engine, not as a parallel renderer. Reuses **B186/B188**'s `stripLabelRot` (label orientation along a strip) rather than re-deriving it. Depended on **B194** for the final two-line label content. Distinct from B188, which fixed label *orientation/consistency*; B195 fixes label *containment under zoom*.

### B194 — Trailer-parking label: stall depth in the title, drop the row-dimension line `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; minted B189, renumbered **B194** — concurrent `main` (#164/#168 + sibling branches) took B189–B193 while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID after B193)*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/cool-babbage-mpc9sd`). The trailer-parking label is now **two lines** instead of three: line 1 = the per-stall trailer length + name (e.g. **"50′ Trailer Parking"**), line 2 = the trailer count (e.g. **"30 trailers"**). The old third line (overall row dimensions, e.g. "360′ × 50′" / "355′ × 50′") is **dropped entirely** — the depth now lives in the title and the overall row length is intentionally gone. The stall depth is read straight off the element's own config (`cfgOf(el).trailerL`, the depth a trailer sits in) — **not** the overall row length and **not** recomputed; the count keeps the existing `trailerStalls`/`estTrailers` math (polygon fields still read "(est)"). One code path in `SitePlanner.jsx` (the centred-label builder), so single strips, wide fields, and rotated vertical strips all pick it up. **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-trailer-label.mjs` + `verify-new1to5.mjs`): a 360′×50′ strip reads **"50′ Trailer Parking" / "30 trailers"** with no dimension line; a wide field reads "53′ Trailer Parking / 18 trailers"; a thin vertical strip runs the same two lines along its long axis. 354 tests (full suite, post-merge with `main`) · lint 0 · build green.
> **Dedup:** distinct from **B188** (which fixed label *orientation/consistency* — running the label in-line on a narrow strip via `stripLabelRot`); B194 changes the label *content*. Builds on B188's strip-label work, doesn't duplicate it. Paired with **B195** (containment under zoom), which depends on this item's final two-line dimensions.

### B193 — Persist current project before switching `[Header/Nav]` (task)  *(arrived as "NEW-3"; filed provisionally as B191, renumbered **B193** — concurrent `main` (#168) took B189–B190 for the Site Analysis tranche, so this is the real next free ID after B190/B191/B192)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/awesome-gauss-jlrq5v`).** A breadcrumb switch (to another project or to the Dashboard) flushes the current project first, so a switch can't silently drop unsaved work — it routes through the **existing** data-loss machinery: in the Site Planner, opening another project goes through `handleOpenSite` → `flushSite()` and the `key`-change unmount `persistOrDrop()`; in Doc Review, the `useReviewPersistence` unmount/visibility flush already guarantees the local write. On top of that, B193 adds the owner-requested **cloud-at-risk surfacing** (the B124/B125 silent-failure rule): each workspace passes a normalized `saveState` to the breadcrumb, and when it's `offline`/`error`, the switcher shows a **passive ⚠ line in the dropdown** AND a **transient "saved on this device — will sync when reconnected" toast** on the switch. The switch is **never blocked** on a successful cloud save, but is **never silent** about an at-risk one.
> **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-new1to3.mjs`): project switches complete cleanly; the at-risk surfacing is gated on `offline`/`error` (the sandbox is logged-out → `local`, no false warning). **Dedup:** no new persistence path — reuses SitePlanner's `flushSite`/`persistOrDrop` + Doc Review's persistence flush; B193 is the routing + surfacing layer over them. 344 tests · lint 0 · build green.

### B190 — Click a constraint card to toggle its layer on the map `[Site Planner / Site Analysis]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; filed provisionally as B185, renumbered **B190** — concurrent `main` (#164) took B184–B188 for unrelated Site Planner items, so this is the real next free ID after B189)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/bold-edison-h8tfkc`).** Each resolved constraint card now carries a **◍ Map** toggle; clicking it shows that category's GIS layer on the planner map, framed to the site; **◉ On map** while shown; click again to hide.
> **Built on the existing shared overlay system — NO parallel renderer.** Each source in `lib/siteAnalysis.js` gained a `mapLayer` id pointing at the layer that already exists in `lib/layers.js` (`flood→fema`, `wetlands→wetlands`, `pipelines→txrrc_pipe`, `oilgas→txrrc_wells`); the finding carries it through. `SiteAnalysis.jsx` renders the toggle **only** for a category that **resolved (present/absent) AND has a `mapLayer`** — so UNKNOWN / info / no-source categories (Road authority, Contamination, Jurisdiction, Zoning) show **no blank toggle**, their error stays surfaced (the bug report's rule). The toggle writes the same app-shared **`overlays`/`setOverlays`** state the Layers panel uses (one source of truth → `syncOverlayLayers` paints it), and `SitePlanner.toggleAnalysisLayer` turns the basemap on + **`frameToActiveParcels()`** (active-parcel extent + 60% margin, since FEMA/NWI are scale-gated). Independent per-card toggles → multiple layers at once. If a just-enabled layer's map service fails, the card shows an honest "service isn't responding" hint (the screen result still stands).
> **Verified live (headless):** clicking Wetlands **◍ Map** flipped to **◉ On map** and added the NWI overlay (`leaflet-image-layer` 0→1), framed to the parcel — screenshot `ui-audit/screens/analysis-verify.png`. lint 0 errors · 341 tests · build green · doc-review/site-planner lazy-chunk split intact. **V45.**
> **Dedup:** distinct from **LayerPanel** (the full layer checklist) — this is a per-finding shortcut into the same `overlays` state; same explicit-click pattern as the jurisdiction identify (never auto-loads all layers). Builds on **B189** (a card only offers the toggle once its query resolves).

### B189 — Site Analysis constraint queries failing (UNKNOWN / "Failed to execute query") `[Site Planner / Site Analysis]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; filed provisionally as B184, renumbered **B189** — concurrent `main` (#164) took B184–B188 for unrelated Site Planner items, so this is the real next free ID after B188)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/bold-edison-h8tfkc`).** Filed AND fixed AND verified live the same session. Bug: on Site Analysis, **Wetlands** + **Pipelines** returned "Failed to execute query." → UNKNOWN, while Floodplain worked. The bug report's instinct to **audit every category, not just the two visible**, paid off: a **third** source (**Oil & gas wells**, below the fold) was 400-ing too.
> **Root cause was a different field bug per source — confirmed live (HTTP 400 with old fields → HTTP 200 with real features) against a known Katy/Sheldon-Lake parcel before patching:**
> - **Wetlands** — NWI split layers 1/2 are **JOINED** layers (`Wetlands ⋈ NWI_Wetland_Codes`), so every field comes back **table-qualified** (`Wetlands_CONUS_West.WETLAND_TYPE`); asking for the bare names 400'd, and the qualifier **differs per sublayer** (East vs West). Fix: request `outFields:"*"` and **`normalizeAttrs()`** strips the `Table.` prefix so the summarizers read plain names.
> - **Pipelines** — queried `OPERATOR`/`COMMODITY`, which **don't exist** (real: `OPER_NM`, `CMDTY_DESC`, `DIAMETER`).
> - **Oil & gas wells** — queried `LEASE_NAME`, which **doesn't exist** on the Wells layer (real: `SYMNUM`/`API`/`WELLID`/…).
> All three fixed + flipped **`verified:true`**, so a now-working empty query resolves to **None found** (not conservative UNKNOWN) — matching the bug report's "expected." The silent-error guard is intact: a genuine HTTP/network error still classifies **unknown**, never a fabricated "none." Added **diagnostics** — `defaultFetchJson` carries `{httpStatus,url,arcgisCode}` on the Error and `logQueryFailure()` prints the real failure to the console, so an opaque "Failed to execute query." is debuggable instead of silent.
> **Verified live (headless, `ui-audit/verify-analysis.mjs`, real USFWS/FEMA/TxRRC endpoints):** Floodplain **PRESENT (Zone AE)**, Wetlands **PRESENT (Lake, Freshwater Forested/Shrub Wetland)**, Pipelines **NONE FOUND**, Oil & gas **NONE FOUND** — zero "Failed to execute query." 341 tests (siteAnalysis 25→36, incl. the qualified-field + corrected-field + normalizeAttrs cases), lint 0 errors, build green. **V45.**
> **Dedup:** this is the per-source debug of **B147**'s "🔲 Remaining (1)." Distinct from **B133/B135** (those fixed the wetlands *map-overlay image* `/export`; this fixed the Site Analysis `/query` connector — a different request path on the same host).

### B188 — Trailer-parking label inconsistent + should run in-line on the strip `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-5"; filed provisionally as B184, renumbered **B188** — concurrent `main` took B180–B183 for unrelated items, so this is the real next free ID.)*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/happy-goldberg-piym6g`). Two trailer-parking instances rendered their labels differently — the wide field kept its 3-line label horizontal, while the narrow wall strip overflowed (the collision engine leadered it OUT of the strip). Root cause: there was no orientation logic, so a label wider than the strip was pulled outside rather than turned to run along it. Fix = the **shared label-orientation helper** built for B186 (`stripLabelRot`, applied to `landscape`/`sidewalk`/`trailer` strips): when a label is wider than the strip is narrow, it runs ALONG the strip's long axis (vertical text on a vertical strip), so both instances now render consistently in-line and neither claims more space than the strip itself. **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-new1to5.mjs`): a thin vertical trailer strip shows its label running vertically down the strip; a wide trailer field keeps its label horizontal. 286 tests · lint 0 · build green.

### B187 — Truck court resize must anchor to the dock wall and push/pull trailer parking `[Site Planner]` (bug) — high severity  *(arrived as "NEW-4"; filed provisionally as B183, renumbered **B187**.)*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/happy-goldberg-piym6g`). Changing a truck court's **Depth** field (e.g. 135→140) resized it from the **centre** — losing depth on both sides, detaching the paving from both the dock wall and the trailer parking (a silently-wrong geometry state). **Two root causes fixed:** (1) `resizeSelEl` (the numeric Width/Depth editor) kept `cx/cy` fixed, so it grew/shrank symmetrically — it now applies the same **`hostClampOf`/`clampToHost`** host-edge pin the resize grips already use, so an attached strip/court stays flush against the dock wall and only the FAR edge moves; (2) `refitChildren` never moved the court's back-side trailer when the court itself was the resized element (it only handled trailers when the *building* resized) — it now registers a resized truck court in `courtBox`, so the `forCourt` trailer follows the moved far edge (pushed out on grow, pulled in on shrink, spacing preserved). Covers both the numeric field and the resize grips. **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-new4b.mjs`, the owner's exact path — Depth 135→170): the building/dock-wall label moved **0 px** (court stays anchored) while the trailer label moved **+54 px** out (pushed flush) — court → court paving → trailer stay connected, nothing detaches. 286 tests · lint 0 · build green.

### B186 — Buffer-strip width labels run along the strip's long axis `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; filed provisionally as B182, renumbered **B186**; shares its helper with B188/NEW-5)*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/happy-goldberg-piym6g`). A "5′ Landscape" / "5′ Sidewalk" label rendered horizontally even on a thin vertical strip, eating canvas across the strip. Added one shared, holistic helper — **`stripLabelRot(el, lines, charW, ppf)`** (covers `landscape`, `sidewalk` AND `trailer`, no per-type duplication) — that returns a rotation when the label is wider than the strip is narrow: the label then runs ALONG the strip's long axis (vertical text on a vertical strip, horizontal on a horizontal one). The shared `labelLayout` collision engine was extended to test the label's **rotated** on-screen footprint, so a vertical label is fitted against the strip's tall height and narrow width (and so it lands INSIDE the strip instead of being leadered out). New unit test in `test/labelLayout.test.js`. **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-new1to5.mjs`): vertical landscape/sidewalk/trailer strips show vertical labels; horizontal strips and wide fields stay horizontal. 286 tests · lint 0 · build green.

### B185 — Site acreage chip is draggable + persisted `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-3"; filed provisionally as B181, renumbered **B185**.)*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/happy-goldberg-piym6g`). The parcel acreage chip ("32.51 ac") was pinned at the parcel centroid and obstructed the layout. It's now **click-and-drag** (in Select), to anywhere — including outside the parcel boundary — storing a `labelOffset` (parcel-local feet) on the parcel so it survives geometry edits. New `startAcChip` + an `acChip` drag-move case mirror the B146 dimension-callout drag pattern; the offset persists via the existing Site Model save path (additive field on `parcels[]`, mirrors to Supabase when signed in). **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-new3.mjs`): the chip dragged 182 px and `parcels[0].labelOffset` was written to the saved store. 286 tests · lint 0 · build green.

### B184 — 24′ road-width dimension drifts left of centre `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; filed provisionally as B180, renumbered **B184** — concurrent `main` took B180–B183.)*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/happy-goldberg-piym6g`). The road-width dimension ("24′") rendered shifted toward the left edge of the road instead of centred on the span. Cause: the dimension line/label were placed at **18 %** along the element's long axis (a sensible default for a building's depth tick, but wrong for a road, where the width tick should sit on the centreline of the length). Fix: roads now place the width dimension at the **midpoint (50 %)** of the length (`posF = el.type === "road" ? 0.5 : 0.18`); the measured value and the perpendicular span anchor were already correct (the label sits at the midpoint of the measured width), so this is a position-only fix — no measurement-accuracy change. **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-new1to5.mjs`): the "24′" label sits centred along the road. 286 tests · lint 0 · build green.

### B183 — Editable layers decouple from backdrop during pan while loading `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; filed provisionally as B177, renumbered **B183** — concurrent `main` took B176–B181, so this is the real next free ID after B181/B182.)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/nice-heisenberg-r6lmf1`).** On a freshly-loaded site, grabbing and panning before load settled made the drawn layers (massing/parcels/markup) visibly offset from the aerial for a frame or two, then snap back. **Root cause (confirmed, not the pasted race-condition theory):** in Planyr the SVG *is* the source of truth and the basemap follows it, so the layers can't reproject against a stale transform — the decoupler was **B65's own ghost snapshot**. A `commit` clones the basemap into a frozen overlay held until the fresh tiles `load`; while loading, that `load` is delayed so the snapshot lingered, and a pan moved the live SVG while the **frozen** snapshot stayed put → the aerial lagged the drawn layers until the snapshot expired (hence "only early on, then snaps back"). **Fix:** drop any lingering snapshot the instant a new gesture starts (`dropGhost()` at the top of the transform path), so a pan is tracked by the live CSS transform (welded to the SVG) and the backfill covers any reveal; a fresh snapshot is taken only at the next commit. **Verified headless** (`ui-audit/diagnose-decouple.mjs`, retina + throttled, pan immediately after load): **0 %** of pan frames have a snapshot on top (idle baseline has one, correctly dropped on the first pan). lint 0 · 257 tests · build green.

### B182 — Basemap tiles missing at high zoom ("Map data not yet available") `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; filed provisionally as B176, renumbered **B182** — concurrent `main` took B176–B181 (jurisdictions/tax + cost takeoff), so this is the real next free ID.)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/nice-heisenberg-r6lmf1`).** Zooming in deep showed gray "Map data not yet available" placeholder tiles instead of imagery. **Root cause (measured, `ui-audit/diagnose-zoomdepth.mjs`):** Esri World Imagery is native to **z19**; `detectRetina` (added in B170 for sharpness) fetches **one zoom level higher** than the display zoom, so at deep zoom on a retina display the detail layer requested **z20** (168 requests), which Esri answers with the placeholder image. `maxNativeZoom:19` didn't account for the retina offset. **Fix:** drop the detail layer's `maxNativeZoom` by 1 on retina (`L.Browser.retina ? maxNative-1 : maxNative`), so the highest native fetch is z19 and beyond that it **upscales the deepest real imagery** instead of fetching nonexistent tiles — exactly the requested "clamp to deepest available zoom, scale the last good tiles up; never put placeholders over the plan." **Verified:** max tile zoom requested now **19** at both retina (DSF 2) and non-retina (DSF 1), **0** placeholder/empty responses (was 168). The coarse backfill (`maxNativeZoom:13`) was already clamping correctly. lint 0 · 257 tests · build green.
> **Follow-up → B218 (2026-06-20):** this fix was applied only to the **planner-canvas** backdrop (`SitePlanner.jsx` GEO_BASEMAP). The **map-finder** imagery layer (`MapFinder.jsx`) had the same `detectRetina` (from B170) but never got this retina clamp, so the placeholder still showed there on a retina display. B218 brought the identical clamp to the map finder (every dropdown source) + capped the labels overlay. Both call sites now clamp.

### B180 — Verify paving area excludes curb footprint `[Cost]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; minted **B180** — highest B# across both files was B179, so this is the real next free ID. Prerequisite for B181's paving-area trim.)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/determined-feynman-l7c61b`). Investigated → confirmed correct by construction, and locked it in.** There was no pre-existing *cost* paving figure to fold curb into — the only paving area the app derived was the **impervious/SF** metric, where including the curb band is *correct* (curb is impervious surface), so that stays untouched. The new cost takeoff (B181) derives paving from the road's **face-of-curb-to-face-of-curb travel width** (`roadTravelWidth` = `min(w,h) − 2·curb`), which **excludes** the curb by definition: a 30′ FC-FC road yields 30′ of paving, never 31′. So the defect the brief warned about (folding the 6″ curb each side into paving) cannot occur — the cost math reads travel width, not the full element rectangle.
> **Locked against regression:** `roadQuantities` (in `lib/costTakeoff.js`) takes the FC-FC width explicitly and a unit test asserts a 30′ FC-FC × 1000′ barrier-curb road = exactly **30,000 SF (3,333.33 SY)** of paving with curb **outside** that width — so a future change that folded curb back in would fail the suite. **Live-confirmed in-browser:** a seeded 26′-cross road (FC-FC travel 25′) reads **1,611 SY** in the Yield panel (25 × 580 ÷ 9); had curb been folded in (26′) it would read 1,675 SY — the 1,611 proves the exclusion. 300 tests green, lint 0 errors, build green.

### B181 — Curb as a separate linear quantity type with curb-type attribute `[Cost]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; minted **B181** — next free ID after B180.)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/determined-feynman-l7c61b`).** A road segment now derives **two independent, separately-priced quantities**:
> - **Paving** — an AREA item, **square yards (SY; 1 SY = 9 SF)** = length × FC-FC paving width ÷ 9. Width is stored/derived as **face-of-curb to face-of-curb** (the drivable surface), so a back-of-curb dimension can't silently inflate it.
> - **Curb** — a LINEAR item, **linear feet (LF)** = length × curbed-side count. **Both sides counted** (a 1,000′ road curbed both sides = 2,000 LF).
>
> **Curb carries a `curbType` attribute that selects its unit price:** `none` / **`barrier`** (vertical ~6″ lip, no gutter pan) / **`curb-gutter`** (curb + flat concrete gutter pan, typ. 18–24″). For **curb-and-gutter**, the gutter pan rides with the curb LF item, so **paving trims by the pan width on each curbed side** (`paving = FC-FC − panWidth × sides`); pan width is a property of the curb-and-gutter type (default 2.0′/24″, editable). Curb LF is split **barrier vs curb-and-gutter** in the rollup so each rides its own price.
> **Implementation:** new pure library `src/workspaces/site-planner/lib/costTakeoff.js` (`roadQuantities`, `costRollup`, curb-type readers) — no React, fully unit-tested (`test/costTakeoff.test.js`, 15 cases). Road-element fields are additive/optional (`curbType`, `curbedSides`, `panWidth`) and persist losslessly through the Site Model (els pass through untouched; no `SITE_MODEL_VERSION` bump). UI: a **"Curb & paving (cost)"** group in the road inspector (curb-type dropdown, curbed-sides Both/One, gutter-pan width, live per-segment SY/LF readout — inline editors only, no dialogs) and a collapsible **"Road cost (screening)"** section in the **Yield** panel (site-wide Paving SY + Curb LF by type, **user-supplied** unit-price inputs — blank by default, never a hardcoded $/LF — and a priced subtotal).
> **Hook left for later (not built):** `roadQuantities` tags each curb run `curbCategory: "linear"` so a future **radius/corner curb** category (often a higher unit price) can be broken out as its own priced line without reworking the rollup.
> **Verified:** 300 tests green (15 new), lint 0 errors, build green, lazy-chunk split intact. **Live headless (logged-out preview):** Yield → "Road cost (screening)" renders **Paving 1,611 SY · Curb · barrier 1,160 LF** with the FC-FC caveat and unit-price inputs, **zero page errors** (`ui-audit/verify-cost.mjs`).

### B176 — Jurisdictions overlay `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; filed provisionally as B167, renumbered **B176** — concurrent `main` took B167–B175, so this is the real next free ID after B175.)*
`[x]` Toggleable boundary overlays so you can see, on the map, which districts a site sits in — county, city limits, city ETJ, and MUD/water districts. "See which sites are in a MUD around me." No school (per spec). Screening-grade, with a hard "boundary = has jurisdiction, NOT physically served/connected" caveat on every layer.

A `dynamic` image export renders via a CORS-exempt `<img>` even if the probe can't reach the host.

If HARC ever proves unreliable in prod, alternates: City of Houston cohgis MUDs, or `services.twdb.texas.gov` water districts — a one-line URL swap in `JURISDICTIONS.jur_mud`.

### B65 — White flashing on zoom/pan and general redraw `[Site Planner / map]` (bug)
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/nice-heisenberg-r6lmf1`).** Zooming/panning a located site flashed (originally white) as the aerial blanked between redraws. **Root cause, measured not guessed** (headless probe `ui-audit/diagnose-flash.mjs`): the basemap view-lock effect called `map.setView(center, z, {animate:false})` on *every* planner `view` change; Leaflet's `setView`→`_resetView` fires `viewreset`, whose GridLayer handler `_resetAll` **wipes and reloads all tiles**, so each wheel step blanked the aerial for a frame (loaded tiles collapsed **22 → 2**), exposing the backdrop.
> **Fix shipped (two parts):**
> 1. **Mitigation (commit `cf26912`):** the basemap container backdrop was `PAL.paper` (`#f4f1ea`, near-white) → any gap read as a *bright* flash. Changed to a neutral mid-dark gray (`#3f3f3f`) **only while the aerial is on** (stays `PAL.paper` with the aerial off so the SVG-off background still matches). Bright flash → dim blink.
> 2. **Real fix — seamless transform-based zoom (commit `af10d1c`):** stop re-`setView`-ing on every frame. Hold Leaflet at a committed center/zoom and, for the small deltas of a live gesture, CSS-`transform` (translate+scale) the whole map container so the already-loaded tiles (and the shared FEMA/NWI overlay layers, which live on the same map) scale to track the gesture — no tile reload, no wipe, no flash. A debounced (180 ms) `setView` re-renders crisp once the gesture settles. First paint / resize / >1.5-zoom-level jumps commit immediately so the aerial is never scaled into a blurry mess. Transform math: `scale = getZoomScale(z, committed)`; translate so the desired center maps to the container centre (matches the SVG, which renders at true scale every frame), `transform-origin:0 0`. Container CSS transforms don't affect Leaflet's coordinate math (it uses cached `_size`/pixel-origin, and `clientWidth` is layout-box, unaffected by transform), so alignment is preserved.
> **Tested + rejected on the way:** flipping the map to `zoomAnimation/fadeAnimation:true` made it *worse* (gap frames 1→4, min loaded still 2) and reintroduces SVG-desync risk — not used.
> **Verified headless:** `diagnose-flash.mjs` now reports **0 gap frames** (min loaded 8, was 2); `ui-audit/verify-zoom-align.mjs` confirms the drawn building/parcel stay locked to the aerial through the transform and after the crisp commit (no jump). lint 0 errors · 257 tests · build green. **Live confirmation on planyr.io still nice-to-have** (a one-frame flash can't be captured headless), but the mechanism + alignment are proven. **Note:** Document Review's PDF viewer uses a different (canvas raster) renderer, not Leaflet — if zoom-flashing shows there too it's a separate fix, tracked if/when reported.
> **Follow-up 2026-06-19 (same branch) — kill the blank-backdrop reveal during the gesture.** After the flash fix shipped, the owner saw (screenshot) large flat cream patches while panning/zooming a project. Cause: the CSS-transformed basemap container (`geoWrapRef`) slid/scaled and exposed the canvas's `PAL.paper` (`wrapRef`) behind it. Fix (no new dependency): wrap the basemap in a **static clip box** (`inset:0`, `overflow:hidden`, dark `#3f3f3f` bg, never transformed) holding an **oversized inner map div** (`inset:-GEO_OVERSCAN`, `GEO_OVERSCAN = 320` px). The map now overhangs the viewport by 320 px on every side with `keepBuffer` tiles already loaded, so a normal pan/zoom transform reveals **real imagery**; anything beyond the overhang shows the **static dark backdrop**, never the cream page. The transform math is unchanged (it already uses `map.getSize()/2`, which adapts to the larger container, so basemap↔SVG alignment is preserved). Verified headless: `ui-audit/pan-reveal.mjs` (a hard mid-pan drag) now shows imagery edge-to-edge with no cream; `verify-zoom-align.mjs` still shows the geometry locked to the aerial through the transform + crisp commit. lint 0 errors · 257 tests · build green.
> **Follow-up 2 2026-06-19 (same branch) — kill the whole-screen "flash to black" on zoom-out.** Owner: zooming out from a building flashed the entire screen dark, even parts already loaded. Cause: the crisp re-render (`commit`) calls `map.setView`, whose Leaflet `viewreset`→`_resetAll` **removes ALL tiles and reloads them**, so for one frame the dark backdrop showed everywhere. Fix = **ghost-buffer the commit**: before the `setView`, clone the current basemap container (with its live CSS transform baked in) into a frozen overlay (`geoGhostRef`) pinned on top; the fresh tiles load underneath; on the tile layer's `load` event (or a 1.4 s fallback) the ghost is removed — so the old picture stays visible until the new one is ready and the wipe is never seen. Also dropped the old non-buffered ">1.5 levels → hard commit" branch; the crisp re-render now fires on settle (160 ms) OR once accumulated zoom drift passes ~0.75 levels, both **ghost-buffered** so a mid-gesture re-base no longer flashes. Verified headless (`ui-audit/zoomout-frames.mjs`, samples a continuous wheel zoom-out and measures the fraction of dark-backdrop pixels per frame): worst-case dark coverage **1.6 %** (UI edges only) — no full-screen black at any frame (was a brief whole-screen wipe). Alignment + crisp settle unchanged (`verify-zoom-align.mjs`). lint 0 errors · 257 tests · build green.
> **Follow-up 3 2026-06-19 (same branch) — fix the slow gray initial load (regression).** Owner: after the above, a freshly-opened site sat on the gray backdrop for ~10 s before the aerial appeared. Cause: the overscan (2.5× viewport) **×** detectRetina (2× density) ≈ **4× the tile bytes** on first paint, so on a real connection the detail tiles took ~10 s to cover (the sandbox is too fast to feel it — reproduced with Playwright CDP network throttling at ~1.2 Mbps: time-to-coverage **9.1 s**). Fix = a **coarse "instant" backfill layer**: a second `L.tileLayer` under the detail layer capped at `maxNativeZoom: 13` (a handful of large-area tiles, no detectRetina) that loads near-instantly and blankets the view with blurry imagery, then the heavy detail layer is added **only after the backfill paints** (`bf.once("load", addDetail)` + a 600 ms fallback) so its many retina tiles don't flood the connection and starve the coarse ones. Result (same 1.2 Mbps throttle): time-to-coverage **9.1 s → ~3 s** (blurry), detail then sharpens on top to the full 45 tiles; on a normal connection the coarse coverage is ~instant. No regression to the interactive fixes (zoom-out flash still 1.6 %, pan still full-imagery). `addDetail` guards against the aerial being toggled off mid-wait. lint 0 errors · 257 tests · build green. Harness: `ui-audit/initial-load.mjs` (optional `THROTTLE=1`).

### B173 — App pinned to the viewport; map scale bar always visible `[Site Planner / UI + Shell]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; filed provisionally as B168, renumbered **B173** — #152 + #153 collisions; next free after B171.)*

Root cause: nothing guaranteed the app couldn't grow taller than the window, so the page itself could scroll and push the bottom-of-canvas scale bar below the fold (and the header off the top). Fix is structural, not a scale-bar move: `index.css` now sets `overflow:hidden` on `html, body, #root` and pins them to `100dvh` (dynamic viewport height — handles mobile browser chrome) via `@supports`; `Shell.jsx` adds a defensive `overflow:hidden` on the shell column. The in-canvas measurement-grade scale bar (bottom-right, `lib/sheetFurniture.js`, shared with print/export) sits a fixed 40 px above the canvas bottom, so once the page can't scroll it is **always** visible — no need to fork a second portal-mounted overlay (kept export parity; the owner's "bottom-left fixed overlay" was the suggested mechanism, the real need was "always visible," now met). **Self-verified headless at 1440×900 AND 1280×600:** `document.scrollHeight === innerHeight` (no page overflow) at both sizes, and the scale bar + north arrow render at the canvas bottom with both header rows visible simultaneously.
> **Dedup note:** distinct from completed **B144** (scale bar clipping/measurement-grade in print/export) — this was on-screen viewport layout.

### B172 — Module tabs read as inactive, not disabled `[global UI / Shell]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; filed provisionally as B167, renumbered **B172** — concurrent `main` took B167/B168 (#152, map items) and B169–B171 (#153, basemap-blur trio), so this is the real next free ID after B171.)*

Icons are crisp fixed-13 px SVG with `shapeRendering:geometricPrecision` (no bitmap scaling). Inactive font-weight bumped 400→500 for legibility; `aria-current="page"` on the active tab. ### B170 — Fix retina/HiDPI tile requests so the aerial basemap renders sharp `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; filed provisionally as B168, renumbered **B170** — concurrent `main` (`claude/brave-galileo-wm8gti`) took B167 + B168 for unrelated map items, so this is the real next free ID; was gated on B169)*
`[x]` Gated on B169 (the diagnostic), which confirmed the dominant blur causes were **(a) HiDPI tiles never requested** and **(b) the planner's fractional zoom** — so the source-swap fix path (B171/NEW-3) was correctly NOT triggered, since the imagery source isn't the problem.
> ✅ **Done 2026-06-19** (branch `claude/awesome-darwin-7ui0qm`). Added **`detectRetina: true`** to **both** Esri World Imagery tile layers — the map finder (`MapFinder.jsx`, `L.tileLayer(bm.tiles, …)`) and the planner backdrop (`SitePlanner.jsx`, `GEO_BASEMAP`). On a HiDPI display (`devicePixelRatio > 1`) Leaflet now requests **one-zoom-higher native tiles and renders them at half size** (downsampled = crisp) instead of upscaling 1× tiles (= soft). This also sharpens the planner's *fractional* zoom (`zoomSnap:0`, driven by `ppfToZoom`) because it prefers downsampling a higher-zoom tile over upscaling a lower one. **Kept the Esri source** (per the NEW-2 constraint) and **did NOT touch the planner map's `zoomSnap:0`** — snapping that map to integer zoom would desync the aerial from the feet-space SVG (the deliberate ppf→zoom scale lock); `detectRetina` only changes which tiles are fetched + their display size, never the map's CRS zoom, so the lock is untouched. **Self-verified in a real headless browser** (`gis-verify/retina-basemap-verify.mjs`, simulating `deviceScaleFactor` 1 vs 2 over a Katy parcel): at standard density the map requests **z11** tiles; at retina density it requests **z12** (one level higher = 2× pixel density), with **0 failed/gray tiles** at either density (no coverage regression) — logged **VERIFICATION V43**. lint **0 errors** · **257 tests** · build green; `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact. (The sharpness gain is invisible at the sandbox's `devicePixelRatio = 1`, so the *visible* improvement is best confirmed on Michael's own retina/4K display — but the higher-density tile request is proven engaged.)

### B169 — Diagnose basemap blur: retina/DPR vs. fractional zoom vs. source resolution `[Site Planner]` (task)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; filed provisionally as B167, renumbered **B169** — concurrent `main` (`claude/brave-galileo-wm8gti`) took B167 + B168 for unrelated map items, so this is the real next free ID)*
`[x]` Diagnostic only — instrument + report the root cause of soft aerial imagery **before** any provider change (the fix paths are B170 + B171).
> ✅ **Done 2026-06-19** (branch `claude/awesome-darwin-7ui0qm`). Root cause established from the two tile-layer call sites (both the **Esri World Imagery** source, `server.arcgisonline.com/.../World_Imagery/MapServer/tile/{z}/{y}/{x}`) plus a live headless instrumentation:
> - **(a) Retina/HiDPI NOT requested — CONFIRMED, primary.** Neither `L.tileLayer` set `detectRetina` (nor any `@2x` / `tileSize:512`): the map finder (`MapFinder.jsx:291`) and the planner backdrop (`SitePlanner.jsx:1043`) both fetched **1× tiles**, which the browser then **upscales** on any `devicePixelRatio > 1` display (most modern laptops / 4K monitors) → soft. This is the most likely "it looks blurry on my screen" cause.
> - **(b) Fractional zoom — CONFIRMED for the planner backdrop.** The planner map runs **`zoomSnap: 0`** (`SitePlanner.jsx:1031`) and its zoom is driven **continuously** from `ppfToZoom(view.ppf, lat)`, so the raster is almost always displayed at a **fractional** zoom = interpolated = blurred (independent of DPR). The map finder uses Leaflet's default integer zoom, so it's not affected by (b) — only (a).
> - **(c) Genuinely low-res source — RULED OUT as primary.** Esri World Imagery is **native to z19** (`maxNativeZoom: 19`, ~0.3 m/px) with good Houston-metro coverage; both layers merely *display* past native (21/24), so the only "source" softness is upscaling past z19 at very tight zoom — not a stale/low-res source. Verified live (Katy parcel): tiles return **HTTP 200** with no gray/missing tiles at the working zooms.
> - **Live instrumentation:** `gis-verify/retina-basemap-verify.mjs` drove the headless map at `deviceScaleFactor` 1 vs 2 and recorded the **zoom level of every World_Imagery tile actually requested** + load status. Confirmed the pre-fix behavior (1× tiles, no DPR awareness) and gave the before/after baseline for B170.
> **Outcome → fix routing:** causes (a)+(b) are real and fixable **without** changing the imagery source → **B170** (add `detectRetina`, keep Esri, don't snap the planner's locked zoom). Cause (c) is not the issue, so **B171** (license-clean high-res source evaluation) stays **gated** — only revisit if B170 proves insufficient by eye on a real retina display. lint 0 errors · 257 tests · build green (no app-code change in this diagnostic item beyond the verify harness).

The same menu opens from a **map marker/boundary** right-click too (shared `statusMenu` path), so "right-click any project → status or delete" is uniform. The menu is a `position:fixed` full-screen-backdrop overlay at `zIndex 4200` — above all map layers, no clipping — positioned at the cursor and clamped to the viewport (clamp bumped to fit the taller menu).

### B166 — Geometry check reads wrong county acreage (homesite carve-out, not total) `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-3"; minted B166)*
`[x]` **Repro (owner-reported):** parcel `0440110000065` — Appraisal panel + drawn boundary agree (17.00 AC vs 17.06 ac) but the geometry check screamed **"county 0.50 ac vs 17.06 ac (3,312% off)."** The 0.50 ac was the **HOMESITE carve-out** (Legal: "PT TR 4D (HOMESITE)"), not the total tract.
> ✅ **Done 2026-06-19** (branch `claude/busy-carson-1zuiuq`). Confirmed root cause against the **live HCAD parcels layer** field list: the record carries **both** `Acreage` (total) **and** `acreage_1` (a sub-acreage) — both match the acres regex, and `countyAcres()` used `keys.find(...)` which returned whichever came first (the homesite ~0.50). Fix in `SitePlanner.jsx` `countyAcres()`: collect **all** acreage-named fields, drop any whose name marks it a sub-acreage (`home_site|homestead|hs_|hmst|exempt|imprv|improv`), and take the **MAX** of what remains — the total tract is always the largest, so a homesite/ag/exemption carve-out can never win. County-agnostic (fixes the statewide carve-out pattern, not just this parcel). Distinct root cause from B75 (that was a m²-vs-acres unit misread; the TxGIO unit handling is untouched). lint 0 errors · 257 tests · build green.

### B157 — Added-detention area label seats on the NEW ground, not the whole-pond centre `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived 2026-06-18 in chat — owner: when expanding an existing pond, show the added surface area + acreage at the centre of mass of the NEW area, because the whole-pond centroid often stays inside the existing basin. Refinement of B139/B140; filed provisionally as B151, renumbered **B157** — concurrent `main` took B150–B156 (easement tool, multipart-parcel + Delete-key bugs, markup hit-testing), so this is the real next free ID.)*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-18 (branch `claude/brave-noether-rwzkqk`). B140 stacked the "+added" increment as a third line on the pond's single centred label, so on a one-sided (or uniform) expansion the added figure floated over the EXISTING basin — the exact case the owner flagged, where the whole-pond centroid stays inside the old pond. Now the added detention area gets its OWN on-map label, seated on the **thickest part of the new ground**:
- **New `lib/pondGeom.js` (`addedAreaLabelPoint`, unit-tested):** the pole-of-inaccessibility of (expanded footprint − baseline footprint) via a coarse grid + local refine — the interior point of the new area farthest from any edge. Handles a one-sided strip (lands mid-strip), a uniform "push banks out" ring (lands in the band, never the centre), and a corner push; returns null on no-expansion / pure shrink / degenerate ring. Pure world-feet geometry (no React/DOM), so it unit-tests without a browser.
- **Label (`SitePlanner.jsx` element-label builder):** in expansion mode the centred label reads **"Existing Detention Pond"** + the existing area, re-anchored over the **existing basin** (baseline centroid); a second label titled **"Additional Detention"** + `"+X.XX ac · +Y sf"` is pushed at the added-region point (owner wording, 2026-06-18). A plain (non-expansion) pond label is unchanged ("Detention Pond" + area). The added area is the **footprint / top-down** area (the metric behind the owner's "20–25 % of the site" pond-coverage rule — NOT water-surface). Both ride B121's existing LOD/collision pool via a per-label id (`<id>` / `<id>#add`) — no parallel renderer. A net shrink / sub-`POND_ADD_MIN_SF` (50 sf) change falls back to the inline "+/−" increment so the delta still shows.
- **Verified (self, headless Chromium, logged-out preview build, 2026-06-18):** seeded a one-sided expansion + a concentric expansion; the existing-area label seats over the old basin and the "+added" label seats over the new ground (one-sided: to the right of the basin; concentric: out on the new ring, 183 px off the centre that sits inside the old pond), correct sf/ac, **zero console/page errors**. Re-verified after the owner wording change — labels read **"Existing Detention Pond"** and **"Additional Detention"** with the +ac/sf in place. lint **0 errors** (14 pre-existing warnings) · **257 tests** (6 in `test/pondGeom.test.js`) · build green · `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact. Browser pass → **VERIFICATION V42**.
> Refines **B140** (stays Done as the acres+sf label); builds on **B139**'s `det.baseline`. No `SITE_MODEL_VERSION` bump — reads the existing persisted baseline, adds no field.
> **Follow-up 2026-06-21 (branch `claude/brave-noether-rwzkqk`) — two-tone color + per-zone controls.** Owner: "make it so there's a slight color difference between the existing and additional and that I can change the settings for both." In expansion mode the **existing basin** keeps the cartographic water gradient (from **B231**) while the **added ring** paints in a lighter solid tint (`POND_ADD_FILL_DEFAULT #A7D3DD`, a lighter shade of the new teal pond), so the two read apart at a glance. Two color pickers — *Existing basin* / *Added area* — in the Expanding panel write `det.existFill` / `det.addFill` (live, saved with the element, both overridable); a normal (non-expanding) pond is unchanged. Reconciled cleanly over **B231**'s pond restyle (gradient default for existing, solid override for added); the pond label's dark-slate + white-halo carto style (B231) already reads over either fill, so no per-zone label ink needed. Both polygon + rect render branches updated. Build green; B157 headless self-check still 7/7 (wording + added-area seating intact).

### B154 — Delete key intermittently needs two presses to remove a selected element `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; filed provisionally as B151, renumbered **B154** — concurrent `main` took B150–B153 (easement tool) plus a second B151 (multipart parcel), so this is the real next free ID; the implementing commit references the bug as NEW-1)*
`[x]` Repro: click an element to select it, press Delete — sometimes it deletes on the first press, sometimes it takes two ("works when I was already on the canvas; fails when I came from a panel/button first"). **Root cause (confirmed, but NOT the report's first guess):** the keydown handler is **already** `window`-level — so it isn't a focus-scope problem. The real cause is a **stale closure via passive-effect re-binding:** `onKey` is created inside a `useEffect`, and although `sel`/`multi` are in its deps, the effect re-binds the listener **after** the commit/paint. A Delete pressed in the brief window right after a selecting click runs the *previously* bound `onKey`, which closed over the old `sel` (often `null`) → the guard `(sel || multi.length)` was false → no-op, no `preventDefault`; the next press (listener now re-bound) works. Under a heavy render (this is a ~6k-line component) the window widens enough to be hit intermittently.
> ✅ **Done 2026-06-18** (branch `claude/gallant-lovelace-82konu`). Added live `selRef`/`multiRef` mirrors (synced during render — a passive effect would lag the same window) and made the **Delete/Backspace branch read the refs**, and `deleteSel` read `selRef.current`/`multiRef.current`, so deletion always acts on the *current* selection no matter which listener instance fired — no second press. The handler stayed `window`-level (no scope change). Also **hardened the existing typing guard** — it already bailed when `document.activeElement` is INPUT/SELECT/TEXTAREA (so Delete never nuked canvas elements while editing a field); extended it to **`contentEditable`** too. The lone same-tick `setSel(x); deleteSel()` caller (the element context-menu Delete) is unaffected — the element is already selected when that menu opens, so the ref holds it. lint **0 errors** · **230 tests** · build green; `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact. **Self-verified in a real headless browser** (built app): (A) select an element → one Delete removes it (2→1); (B) touch a tool/panel button, then select an element, then a **single immediate** Delete still removes exactly one — the reported flow, now first-press reliable; zero console errors. Logged as **VERIFICATION V40**.

### B150 — Easement drawing tool (core): first-class Easement object, input modes, attributes, editing, render, persistence `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; minted B150 — next free ID after B149)*
`[x]` New first-class **Easement** object on the editable layer (immutable-backdrop model preserved): a `markups[]` entry `kind:"easement"` with a stable UUID and a display label derived from type + width (cosmetic, editable override). **Mode A — Centerline + width:** digitize a polyline centerline, enter total width → strip generated by offsetting the centerline ±width/2 with flat end caps; width is editable after creation and re-offsets the strip live. **Mode B — Boundary polygon:** draw a closed ring directly. Attributes panel (Element tab): type (Utility/PUE, Sanitary Sewer, Storm/Drainage, Water, Pipeline, Access/Ingress-Egress, Aerial/Overhead, Temporary Construction, Other), holder/beneficiary, width (auto-filled in mode A), recording reference, exclusive (y/n), status (existing/proposed), restrictsBuildings (default true), restrictsPaving (default false), notes. Editing: draggable centerline/polygon vertices (＋ add, Shift-click delete), move, delete, relabel; reuses the existing snap system + persistent toggle. Rendering: semi-transparent hatched fill color-coded by type, centerline shown for strip easements, proposed rendered dashed; per-easement area readout + total encumbered area in Yield. Persistence: Supabase, editable layer, private by default, RLS-protected.
> ✅ **Done (branch `claude/clever-franklin-7ds6kg`).** **Engine:** inspected the codebase first per the gate — an offset/buffer utility already existed (`bufferPolyline` in `lib/metesAndBounds.js`), so **no JSTS added**. Generalized it to be asymmetric-ready (`{leftW,rightW}`, default still symmetric ±w/2) so a future asymmetric-strip UI needs no geometry rework, and factored out a shared one-sided `offsetPolyline` primitive. **Domain logic** in new `lib/easements.js` (`EASEMENT_TYPES`, `easementLabel`, per-mode `deriveEasementRing`, `easementArea`). The **type dropdown uses the shared portal `AnchoredMenu`** so it can't render behind the rail/zoom rail. Easement is a markup → persists through the existing markups[] save path (Supabase, private, RLS) with no schema change. New rail "Easement" section (mode + default width/type via the portal menu). Self-verified in a headless browser (centerline + boundary draw, attributes panel auto-opens, portal type dropdown swaps type + relabels, vertex grips). **246 tests pass** (16 new in `test/easements.test.js`); lint 0 errors; build green.

### B147 — Markup/shape tools: Bluebeam-style editing (rotate + resize boxes, vertex-edit lines/polylines/polygons) `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived 2026-06-17 in chat: "fix the rectangle and markup tools … make them more like bluebeam, not being able to rotate a rectangle is wild"; minted B147 — next free after B146)*
`[x]` The neutral markup shapes (drawn with the Line / Rectangle / Ellipse / Polygon / Polyline tools) could only be **moved, restyled, or deleted** — selecting one just recoloured it, with **no handles**. You couldn't rotate or resize a rectangle/ellipse, or reshape a line/polyline/polygon. Meanwhile elements have resize/rotate grips and measures/parcels have vertex editing, so markups were the odd one out. **Owner's headline: "not being able to rotate a rectangle is wild."**
> ✅ **Done 2026-06-17** (branch `claude/gallant-lovelace-82konu`). Added Bluebeam-style geometry editing to the markups[] layer, **reusing the existing element/measure transform machinery** (no parallel system):
> - **Rect / ellipse:** on select (Select tool), 4 corner + 4 edge **resize grips** + a **rotate handle** above the top edge — mirrors the element handles. Resize is computed in the shape's own rotated frame (opposite side stays fixed); rotate spins about the centre, snapping to 15° when Snap is on, free (whole degrees) when off. The `rot` field already existed on rect/ellipse (rendered via `transform=rotate`), so this is purely the missing UI. New `mkResize`/`mkRotate` drag modes + `startMarkupResize`/`startMarkupRotate`.
> - **Line / polyline / polygon:** draggable **vertex dots**; **＋** on edge midpoints (polyline/polygon) to insert a point; **Shift-click** a dot to delete one (keeps the kind's minimum — 2 for line/polyline, 3 for polygon). New `mkVertex` drag mode + `startMarkupVertex`/`addMarkupVertex`, mirroring the measure-vertex handlers (B141). Shared helpers `mkPts`/`setMkPts` normalise line `{a,b}` ↔ point arrays.
> - **Properties panel:** rect/ellipse gain numeric **Width / Height** and **Rotation°** fields (precise entry; kept out of `mkStyle` via a separate `setSelMarkupGeom` so new shapes don't inherit a past size/angle), plus a one-line editing hint per shape.
> - **Scope:** only the 5 neutral annotation kinds get grips; **semantic markups stay move-only** (utilRoute / traced / infwater / encumbrance carry derived geometry — corridor/pad/centerline/calls — that hand-editing would desync). Locked markups show no grips.
> lint **0 errors** · **225 tests** · build green; `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact. **Self-verified in a real headless browser** (drove the built app): drew a rectangle → corner+edge grips + rotate handle appear → dragged a corner (300→410 px) and the rotate handle (rotate(0)→rotate(53)); drew a 3-point polyline → 3 vertex grips + 2 ＋ handles → dragged the middle vertex and the path updated; zero errors from the change. Logged as **VERIFICATION V38**.

### B144 — Scale bar clips off-frame and isn't measurement-grade in print/export `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; filed provisionally as B141, renumbered **B144** — concurrent `main` PR #114 had already taken B140–B142 and PR #117 took B143, so this is the real next free ID; the implementing commit still references the provisional B141/B142)*
`[x]` Repro: Print/PDF (and PNG export) of the map view → the scale bar's max label ("500") clipped at the right frame edge, the "0" floated above the bar instead of under the start tick, and the segments read as noise rather than a measured ruler. **Root cause (confirmed):** the export reused the *on-screen* scale bar's **screen-pixel** sizing (`scaleBarFt.px ≈ 120 px` + fixed `28`/`30` px offsets) and screenshotted it into a differently-sized export frame, so it overflowed; labels were also drawn *above* the bar with no plate.
> ✅ **Done 2026-06-17** (branch `claude/gallant-lovelace-82konu`). New pure module **`lib/sheetFurniture.js`** draws the furniture **sized in OUTPUT units and anchored to the export FRAME**, not the screen: everything is a fraction of `refS = min(frame w,h)`, so it lands at a fixed physical size on the page (on a letter sheet the short side ≈ 8.5 in → safe-area inset ≈ 0.38 in). The scale bar now **snaps to a round real-world distance** (`pickScaleBar`, from 50/100/200/250/500/1000 ft + smaller/larger steps for extreme zoom) that best fills a target width band **without exceeding a hard ceiling** (so it can't clip); **alternating black/white segments**; **tick marks at 0 / midpoint / max with the numbers centered directly under their ticks**; a **"FEET"** unit label; on a **translucent legibility plate** so it reads over light pavement or dark canopy. The graphic bar stays the source of truth (its length encodes the distance, so it survives image rescaling — no "1 in = X ft" text scale). Recomputes on zoom. `buildExportSvg` (`SitePlanner.jsx`) composites it into the print/PNG viewBox; the old screen-pixel furniture block + the now-unused `scaleBarFt` were removed. **Also applied on-screen** (owner asked to "fix the site planyr app too"): the live canvas uses the same primitives via `buildScreenFurnitureSvg` (viewport-anchored, fixed modest size) so the app matches the print. **Workspace confirmed Site Planner only** — Document Review has no print furniture (nothing shared to fix twice). lint **0 errors** · **222 tests** (18 new in `test/sheetFurniture.test.js`: round-distance snap, no-clip ceiling, safe-area anchoring, plate/label/FEET render, no compass rose, screen variant) · build green; `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact. **Self-verified in a real headless browser** (drove the built app: drew buildings → File ▾ → Print / pick frame → Print, captured the actual print page; also captured a PNG export and the on-screen corners) — scale bar fully inside the frame, round **0 / 125 / 250 FEET**, no clipping. Logged as **VERIFICATION V34**. Shared root cause + fix with **B145**.

### B145 — North arrow oversized and illegible in print/export `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; filed provisionally as B142, renumbered **B145** after the same concurrent-`main` collision as B144)*
`[x]` Repro: Print/PDF (and PNG export) of the map view → the north arrow was oversized for the frame, sat directly on the imagery (illegible over dark canopy), and used generic placeholder styling. **Same root cause as B144** — drawn as a screen-pixel overlay (a fixed-radius circle + triangle) screenshotted into a differently-sized export frame, rather than composited in output units.
> ✅ **Done 2026-06-17** (branch `claude/gallant-lovelace-82konu`, same change as B144). The north arrow is now a **clean filled arrow + "N" on the same translucent legibility plate** as the scale bar (`northArrowPlate` in `lib/sheetFurniture.js`), a **modest fixed ~0.5 in tall in the export** (`0.06·refS`), **anchored top-left with a fixed margin inside the safe area** so it never clips, and it **rotates to true map bearing** (points straight up on the planner's north-up canvas; `bearingDeg` param wired for any future view rotation). **No ornate compass rose** — a simple arrow, the convention for engineering exhibits (a unit test asserts no `<circle>`). ### B143 — Text box edits like Bluebeam: Enter = newline, click away / Esc to finish `[Site Planner]` (bug) — follow-up to B142
`[x]` Done 2026-06-17 (branch `claude/practical-noether-ln1f46`). Owner: starting a text box then clicking out "won't let me" exit. Two causes, both fixed to match Bluebeam's Text Box markup (researched against the Bluebeam Revu docs — "finish by selecting away or pressing Esc"; a text box is multi-line):
- **Click-out was trapped at ANY distance:** the canvas pointerdown `preventDefault`s the textarea blur, so `onBlur`→`commitEditCallout` never fired and you stayed in the editor even clicking 400 px away. Fix: a full-canvas transparent catcher rendered under the inline editor (`pointerEvents:"all"`, commits on pointerdown) — clicking anywhere outside the box now finishes it.
- **Enter committed (single-line behavior):** Enter now inserts a **newline**; you finish by clicking away or Esc (Esc keeps the text). Placeholder updated to "Type; click away or Esc to finish".
- Empty box is still removed when you click away without typing (matches Bluebeam).
- Verified live (headless): Enter → "Line1\nLine2" (still editing); click away +80 px → finishes + commits two lines; Esc → finishes keeping the text; empty box removed on click-away; zero console errors. lint 0 errors · build green · tests pass. Browser pass → **VERIFICATION V33**.
> Cross-ref: completes the text-box UX started in **B142** (selectable across the whole box) — together they make text boxes select / edit / finish like Bluebeam.

### B132 — Detention pond expansion: lock an existing pond as a baseline, then read the storage gained `[Site Planner]` (feature)
`[x]` Done 2026-06-17 (branch `claude/practical-noether-ln1f46`). Owner workflow: trace an existing on-site detention pond, lock it as the baseline, then enlarge it (drag banks out and/or deepen) to read the **added detention** in acre-feet. Built entirely on the existing pond machinery — no parallel store, no new schema bump.
- **Panel** (`SitePlanner.jsx`, pond branch of the selected-element inspector): the **Detention storage** section gains a **"Lock as existing pond"** button. Locking snapshots the current footprint ring (world feet: `selEl.points` or `elCorners`) **plus its own depth/freeboard/slope** into `el.det.baseline`, so the comparison is frozen and apples-to-apples. Once locked, an **"Expansion vs. existing"** box shows **Existing** / **Proposed** storage and a live **"Storage gained +X.XX ac-ft"** (green) — or **"Storage lost"** (red) when shrunk below baseline — plus the cubic-feet delta. **Clear** removes the baseline (keeps depth/freeboard/slope).
- **Increase = `detentionStorage(proposed) − detentionStorage(baseline)`** — the *same* prismoidal/taper function for both sides, so the delta can't drift from a method mismatch. Reflects both footprint growth and any depth/slope change.
- **Canvas ghost** (`renderElPx`): the locked baseline ring draws as a faint **dashed outline** under the pond so the expansion is visible. Handled for both the irregular-polygon branch (drawn in world feet directly) and the rotated-rectangle branch (a counter-rotated `<g>` undoes the element's `rotate(el.rot)` so the world-feet ghost lands true). `pointerEvents:none` so it never interferes with selection/drag.
- **Persistence:** `baseline` rides inside the already-persisted `el.det` (additive, lossless) — survives save/reload, no `SITE_MODEL_VERSION` bump. Honest framing kept: "screening only — confirm with your civil engineer."
- **Scope (owner-chosen):** "just the increase." Deliberately **excluded** for now (offered, declined): a required-vs-provided "is it enough?" check against added impervious, and a solver ("grow this much to hit a target"). Easy follow-ons if wanted.
- **Verified:** lint 0 errors (14 pre-existing warnings, none in new code) · **191 tests pass** · build green · lazy-chunk split intact (`SitePlannerApp` own chunk). Browser click-through logged as **V25** in `VERIFICATION.md`.

### B123 — Restructure building label + make square footage persist on zoom-out `[Site Planner]` (feature)
`[x]` Done 2026-06-16 (branch `claude/determined-brown-bf86l7`). The building label is now a 4-line **level-of-detail stack** built on B121's shared engine — name → square footage → "(incl. N bump-outs)" → dimensions — so the **square footage survives zoom-out far longer** instead of vanishing early.
- **New ordering + wording** (`lib/labelLayout.js` `buildingLabelLines`, unit-tested): square footage is now its **own line** (was crammed onto the sf line with the bump-out note), the bump-out note is a **separate parenthetical line shown only when the building has bump-outs**, and its wording changed from "+N bump-outs" to **"(incl. N bump-outs)"**. `SitePlanner.jsx`'s building-label branch builds the stack via that helper; every other element label is unchanged.
- **Drop order = dimensions → parenthetical → square footage → name.** The stack is ordered highest-priority-first and B121's `fitLines`/`layoutLabels` drop from the end, so dimensions go first on zoom-out and square footage outlives them (it drops only at extreme zoom-out). Reuses B121's pool — not a parallel renderer, as the item required.
- Poly-drawn buildings keep their existing name/sf/ac label; only rect buildings get the 4-line stack.
- **Tested:** `test/labelLayout.test.js` adds a `buildingLabelLines` case (exact order, singular/plural + conditional parenthetical, and a `fitLines` assertion proving sf outlives dimensions). lint 0 errors · **174 tests pass** · build green · lazy split intact. Browser-verify logged as **V21** in `VERIFICATION.md`. Completes the B122 → B121 → B123 building-label arc.

### B122 — Auto-number buildings with contiguous renumber-on-delete `[Site Planner]` (feature)
`[x]` Done 2026-06-16 (branch `claude/determined-brown-bf86l7`). Each standalone building now shows a sequential **"Building N"** label, numbered by placement order and contiguous (1…N) at all times. Deliberately **render-derived, not stored**:
- **New selectors** in `lib/siteModel.js`: `isBuilding(el)` (a `type:"building"` element that is NOT an attached dog-ear/bump-out — those carry `dogEar` + `noLabel`) and `buildingNumbers(els)` → `Map(id → N)` assigned in `els` (placement) order. The number is recomputed from list position every render, so **deleting a building renumbers the rest 1…N in one pass** with no stored field to migrate; a lone building is "Building 1".
- **Label** (`SitePlanner.jsx` element-label render): a standalone building's first label line is now `Building ${n}` (was the bare type name "Building"); every other element label is unchanged. Dog-ears/bump-outs are excluded (already `noLabel:true`), so the parent's bump-out tally ("… (+2 bump-outs)") is untouched.
- **Identity unchanged + safe:** the "stable internal ID, separate from the number" requirement was already met — every element has a persisted, collision-seeded `el.id` (`uid()` + `ensureIdAbove` on load), and every cross-reference (`attachedTo` for parking/trailers/dog-ears) already binds to `el.id`, never a display number. So a renumber can't silently re-point anything. No schema change, no migration, no `SITE_MODEL_VERSION` bump.
- **Tested:** `test/siteModel.test.js` adds a `buildingNumbers` case (contiguous 1…N by placement order, dog-ears excluded, renumber-on-delete, single→"Building 1", null-safe). lint 0 errors · **139 tests pass** · build green · lazy-chunk split intact. Browser-verify logged as **V13** in `VERIFICATION.md`.
> Unblocks **B123** (building-label restructure): it reuses `buildingNumbers`/`isBuilding` for label Line 1, then folds the rest of the 4-line stack into **B121**'s shared label collision/LOD engine.

### B119 — Parking orientation flipped: first bay must sit against the building `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1")*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-16 (branch `claude/youthful-heisenberg-9w64n4`). **Root cause:** `addParkingRowSide` created building-attached parking with `cfg:{ flipDepth:true }`. The strip's inner (local `y=0`) edge sits against the wall, and `flipDepth` mirrors `carStalls`'s layout so the **drive aisle** landed on that inner edge — i.e. the aisle hugged the building and stalls were pushed outward (the inverse of the spec). **Fix (one line):** drop `flipDepth` for building-attached parking. `carStalls` now lays the first stall row at the building edge with the drive aisle outboard, and `growParking` already grows on the away-from-host edge — so the field grows **outward, away from the building**, exactly as specced. The per-field "Drive aisle on the far side" toggle (B59) still flips it by choice; existing saved parking keeps its stored `cfg` (only newly-added side parking changes). Lint 0-errors, 152 tests pass, build green. Browser-confirm logged as **V17** in `VERIFICATION.md`.
